# Changelog

All notable changes to Xenon are documented here.
Format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.0.0/).
## [v4.9.0] - unreleased
### ✨ New
- **A widget can now move your sound to another set of speakers.** Until now a widget could turn the volume up and down but not choose where that volume came out, so a mixer could not offer the one control people reach for when they unplug their headphones. It can now ask for that ability, and it has to ask **separately**: it is its own permission rather than something bundled into "change the volume", because approving one is not approving the other — and folding them together would have handed the new power to every widget you had already approved, without asking you again. A widget can only pick from the output devices Windows is already showing you, and only outputs: there is deliberately no way for one to change which microphone is listening.

- **Xenon can now hear how loud each app actually is.** Until now it knew what volume every app was set to, which is not the same thing: a music player sitting at 80% while nothing is playing reads exactly like one at 80% mid-song. Windows does not hand that number out for free, so Xenon Helper now measures it directly — the same reading the Windows volume mixer draws — and it becomes available to widgets that ask for it, roughly twelve times a second. A widget can finally show a meter that follows the music instead of an animation that only looks like one. There is nothing to switch on: a widget asks for it the way it asks for anything else, and the permission you approve is what starts the measurement — it runs only while some widget you granted it to is installed, and stops when none is. That matters because it is a continuous measurement sent to every dashboard you have open, so it should cost nothing until something actually wants it. It needs Xenon Helper, the optional companion the installer sets up; without it nothing happens, because there is no other way to read this on Windows, and the widget is told why. Widgets are expected to work without it — the developer documentation says so plainly, since most people will never turn it on.

- **Xenon can tell you when something happens, and you decide whether it does.** Two switches in Settings → Aggiornamenti. **Annunci e novità** is a short note when a version ships or something new lands in the Store, at most once a day. **Segnala nuove edizioni limitate e contenuti per sostenitori** is the card that already existed for numbered copies and supporter packs. Some announcements are only meant for some people, say those running a particular widget: that filtering happens **on your PC**, because your dashboard downloads the same list everyone gets and decides for itself which parts apply. Nothing about what you have installed is sent anywhere to work that out, so there is no way to single you out and no record of who was shown what. The privacy page says the same in more detail.

- **An announcement can ask you a question, and answering takes one tap.** Some of what gets built next depends on what people actually want, and until now the only way to find out was a Discord thread that reaches the people already in Discord. An announcement can now carry a short poll: the question, two to five answers, one tap and it closes. What gets sent is which option you chose and nothing else, not even a time, so there is no way for me to ask what any particular PC answered. Results are a rough sense of the room rather than a vote count, and the page explaining what Xenon sends says exactly that. Answering is never required, closing the card sends nothing, and turning announcements off in Settings stops polls with them.

- **Creations in the Store can now show how many times they were installed, without anyone being counted.** Community creators had no way to tell whether anything they published was being used. There is now a switch in Settings → Aggiornamenti: with it on, installing something from the Store adds 1 to that creation's counter. What gets sent is the id of the thing you installed, and nothing else: no install identifier, no account, and the server adds 1 and throws the request away. Your own dashboard keeps track of which creations it has already counted, so each one is reported at most once from your PC, which is exactly why nothing identifying has to be sent to avoid counting you twice. It also means the number is "installs reported" rather than "how many people own this", and it says so wherever it appears. **If you already have Xenon, it starts off**: only installs made from v4.9.0 onwards start with it on, and either way it is one switch away.

### ✨ Improvements
- **The top bar can now be switched off from Settings, not only from the Layout editor (#115).** Hiding it was always possible, but only by opening the Layout editor and finding the button there, which is not where anyone looks for it. Settings → Barra superiore now offers a third choice next to Completa and Minimal: **Nessuna**. It is the same switch as the one in the Layout editor rather than a second setting that could disagree with it, so whichever one you use, both show the same thing. Choosing Nessuna remembers whether you were on Completa or Minimal, so bringing the bar back gives you the look you had instead of resetting you. With no bar on screen, the floating Layout button is the way back in, and the hint under the setting says so. Translated in all eleven languages. (Thanks to the community contribution behind this.)

- **The "don't show me these again" you pressed once is no longer permanent.** The card announcing new limited editions and supporter packs has always had a way to switch it off, and no way to switch it back on: the choice lived only in the browser it was made in, nothing else read it, and getting the cards back meant clearing your browser storage. It is now the ordinary setting described above, so it can be turned back on, and it follows you to your other screens instead of applying only to the one you were looking at. If you had switched the cards off, they stay off.
- **A promotional card can no longer appear on top of a question you were asked to answer.** When a widget asks to be allowed to do something, to copy to your clipboard, or to send you to a site it did not declare, Xenon shows you a prompt and waits. Until now the "new in the Store" card did not count those prompts as something already on screen, so it could open over one of them. That is the worst possible moment for it: you end up approving or dismissing with a promo card in the way. It now waits, like it already did for the update window and the Store. The rule about when to interrupt you now lives in one place instead of being copied into each card that can appear, so a card added later cannot forget a case by accident.

- **The two things the Claude Code widget can put on screen while you are looking elsewhere are now switchable.** Both were deliberate and neither could be turned off: the permission card appears wherever you are, because a session waiting on your answer is not something to hide behind a page you are not on, and the marker next to the clock is there so you know a session finished without going to look. That is the right default and it is not the right answer for everyone, so Settings has a new **Claude Code** section with a switch for each. Turning the permission cards off is a real change and not just a hidden card: Claude Code is told immediately that this screen is not answering, so the question goes back to your terminal at once rather than leaving the session waiting for a card that will never be drawn. Turning the top bar marker off gives the space back to the clock. Both stay on unless you change them, and neither affects the widget itself, which keeps showing quota and sessions as before.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **241 pieces of text that were written in your language were showing in English.** If you use Xenon in Korean, Japanese, Chinese, Spanish, French, German, Portuguese, Russian or Dutch, parts of the app were English even though the translation existed and had been there for versions: the Deck's task actions, the whole top bar section in Settings, the Store gallery and its supporter and limited-edition wording, the code redemption messages, and every message the update flow shows when something goes wrong. The cause was an ordering mistake in the translation file. Each language starts from English and then replaces what it has translated, but in nine of them the "start from English" step was written in the middle of the list instead of at the top, so everything above it was overwritten by English again the moment the app loaded. Nothing looked broken, which is why it lasted: the text appeared, just in the wrong language, and the correct translation sat in the file the whole time. Italian and English were never affected. There is now a test that fails if the ordering is ever wrong again.

- **Deck keys with an icon can be dragged again (#114).** In edit mode you reorder keys by dragging them, and on any key showing a picture, an app icon or a background image, that barely worked: the browser saw an image being dragged and started its own drag instead, which swallowed the movement and left the key where it was. Keys with only a letter or a symbol were fine, which is why it looked random. Pictures are now excluded from that behaviour, so every key drags the same way. The other half of the same problem: the drag only began after the pointer had moved a short distance, and a quick flick could carry your finger off the key before then, so nothing happened at all. The key is now followed from the moment you press it. (Thanks to the community contribution behind this.)
- **A Deck key can be dragged onto another page (#114).** Until now a key could only be moved within the page it was on, so getting one onto the next page meant deleting it and building it again there. In edit mode you can now drop a key onto the `‹` or `›` arrow at the bottom and it moves to that page, into the first free spot, with the deck following it there so you can see where it landed. If the next page has no room the arrow does not light up and the key stays where it is, rather than the deck quietly resizing every page to make space. (Thanks to the community contribution behind this.)

- **A question from Claude no longer asks your permission to be asked.** When Claude wanted to put a choice in front of you, the touchscreen showed a card with the question, its options, and two buttons: **Chiedimelo** and **Nega**. Neither did what it looked like. The options were not tappable and never had been, because the tile cannot hand Claude an answer; **Chiedimelo** only meant "go ahead and put this in the terminal", and **Nega** threw the question away unread, so Claude carried on guessing at the exact moment it had decided to ask you. Questions now go straight to the terminal, where they can actually be answered, and the tile shows them only as a heads-up: the question, the options, where to answer, and one button to clear the card. Permission requests for things that really do run on your PC are unchanged.

- **The Store button in Settings is readable, and now looks like a way in.** Three things were wrong with it. Its label and icon were painted white and pinned there whatever accent colour you had chosen, so on a pale accent such as amber it was white on light and nearly invisible; it now takes the same text colour every other accent-filled button uses, which Xenon works out from the accent itself and checks for contrast. It was also the same height as the little close button beside it, which made the one thing in that header worth opening read as just another icon in a row, so it is bigger now. And its icon was a filled shop awning that turned into a shapeless blob at that size — people read it as a cup — replaced by an outlined shopping bag, which still looks like a bag when it is small. The two buttons in the Xenon message card had the same colour fault and are fixed with it.

- **A permission request that did not fit on screen no longer gets cut off at the bottom, which is where the buttons are.** When Claude Code asked something with a long command or a question with several options, the card was drawn at its full height and whatever did not fit was simply clipped. On the Xeneon Edge, which is a short screen, that regularly took **Consenti** and **Nega** with it, so the one thing you were being asked to do was the one thing you could not reach, and there was no way to scroll to it. The card now keeps the question and the buttons fixed and scrolls only the part in the middle, so both ends stay visible however long the request is or however small the tile. The full-screen version also no longer shortens the command it is asking you to approve: you are agreeing to it, so you get to read all of it.

- **An animated background no longer draws more pixels than any screen needs.** A background is the one thing on the dashboard that is repainted whole, every frame, and handed to the graphics card each time. On a 4K screen at 150% scaling that was over seven million pixels per frame, roughly four times what the same background costs on the Xeneon Edge, and on the kiosk that work lands on the small integrated graphics chip that drives the Edge over USB-C. Backgrounds now draw at a sensible ceiling and are stretched to fit. Nothing changes on the Edge or on an ordinary 1080p screen, which were already under the ceiling; on very large screens the background is very slightly softer, which is invisible on the soft, dimmed backdrops these are, and costs a fraction to draw. Applies to every animated background, including ones you write yourself.

- **The switches that pause animations now pause everything they promise.** Xenon has four states that are supposed to quiet the screen: a dialog open on top, a minute without touches, game mode, and the hybrid GPU option. Several things slipped through all of them. The glow that breathes on Deck keys was not covered by any of the four, even though the hybrid GPU option literally says key decorations stay still. The blinking clock colon, the shimmer on the Xenon button and the Claude activity dot restart whenever the top bar redraws, which put them back in motion moments after the idle pause had stopped them. And the graphs were invisible to all of it, because their glide is not an animation but a movement restarted by every new reading, once a second, forever, even with nobody there. Each of those kept the graphics card producing frames around the clock, which is why enabling the pause options could show no improvement at all. All of them now stop in all four states; the graphs step to the new value instead of gliding while one is active, and glide again when it ends.

- **The graphs in the System widget were quietly costing more than everything else on screen.** Each line glides to its new shape over half a second, and it had a glow drawn as a real blur. A blur has to be recomputed every single frame the line moves, and since a new reading arrives every second, each graph was moving most of the time. One or two graphs and you would never notice. Eight of them, which is what the System widget shows, and your graphics card was doing more work for the graphs than for the entire rest of the dashboard, with nothing else running. The glow is now drawn as a wider, fainter copy of the line underneath it, which looks the same and costs a fraction. The lines still glide.

- **A widget you cannot see no longer works as if you were watching it.** Xenon knew whether a widget's page was on screen, but not whether the widget itself was: one sitting behind another tab in a tab group counted as visible. So it kept receiving every sensor update, several times a second, and redrew itself each time for nobody. With two or three widgets in a tab group that is most of them, all the time, and it showed up as CPU use with nothing on screen to explain it. A widget now counts as visible only when its own tile is, and gets the current state of everything it reads the moment it comes back, so you still see fresh values and not a stale tile catching up.

- **Widgets can now be told when they are off screen, so they can stop working.** A widget runs in a sealed frame, and inside that frame the only thing it could ask was whether the whole browser window was hidden. That answer is "no" even when the widget is behind another tab or on a page you have scrolled away from, which is why a well-written widget still burned CPU out of sight: it had no way to find out. Xenon now tells it, and the SDK documentation asks widget authors to stop their timers when it does. Xenon cannot stop them from the outside, so a widget that ignores this keeps costing what it costs. If one is using more than its share you can still pause it from the Store, Installed tab, where it is also labelled.

- **Adding a custom widget to a tab now asks you which one, and lets you add more than one.** Pressing "+ Tab" and choosing a custom widget did not show the chooser: it filled the tab with whichever widget you had placed there last, and after that the option disappeared from the list, so a tab group could hold exactly one custom widget. The reason is that every widget from the Store shares the same slot, and the tab was reusing that one slot instead of creating a new one. Each custom widget added to a tab now gets its own slot, so it starts empty with the chooser and you can add as many as you like to the same tab group. Existing tabs keep the widget they are showing.

- **A tab group holding a widget from the Store no longer disappears after a restart.** If you put a Store widget in a tab group next to a built-in one, the group could be gone the next time Xenon started, and the only fix was to build it again. It was not random: every startup briefly stripped the group, because the part of Xenon that checks your saved layout runs before the part that knows how to read duplicated tiles, and rather than leaving them alone it dropped them. A group with only one tab left in it gets removed, and a Store widget always sits in a group as a duplicated tile, so those groups were exactly the ones that fell apart. Normally the layout was rebuilt a moment later and you saw nothing; when the dashboard happened to save itself in that moment instead, the stripped version was written down as the newest one and overwrote the good copy on disk. Saved layouts are now left intact until they can be read properly. The same fault could have emptied the Store's Installed list, and is fixed there too. Xenon also cleans up the leftovers each of these losses left behind, which mattered because enough of them would have started pushing real widgets out of their tiles.

- **The good morning screen now waits until you are actually there.** Xenon greets you once per part of the day, and it was greeting the clock rather than you: the moment it turned 05:00 the morning greeting played, spoke, and marked itself done, whether or not anyone was in the room. On a screen that is always on, that is what happened every single day, and by the time you sat down there was nothing left to show. It now holds the greeting until it can tell someone is at the PC and shows it then, so arriving at half past eleven still gets you a good morning. Two smaller faults went with it: the day rolled over on London time rather than yours, so a late night greeting could swallow the one just after midnight, and a greeting that failed to draw still counted as shown.

- **Widgets can now keep their API key out of the package when the service wants it in the address, not in a header.** A widget from the Store never ships its own keys: you type yours into Xenon, it is kept on this PC, and Xenon fills it into the widget's requests so the widget itself never sees it. That worked when the key went into a header or after the `?` in an address, but not when a service expects it as part of the address itself, which is how TheSportsDB and a few others are built. In that one case the key was not filled in and the request went out with the placeholder text instead, so the widget got nothing back and the author's only way around it was to write a key into the package where everyone can read it. Both forms now work the same way. Reported by DanielGarciaMorato while building a sports results widget.

- **A tab whose content you moved into its own panel no longer stays behind as an empty one.** Volume and Microfono live inside the System tile until you pull them out as separate panels, and Attività, Timer and Note do the same inside Agenda. When you pull one out, its content physically moves to the new panel and its tab is supposed to disappear along with it. The instruction to hide it was there and had been since the beginning, but a styling rule took priority over it, so the tab stayed visible and led to a blank pane. Adding Volume as its own panel and then pressing Volume inside System showed nothing at all, which is exactly what it looked like: two things fighting over the same content. They were not, and the tab now goes away as intended. The same rule was hiding the Cronologia tab even when sensor history is switched off, where pressing it quietly sent you back to Sistema. Tabs are also no longer reachable by keyboard once their content has moved, and the tab bar disappears properly when only one tab is left in it. Reported by Driahva.

- **Adding Volume or Microfono to another page now gives you the real thing, not a copy of it.** Putting one of these on a page of its own behaved differently depending on how you got there: added as a tab next to System it left the System tile, added to a different page it stayed in System as well and the new page got a duplicate. That duplicate was not the full widget, because a copy cannot carry the per-app mixer: you got the master slider and none of the per-app sliders, which for Volume is most of the point. The first time you place one of these anywhere it now moves out of its host tile, the same way it always did when added as a tab, and only further copies are duplicates. This also applies to Attività, Timer, Note and Calendario leaving the Agenda tile. The reason it duplicated was that moving it out appeared to leave an empty gap behind, which was the tab-hiding problem described above rather than anything to do with moving. Existing layouts are untouched: a duplicate you already placed stays a duplicate. Reported by Driahva.

## [v4.8.0] - 19-07-2026
### ✨ New
- **The Claude Code widget now shows how much of your plan is actually left.** This was the one thing it could not tell you. It read your local session transcripts, which contain how many tokens you spent but nothing at all about your subscription, so the gauge measured you against a weekly ceiling you had to type in yourself and then trust. Claude Code does report the real figures, through its status line, and Xenon now reads them: the 5-hour window and the 7-day window, each as the percentage you have left and a live countdown to when it resets. To get them, press **Collega Claude Code** on the widget. It adds a status line and a set of hooks to your Claude Code settings, keeps a copy of the file first, and if you already had a status line of your own it keeps running yours as well instead of replacing it. **Scollega** puts everything back. The windows exist for Claude Pro and Max subscriptions; on an API key there are none to show, so the widget keeps the weekly budget it always had, and says which of the two you are looking at.

- **You can approve what Claude Code is about to do by tapping the Xeneon Edge.** When Claude Code asks permission to run a command or write a file, that request now appears on your dashboard with the tool and the exact command, and **Consenti** or **Nega** decides it. Claude Code waits for your answer. It means you can leave a session running, walk away from the keyboard, and keep working from the touchscreen instead of going back to the terminal each time. A request that goes unanswered for a moment takes over the whole screen, and anything with a wide blast radius (`rm -rf`, `git reset --hard` and similar) does that immediately rather than waiting. Nothing is ever approved for you: if you do not answer, or Xenon is closed, or the connection fails, the question simply goes back to the terminal exactly as before. Xenon can only answer a request it shows you.

- **The widget now knows what your sessions are really doing, instead of guessing.** The old list was built from file timestamps, so a session thinking hard or running a long build wrote nothing and vanished after four minutes, one you had already closed lingered just as long, and a session you just started could take a minute to appear. Now Claude Code reports its own state: each row says whether it is working, waiting for you, or idle, shows the tool it is running right now, and appears and disappears the moment it actually starts and ends. Sessions on your other projects show up too, each with its model and how full its context window is.

- **You can now start Claude Code from the touchscreen, not just watch it.** Until now the widget was read-only: it told you what your sessions were doing and let you approve what they asked, but you could not give Claude anything to do without going back to the keyboard. The widget now has a **Chiedi** button. Pick one of your projects, type what you want done, choose the model if you care to, and Claude Code starts working in that folder. Progress and the answer come back to the tile, and there is a Stop button while it runs. Tapping an existing session instead sends it a follow-up rather than starting something new, and shows you the last turns of that conversation first, so you are not writing into it blind. You can attach files and images too, or paste a screenshot straight into the box: they are saved on this PC and their location goes to Claude, which reads them with its own tool, so the read comes back to you as a card to approve like anything else. Enter sends and Shift+Enter breaks the line, the way every other chat box works, and sending a follow-up leaves you in the conversation rather than closing it. Two sessions open in the same folder are told apart by a short tag next to the name, shown only when there would otherwise be two rows reading the same thing, and repeated in the header so you can see which one you opened. While a session is working, the conversation keeps itself up to date and a "Claude is working" line sits at the end of it, showing the tool being run right now, so you can watch a session get on with it instead of tapping to check. Sessions that go quiet are no longer thrown away after a few minutes: they are kept for an hour under a Finished heading you can unfold, because the follow-up you think of ten minutes later needs the session to still be there. And a session that finishes while you are writing to a different one now says so, with a tap to switch to it.

- **Deck keys for Claude Code.** Two new key actions, under a Claude Code category that appears once you have connected it. **Chiedi a Claude** carries a project, a request and optionally a model, all set when you configure the key: one press and Claude starts working on it. It suits the things you ask for over and over, like running the tests and reporting what broke, or summarising what changed today. **Ferma Claude** stops the run that is going. Both go through exactly the same path as asking from the touchscreen, which means normal permissions: every command and every file write still comes back to the Edge as a card you approve. A key starts work; it does not grant any. There is deliberately no key that approves a pending request, because a fixed button answering a prompt without showing it removes the one step that whole flow exists for. The key stores which project to use, never a folder location, and the list it offers is the one Xenon builds from Claude Code's own history.

- **The top bar tells you when Claude Code is working, and when it has finished.** A session that finishes answering while you are looking at something else announced itself nowhere, so you found out by going back and checking. There is now a small Claude marker in the clock island: it breathes quietly while a session is working, turns solid when one has finished and you have not looked yet, and goes red when Claude Code is blocked waiting for your permission. Tapping it opens that session. It sits with the clock, so it is there in both the full and the minimal bar, and like every other island element you can reorder it or hide it in Settings → Aspetto. When nothing is happening it takes no space at all. The list of projects you can pick is built by Xenon from Claude Code's own history, so the dashboard can only start work in folders you already use, and it is Xenon that resolves the folder, never the page. Nothing about permissions changed: runs started this way go through Claude Code's normal permission mode, so every command and every file write still comes back to the Edge as a card you have to approve. There is no way to skip that, deliberately, and no setting to turn it off.

- **The Claude Code widget has been redesigned around what you actually need to read.** The animated reactor was the nicest thing on the dashboard to look at and the hardest to read anything from: a glowing ring, a number, and no way to tell what any of it meant at a glance. It is gone. In its place are three plain bands, in the order you need them: your quota as horizontal bars with the percentage left and the reset countdown, then your live sessions, then today, this week and cache hit rate. Taller tiles still fill in the 30-day history and the project and model splits underneath. It also costs less to draw, since there is no longer a canvas animating behind it.
- **The Slideshow widget can now show a folder on your PC, with no limit on how many images.** Until now every image had to be added one by one and copied into Xenon's own folder, which is why there was a ceiling on how many you could have. Settings → Slideshow now lets you point at a single folder instead: paste its path and Xenon shows what is inside it, without copying anything. Add a GIF to that folder and it turns up in the slideshow on its own, delete one and it goes away, and the folder tells you how many images it found so a typo in the path doesn't leave you staring at an empty tile. Subfolders are not read, and the ceiling is 20,000 images in one folder. The request came from someone running a 844-GIF folder who had been keeping a second app open just for this. There is also a new **Random order** switch, which works with either source. Images larger than 20 MB are skipped, the same ceiling that already applied to images you add by hand.

- **The slideshow gets out of the way while you are gaming.** An animated GIF keeps decoding every frame for as long as it is on screen, and the browser offers no way to pause one. Xenon now replaces it with a still frame while game mode or performance mode is running, and puts it back the moment they end. While it is stopped the slideshow does not change picture either, so nothing is fetched or decoded at all. There is a switch in Settings → Slideshow, on by default, if you would rather have it moving even mid-game. The same still-frame swap happens whenever the tile genuinely cannot be seen, such as a page you are not looking at, and that needs no setting.

- **A widget can now put a web page on the Xeneon Edge, instead of on your other monitor.** Until now the only way a community widget could open a link was to hand it to Windows, which opens your default browser wherever Windows feels like, usually the big monitor, which is the opposite of what a widget on the Edge is for. Widgets can now ask the **Browser tile** on your dashboard to show the page instead, optionally filling the whole screen, with touch working properly: pan, pinch, and tap the site's own controls. It's a new permission, listed as "Open web pages in the Browser tile on your dashboard", and you approve it at install time like any other. Nothing about the widget sandbox changed: the widget names an address and never sees the page, exactly as before; it just gets to choose a destination Xenon owns. As with links, you're shown the domain the first time a widget sends you to a site it didn't declare at install, and sites on your own network or on this PC are refused outright, so the tile can't be used to reach things the widget was never allowed to reach. Widgets that catalogue maps, wikis, dashboards or docs are the obvious use; the request came from a creator building a game-map browser for the Edge.

- **Safe mode: one switch that answers "is an installed item causing this?".** Settings → Widget e condivisione has a new switch that temporarily pauses every third-party widget, your custom theme and skin, and any imported background (code, image or video), returning the dashboard to its factory look. Nothing is uninstalled and nothing you configured is touched: turn it off and everything comes back exactly as it was, permissions included. It exists because until now the only way to find a misbehaving install was removing things one by one. It came out of a real report: a user chased abnormal GPU usage for days and had to uninstall everything to find the cause.
- **Xenon now notices when a widget is slowing things down, and tells you which one.** Every community widget now reports how much main-thread time it actually costs, and the Store's Installed tab shows a small activity label next to each one (light, moderate, heavy). If a widget stays heavy for a sustained stretch, Xenon tells you once, with its name, and points you to the pause button. The measurement runs inside the widget's own sandbox and grants it nothing new.
- **You can pause a single widget without uninstalling it.** Each widget row in the Store's Installed tab has a new Pause button: the widget stops completely (its Deck keys too, on purpose), its permissions and settings stay saved, and Resume brings it back as it was. Pausing survives restarts and follows you across screens.
- **The publish portal now checks your submission while you type, and shows you exactly what a reviewer will see.** Pasting your share code at xenon-app.com/submit runs the same automatic analysis the review process uses: security patterns, performance habits, oversized files, undeclared hosts and more, each finding with the file and line it came from. A clean result says so in one line. If the check flags something, you are asked to explain why your creation needs it before you can send, and the page says plainly that flagged submissions may not be accepted. Encrypted packages are marked for full manual review. The same analysis, and your explanation, land in front of the reviewer with the submission. You can also save the whole thing as a file or copy it, so you can work through the findings in your editor, keep a record of what a version was flagged for, or paste it somewhere to ask for help. It is the same document the reviewer reads, built in one place so the two can never say different things.
- **Heavy items are labeled in the Store before you install them.** When the review analysis finds that a widget or scene runs costly animations or very frequent updates, its Store card carries a small "may use more resources" note, repeated in the import window. It is informational only: you can still install everything, and the new pause button means trying something heavy is never a commitment.
- **Xenon now tells you where a widget's link is about to send you.** A widget with the "open links" permission could hand any address to your browser, and the addresses that matter are the ones it never declared: a news widget opens whatever its feed says, so the destination isn't really chosen by the widget's author either. Nothing on screen had to say where a tap led. Now the first time a widget opens a given site, Xenon shows you the domain and you decide, and it remembers that site for that widget until you restart, so you're asked once per outlet, not once per headline. Sites the widget declared up front (the ones you already approved when you installed it) never prompt. A widget that's built well shows you the domain itself; this makes sure the ones that don't still can't send you somewhere unannounced. Addresses on this PC are refused outright, with no prompt at all: there is no reason for a widget to send you to Xenon's own local server, and a confirmation box reading "127.0.0.1" is not something anyone can reasonably say yes or no to.

### ✨ Improvements
- **The anonymous version count is now on by default for new installs, and unchanged for everyone else.** v4.7.0 added a switch that adds your version number and operating system to the update check Xenon already runs, and nothing else: no install id, no extra request, and the server keeps a daily total per version then throws the request away. It shipped off by default, and almost nobody turns on a switch like that, so the count could not answer the question it exists for. From this version it starts on for installs made from v4.8.0 onwards, and you can turn it off in Settings → General → Updates whenever you like. **If you already had Xenon, nothing changed for you**: the new default is only read where there are no settings yet, so an install that predates v4.8.0 keeps exactly what it had. If you left the switch alone back when it was documented as off, it is still off. The privacy page now spells this out, including which installs the new default reaches.

- **The dashboard stops animating behind full-screen windows, and the GPU with it.** Opening Settings, the Store, an import window or a drop card lays a large blurred panel over the dashboard, and every blink of the clock or shimmer of a button underneath forced the whole blur to be recomputed, every second, for nothing you could see. Those animations now pause while such a window is open and resume, mid-beat, when it closes. Measured on a real report: Settings open went from ~10% GPU to near the dashboard's idle level. Settings and the update window already did this for the background effects; now every big window does it, for everything that moves.
- **Dashboard pages you are not looking at stop being drawn.** With more than one page, the pages parked off-screen kept rendering the whole time: their widgets, their animations, and any community widget's own internal work. They now stop rendering entirely between swipes and pick up again the instant a swipe starts, so nothing visible changes, the page sliding in is always live, and a widget parked on page 2 no longer costs GPU while you look at page 1.
- **A large slideshow library no longer slows the whole app down while you're in Settings.** The Slideshow settings page showed each of your images as a live picture, which for animated GIFs meant every one of them playing at once, all the time the page was open. With a couple of hundred GIFs that was enough to make the rest of Xenon stutter. The page now shows a still frame of each image, and only loads the ones you have actually scrolled to. Nothing changed about the widget itself: it always showed one image at a time and was never the slow part.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **CORSAIR RGB control now sets itself up, instead of depending on a file iCUE no longer installs.** Xenon talks to your CORSAIR devices through a component that iCUE used to place on your PC. Recent iCUE versions no longer install it anywhere, so on many machines the lighting page had nothing to talk to, and on the rest it worked only because some unrelated software happened to include a copy, sometimes one several years old. The installer now fetches the current version directly from CORSAIR's official release, checks it against a known fingerprint before using it, and Xenon prefers it over any older copy it finds. It is downloaded rather than shipped with Xenon because CORSAIR's licence allows using the component, not passing it on. If the download does not succeed, everything else works as normal and the lighting page explains what is missing. And if you updated into this version rather than installing it fresh, the installer never runs again, so the lighting page now offers the download as a button: one tap, and your CORSAIR lighting works without reinstalling anything.

- **RGB devices that appear after Xenon starts are no longer invisible until you restart the server.** Xenon asked iCUE for your devices exactly once, the moment the connection came up. On a PC that has just booted, Xenon is ready before iCUE has finished registering everything, so whatever iCUE had not listed yet was missing for the rest of the session: typically the direct devices like RAM lit up while a cooler or the fans behind an iCUE LINK hub stayed dark. Xenon now rechecks periodically while the lights are in use, so a device that turns up late starts working on its own, and the same goes for anything you plug in later. Reinstalling or updating iCUE while Xenon is running is also handled now: the old connection is noticed as dead and rebuilt, instead of leaving the lighting page reporting a healthy connection that painted nothing.

- **A lighting effect that fails now says so, instead of reporting success.** When a write to your devices was refused, Xenon treated it as done: the lighting page stayed green with no error, the colour was recorded as already applied, and nothing was retried, so the lights simply never responded again until a restart. Failures are now detected, shown on the lighting page, and the write is retried rather than remembered as successful.

- **The Settings → Display section has been removed, as a precaution.** Since v4.1.0 it let you adjust a monitor's brightness, contrast and colours directly, and included a button that restored the monitor's factory values. Some Xeneon Edge panels that were used with that section later stopped being configurable in iCUE. We cannot yet prove the two are connected, and we have asked CORSAIR to check what that reset command does on the Edge, but rather than wait for the answer with any risk open, the whole section is gone. Nothing about your Xenon settings is affected: the section only ever talked to the monitor itself. If it comes back in a future version, it will be after CORSAIR confirms it is safe.

- **Uninstalling Xenon now removes the second screen's virtual display too.** If you ever set up the second screen, Xenon installed a virtual display driver and created a virtual monitor with it. Nothing ever took that monitor away again: not closing Xenon, not uninstalling it. It stayed registered in Windows, and setting the second screen up more than once left a trail of dead entries behind it, one per attempt. The uninstaller now removes the virtual monitor and the settings file that goes with it. The driver itself is still asked about separately, since other apps can use it. If you have a pile of leftover entries right now, uninstalling will clear them.

- **Setting up the second screen no longer reports success when it failed.** The setup ran its steps through a Windows elevation prompt and then read the wrong program's result, so it always came back as "done": if the driver had not installed, or you had dismissed the prompt, you were told the second screen was ready and then found no screen. It now reads the real result, tells you when you dismissed the prompt rather than calling it an error, and confirms an install by checking the driver is actually there instead of trusting a number.

- **The kiosk app can no longer open full-screen on the wrong display.** It finds the Xeneon Edge by its 2560x720 panel size, and the second screen's virtual display can be set to exactly that size, so it was possible for the dashboard to go full-screen on a screen you cannot see. It now skips virtual displays when there is a real Edge to use.

- **Menus and colour pickers no longer open off the edge of the screen.** In the per-widget style editor the Font and Fit menus were plain Windows dropdowns, which open below wherever you tapped: near the bottom of the Xeneon Edge the list fell past the display and the options could not be read or reached. They now use Xenon's own dropdown, which is anchored to the button, kept inside the screen and opens upwards when there is no room below. The same was true of the model pickers in Settings → Xenon AI, and they are fixed too.

- **The colour picker no longer opens off the edge of the screen.** A few colour swatches still opened Windows' own colour dialog instead of Xenon's: the per-widget style editor, the Deck's gradient and media accent, and the lighting widget's custom colour. That dialog is a separate window Xenon cannot place, so on the Xeneon Edge it came up half outside the display, with no way to drag it back on a touchscreen. All of them now use the in-app picker, which is always kept inside the screen. The picker itself also got stricter about it: it can no longer be pushed past any edge, and on a short window it scrolls instead of running off the bottom.

- **A Store section holding a single item no longer leaves most of the row empty.** The Supporters shelf, and any other section with just one entry in it, drew one narrow card at the left edge and nothing at all beside it, with the description cut off after two lines while there was room to spare. That section now lays its single card out wide, picture on the left and the full description on the right, the same way the catalog on the website does. It applies everywhere a section can end up with one item: the Supporters and Limited edition shelves, a category with a single creation in it, and a search that matches exactly one thing.

- **A slideshow on a page you are not looking at really does stop now.** Swiping to another page was supposed to freeze the slideshow on the page you left: it shows a still frame and drops the picture, so nothing is being decoded. It never happened. A parked page stops being drawn but keeps occupying its space in the layout, and the check asked "does this tile still take up space?" rather than "is this tile being drawn?", so a slideshow one page over always answered yes and carried on decoding a picture nobody could see. On top of that, nothing told the widget a swipe had happened, so even a correct answer would have waited until the next picture change, up to the whole "time per image" setting, two minutes at the longest. Both are fixed: the tile freezes the moment the page parks, and comes back the moment you swipe to it. Reported by a user watching a slideshow keep burning CPU from a page they had left.

- **On a two-GPU PC, the animated background stays frozen once it has been frozen.** On a machine with both an integrated and a discrete graphics chip, Xenon deliberately renders on the one driving the Xeneon Edge and stops animated backgrounds, because that chip has no budget to spare for a full-screen repaint. That is what the "Reduce animations on hybrid GPU" switch does. The freeze was applied when the dashboard started, but if anything later cleared it, every following settings change re-sent the same unchanged preference, saw nothing had moved, and never put the freeze back: the background quietly animated for the rest of the session, burning a chip that cannot afford it, with no way to recover short of reloading. The freeze is now re-applied on every settings change rather than only when you flip the switch.

- **Widgets that come inside a package now ask for their permissions, instead of installing and staying dead.** Importing a package installed its widgets but never asked you to approve them: the only way to approve one was to place its tile on a page, so a widget designed to live *without* a tile, the ones that just put a small readout next to the clock, had no way to be approved at all. It installed, it looked correct in the list, and it simply never appeared. And when a prompt did show up it was the package's ambient scene, opening *underneath* the import window, which is why it seemed to appear at random. Now the import finishes, its window closes, and each widget still needing approval is asked for in turn, above everything else. If you already imported a package and something from it never showed up, open Settings → Custom widgets and approve it there; it works from that point on.

- **A numbered limited edition now shows its own artwork, and gets its own updates.** A numbered drop hands out one copy per person (VANGUARD 50 // 01/50) while the Store publishes a single page for the whole edition. Installed was matching your copy's id against the Store's, they never matched, and the result was the plainest possible bug on the least plain thing you can own: your limited edition sat in the list with a generic grey box instead of its screenshot, and an update published for the drop was never offered to you. Both now resolve through the edition the copy belongs to.

- **You can approve a widget's permissions straight from Installed.** Approving used to require placing the widget's tile on a page, which is impossible for widgets that are meant to have no tile, like the ones that only add a small readout next to the clock. They installed, sat in the list looking fine, and could never be switched on. Any package still waiting for approval now shows a Permissions button right in the list.

- **The Lighting settings now tell you why the lights are dead, even with the master switch off.** Each effect drives the LEDs on its own: Album → LED, CPU temperature, and the timer, notification and reminder flashes all work without the master switch, and using the page that way is perfectly normal. The message explaining a failed iCUE connection, though, only appeared when the master switch was on. Anyone relying on the effects alone saw ticked boxes, motionless lights and no explanation, while the server had the reason ready the whole time. That message now appears whenever something wants the LEDs and the iCUE session isn't up.

- **The publish form no longer accepts a version number that would reach nobody.** Xenon only offers an update when the version goes up, so submitting a version *lower* than the one already published was a silent dead end: the entry was reviewed, published, and never delivered to anyone who had the previous version installed. It was easy to do by accident when renumbering a project (1.0.0 → 0.1.2 reads like a fresh start). The form now refuses it and tells you which number to use, and it also catches the equivalent-but-differently-written case (1.0 against a published 1.0.0).

## [v4.7.1] - 18-07-2026
### 🐞 Fixes
- **Claiming a limited edition now works, and the Store tells you where to put your code.** A limited drop hands you two things: a personal file and a personal code that unlocks it, both sent by Discord DM and shown on the claim page. Neither of them lives in the catalog, because every copy is its own numbered artifact, so once you had them the Store had nothing left to offer you and no field to type the code into. The only way in was Settings → Widget e condivisione → Importa…, which you had to already know about. The card of a limited drop now carries an **"Ho il codice"** button that opens that import window directly. It stays there after you claim, on purpose: your code works on three devices, so it is also the way back in on a second PC or after a reinstall.
- **The "Apri Discord" button on a limited drop no longer drops you on the welcome channel.** It is meant to open the drop's own post, but when an entry does not name one it fell back to the plain server invite, so it looked like a broken claim button sitting next to the real one. It now appears only when it has somewhere to go, or when the drop can be claimed on Discord and nowhere else.
- **A sold-out limited edition no longer sits in the Store next to one you can still get.** The Limited edition shelf listed every drop ever released, so a sold-out card kept the shelf occupied while a claimable one led the page. Sold-out drops now show only when nothing in the tier can still be claimed, which is also how the website has always behaved. They stay reachable through search and the Limited filter, where seeing the history is the point.

## [v4.7.0] - 18-07-2026
### ✨ New
- **Xenon now has a privacy page, and it holds nothing back.** [xenon-app.com/privacy.html](https://xenon-app.com/privacy.html) lists every network call the app makes, when it makes it, and what it sends — including the ones that were always there and never written down: the update check that runs at launch, the IP-to-city lookup the weather widget uses if you leave auto-location on, and the anonymous install id attached to catalog ratings. Nothing about the app changed here; what changed is that you no longer have to read the source to know. If a future release adds a call, that page gets updated in the same release.
- **You can now be counted, if you want to be.** A new switch in Settings → Generale → Aggiornamenti, **off unless you turn it on**, adds your version number and operating system to the update check Xenon already performs. That's the whole payload — no install id, no identifiers, and no extra network request, because it rides a call that was already happening. The server keeps a daily count per version and throws the request away, so there's no record of you, only a number. It exists because "how many people are still on an old release" is currently unanswerable, and the alternative was guessing from download counts.
- **Experimental Linux support for the tiles that used to sit empty.** Xenon's core is a local web server, so it already ran on Linux, but five features were wired to Windows-only tooling and came up blank there: the GPU, disk, CPU-temperature and network tiles showed `--` because their collectors shell out to PowerShell and WMI, the "Open applications" widget reported "No open windows found" because it drives a Win32 EnumWindows helper, and the volume mixer said "audio unavailable" because it drives SoundVolumeView.exe. A new `server/linux-collectors.js` supplies native equivalents (nvidia-smi, `df`, `/sys/class/hwmon`, `/proc/net/dev` and ping, wmctrl/xdotool/xprop, and PipeWire through pw-dump and wpctl), each returning the same shape its Windows counterpart returned, so the caching, bandwidth-delta and mixer logic above them is untouched. Every SoundVolumeView call now goes through one helper that translates the same arguments to wpctl on Linux, and the capability probe reports what is actually usable instead of assuming PowerShell is present. Windows behaviour is unchanged: the Linux paths are reached only when the server is running on Linux.
- **Known limits, deliberately not papered over.** GPU readings come from `nvidia-smi`, so AMD and Intel cards still report nothing. The application switcher uses X11 tools and returns an empty list under a Wayland session, which is now the default on recent Ubuntu and Fedora. Each collector degrades to the previous empty state when its tool is missing, rather than erroring, and the mixer reports "audio unavailable" when no PipeWire server answers instead of showing an empty but apparently working list of devices.

- **Updates from the Store are now one tap, for everything — not just widgets.** The Store's **Installed** tab shows a banner at the top the moment anything you installed has a newer version, with an **Update all** button that refreshes every community widget in one go. Themes, Deck profiles, pages and icon/sound packs keep their own per-row button, because each one opens the usual preview and approval before it changes anything — they're counted separately in the banner so it never promises more than it does. Nothing is ever swapped silently: an update is always the same import you'd do by hand, with the full preview and, for widgets, permission re-approval.
- **An update now tells you what changed before you accept it.** Creators can attach a short "what's new" line to each version, and it shows up wherever an update is offered: on the row in **Installed**, on the item's page in the Store, and in the daily notice. Until now the prompt asked you to re-approve a widget's permissions while explaining nothing, so deciding whether to update was guesswork.
- **The publish form now asks for everything a catalog card needs, so nothing is missing at review time.** Both ways of submitting (the form at xenon-app.com/submit and the GitHub issue template) now require the author name, a version number, at least one tag, a description, a category, the three colours that paint your card in the Store, and at least two screenshots. The colours and the widget package id are read straight out of the share code you paste, so for a theme they fill themselves in and you only correct them if you want the card to look different. Before this, half of a listing was optional: a submission could arrive with no pictures, no category and no colours, and the missing half had to be invented at review time from the code itself. Everything you enter now arrives already filled in on the review screen.
- **Creators can publish an update to something they already have in the catalog.** The publish form at xenon-app.com/submit has a new "This is an update" option: pick your existing entry from a list, say what changed, bump the version, and it replaces the published item instead of appearing as a second, unrelated listing. Before, an update was indistinguishable from a new submission and had to be recognised by hand at review time — and if the match was missed, the new version reached nobody, because Xenon links what you have installed to the entry it came from.

- **On a PC with two graphics cards, you can keep everything moving.** A new switch in Settings → Aspetto → Superficie, "Riduci animazioni su GPU ibrida", turns off the freeze described below, so the aurora, neon grid, animated background and Deck key decorations keep running. It stays on by default, because on that hardware those effects cost real frames. The switch only appears on a PC where it actually applies, so it will not show up on most machines.

### ✨ Improvements
- **Updates now download about a quarter of what they used to.** Every update fetched the whole project, which included the material that builds the xenon-app.com website: the screenshots in the README, the gallery pages, and the community catalog with its preset codes. None of that is ever read on your PC, but it was copied into your Xenon folder anyway on every install and every update. The update package now leaves it out, so a release goes from roughly 21 MB to under 6 MB, downloads faster on a slow connection, and your install folder stops filling up with files it never opens. The leftovers from earlier versions are removed automatically the first time you update. Nothing changes in what Xenon can do: the Store and the community gallery fetch their content from the website as they always have.
- **SDK widgets that draw their own clock now follow your 12h/24h choice.** A sandboxed widget that renders time itself — like the POW! Comic screensaver's big hero clock — had no way to know whether you run a 12- or 24-hour clock, so it was stuck on 24-hour. The `theme` bridge payload now carries a resolved `clock12` flag (auto/12/24 already decided), sent on connect and re-sent the instant you change the setting, so a widget's own clock can match the dashboard and show `01:30 PM` without a reload. Documented in the Widget SDK guide.
- **The Slideshow widget no longer stops you at 30 images.** The old limit existed because every image was stored inside your settings as text, which had to stay small enough for the settings backup — a folder of GIFs hit the wall fast. Slideshow images now live as real files on disk (the way iCUE keeps them), and your settings only remember which file goes where. So a slideshow can hold a whole folder of GIFs, saving and loading stays fast no matter how many you add, and unused images are cleaned up automatically when you remove them. Any slideshow you already have keeps working untouched. One thing to know: because the pictures now live on disk, a slideshow built this way isn't carried inside a settings backup the way the old inline images were — tell us if you'd like it to be.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **Your weather location now sticks on every screen.** Setting it on one screen could still leave another one showing a different place. v4.6.1 fixed the Xeneon Edge holding on to a stale location, but a browser could keep showing its own instead: it reverted to the automatic location on every refresh, and setting it by hand there only lasted until the next reload. Each screen stamps its settings with a version number so the others can tell when they are behind, and the weather save was handing back a number lower than the browser already had. The browser therefore read every incoming change as older than its own copy and ignored all of them, including the location set on the Edge. Both places that save settings now assign that number through the same shared rule, so the two cannot drift apart again.
- **A widget folder Xenon cannot read now says so, instead of just not appearing.** The folder name is the widget's id, so it may only contain lowercase letters, digits and dashes: a folder called `ip-info-widget 1.0.0` was skipped, while `ip-info-widget` worked. Xenon had always recorded why it skipped a folder, it just never showed it anywhere, so the widget silently failed to turn up and the only way to find out was to guess. The Store's Installed tab now lists every folder that was refused, with the reason and what to change, and it shows even when you have nothing installed yet, which is exactly the case where the old silence was most confusing.
- **A custom widget no longer reloads over and over when two screens are open.** v4.6.1 added syncing for widget storage, so changing a widget's settings on one screen carries over to the others. Reloading the widget is how the other screen picks that change up, but a widget that saves something as it starts, a cached result or a "last updated" time, wrote again the moment it was reloaded, and that write told the first screen to reload as well. The two screens bounced off each other and the widget reloaded without stopping, on both. Writes a widget makes while it is settling after a sync reload no longer trigger another one, and there is now a minimum gap between reloads. The syncing itself works as before.
- **Community widgets with a version like `2.0.0-beta` could never be updated.** Xenon accepts those version numbers when a widget is installed, but the check that decides "is a newer version available" only understood plain numbers like `2.0.0`, and deliberately stays silent when it can't read a version rather than risk offering you a downgrade. The result was a widget stuck on its beta forever, with no badge, no notice and no error to explain why. Version numbers with a `-beta` suffix, a leading `v`, or build metadata are now understood, and a prerelease correctly reads as older than its final release.
- **The daily "there are updates" notice only ever counted widgets.** If your themes, Deck profiles and icon packs all had updates waiting, it said nothing — and with the widget SDK switched off it never appeared at all, even though the Store had updates listed the whole time. It now covers everything you installed from the Store, names the item when there's only one, shows its "what's new" line, and opens straight to the Installed tab when you tap it.
- **Updated items no longer look as old as the day they first appeared.** The catalog only recorded a first-publish date, so a theme republished last week still showed its original date. Entries now also carry a last-updated date, stamped only when a save actually changes something.
- **On a PC with two graphics cards, your animated background stopped and nothing said why.** When the native app runs on a machine with both an integrated and a dedicated card, Xenon draws on the card that feeds the display, which leaves less room for heavy effects. To protect the frame rate it stops the animated background a few seconds after startup and leaves it stopped for the session. That part was deliberate, but two things around it were wrong. The aurora and neon grid that Xenon draws itself were supposed to stop first and never did, so the decoration kept moving while the background you chose was the one frozen, which is backwards. And nothing on screen explained any of it, so anyone writing a background saw it "stop looping" after a few seconds and reasonably assumed their own code was broken. The two layers now stop together, and the background editor tells you when your PC is the reason, with a pointer to the new switch above.
- **The Store no longer offers to re-import something you already have — it offers to update it.** Every catalog entry you've installed now shows a settled "Installed" state instead of an Import button, so you can't accidentally re-run an import over your own tweaks. When a newer version of an installed item is published, that same button turns into "Update…" (a normal re-import with the full preview and permission re-approval). This covers supporter drops too: an unlocked pack reads as installed, and shows "Update…" only when a newer version ships.
- **A custom widget grouped into a tab now shows its own name, not "Custom widget".** When you add a custom SDK widget as a tab, the tab always read the generic type name, so two custom widgets sharing a group were impossible to tell apart. Each tab now carries the name of the widget it actually holds (for example "Keyring"), and it fills in the moment the widget list finishes loading after a reload.

## [v4.6.1] - 17-07-2026
### ✨ New
- **You can turn off the idle animation pause.** After a minute without a touch or keypress, the dashboard pauses the aurora, neon grid and the small looping animations to save GPU, and resumes them the instant you interact. That was always on; a new switch in Settings → Aspetto → Superficie, "Pausa animazioni quando inattivo", lets you keep everything moving while the screen sits idle. It stays on by default, since on a Xeneon Edge driven by the integrated GPU the pause saves real power. The pause while the window is hidden is unaffected.

### ✨ Improvements
- **A supporter pack now tells you how to get in.** On a supporters-only entry, both in the app's Store and on the website catalog, a warm "Diventa supporter" heart button sits right under "Unlock with a code", linking straight to Buy Me a Coffee. Before, a visitor without a code saw only the locked button and no next step. It shows only on supporter entries; free and limited-edition items are unchanged.
- **"Opacità pannelli" now reaches the cards inside every widget, not just the tiles.** The nested cards, rows and tabs across the dashboard (the System sensor cards, calendar and task rows, media, streaming and smart-home surfaces, and the rest) carried a fixed solid colour, so turning panel opacity down made the tiles see-through but left their contents opaque. They now use that same themed colour tied to the panel's opacity, so a background image shows through the whole dashboard as one piece of glass. At the default opacity everything looks exactly as before; the Pixel Retro and Comic skins, opaque by design, are unchanged. Third-party widgets can join in too: the SDK's `theme` payload now carries `surfaceSoft` and `panelAlpha`, documented in the Widget SDK guide and on the Create site, so a community widget's own cards can follow the setting like the native ones.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **The "just landed in the Store" drop shows its artwork again.** The new-drop nudge was still loading its preview image from the old screenshot host, which no longer holds them, so it always fell back to a plain dark gradient. It now reads from the same assets host as the Store and the website, so a drop shows its real screenshot.

## [v4.6.0] - 17-07-2026
### ✨ New
- **A theme can carry both a light and a dark look, and follow your mode.** Xenon paints the half matching the mode you chose in Settings, and on Auto it follows the Windows scheme as it changes, with no re-import. The Light/Dark buttons switch between the two authored looks instead of resetting the theme, each half is contrast-checked on its own, and a colour you pick by hand always wins. Themes with a single look are unaffected. Authors: see the "one theme, light and dark" section in the maker's guide.
- **Theme colours now come from one semantic palette across the entire app.** You can set the app canvas, panels, secondary surfaces, controls, primary and muted text, borders, text on accent and the four state colours from one place; anything left on Auto is derived from the chosen surface. A contrast guard repairs unreadable combinations by default and can be switched off deliberately. The roles survive saved themes, import and export, backups and page presets, can be overridden on a single widget, and reach sandboxed SDK widgets as that tile's effective palette. They also cover what used to keep fixed colours of its own: the small grey labels across the dashboard and Settings, the Focus detail popup, Bit's speech bubbles and quick menu, and the AI chat tile, so a light palette stays readable everywhere (the full-screen voice overlay keeps its own dark contract). Existing three-colour themes import unchanged and gain derived roles automatically.
- **Community widgets can build a complete Discord surface, not just four voice buttons.** The Widget SDK adds three opt-in feeds: voice channels with their live member roster, the account's Soundboard catalog, and private DM and mention notifications; the existing `discord` feed remains the lightweight live voice state. Rich data loads only when the widget opens the relevant view, through fixed local sources selected by Xenon, and every feed has its own visible permission, rate limit and cache. Notification content keeps your privacy setting and is never revealed by default. Payloads and the refresh protocol are documented in the SDK guide and the Xenon Creator reference.
- **Widgets can speak through the dynamic island.** In the minimal top bar, a widget that declares the new **`island` permission** and that you approve may project one short line of plain text into the floating clock pill: a teleprompter's current sentence, a download percentage, a build status. The island expands into a card when the line wraps, an optional second line shows what is coming next in dim, a corner chip can carry a live number, and a hand-over glides the block up karaoke-style. The widget only ever sends text: Xenon draws the line (never links, images or markup, capped at 160 characters), one widget owns the island at a time, real notifications take priority, and the line clears when the widget's tile is gone. The full top bar has no island and is unchanged. Authors: see the *Island projection* chapter in the SDK guide.
- **Widgets can also keep a permanent badge next to the clock.** Where the island is for something happening right now, the new **`badge` permission** is for something that stays true: an unread count, a connection light, a star count. Up to four widgets can each hold their own chip, in both the full and minimal top bar, drawn as flat inline text like the clock and date. A badge may carry a leading glyph plus a colour for it (`icon` and `color`, the pair a Deck key's live badge already accepts), so the mark keeps the widget's identity while the value stays in your theme's text colour. In the minimal bar the badges are an island element, so **Settings → Aspetto → Elementi dell'isola** lets you drag them anywhere in the capsule or hide them. Same text-only, host-drawn sandbox as the island. Authors: see the *Persistent badge* chapter in the SDK guide.
- **New in the catalog: Teleprompter.** Paste a script into the tile, press play, and after a **3-2-1 countdown** it scrolls as large prompter text with the current sentence highlighted: tap to pause, drag the text to jump anywhere, set the speed from 0.5× to 3×, and watch the live **time remaining** estimate. Keep a library of named scripts that survive restarts, drop a **`[2s]` marker** in the prose wherever the scroll should hold, flip **mirror mode** for teleprompter glass, and mute the island line with one tap. Play/pause, speed and back-to-top can go on **Deck keys**, with speed and remaining time live on the keys themselves. On a Xeneon Edge your script is invisible to any recording or screen share by construction, since the Edge is a physically separate screen. Local and sandboxed: it asks only for storage, the island line and its Deck keys.
- **New in the catalog: GitHub Stars.** A small reference widget tracking any public repo's live star count, as a tile and as a permanent top-bar badge with GitHub's own gold star. Set the repo once and it keeps itself current. The Store's "Install example" button now offers Teleprompter and GitHub Stars alongside Hello Xenon.
- **Three new dashboard widgets: Fans, Energy and Batteries.** Add them from the "+" palette (System category). **Ventole** shows the live RPM of every fan your PC exposes: CPU and case fans through LibreHardwareMonitor, **each** graphics card fan individually from its own tachometer (so a card in zero-RPM mode reads stopped, not the percentage its curve is aiming for), and the AIO coolers and fan hubs that bypass the motherboard entirely (NZXT Kraken, Aquacomputer Octo/Quadro/D5 Next, MSI CoreLiquid, Razer and Arctic controllers, and more). Each fan is a compact row, colour-coded by how hard it works, with pumps scaled on their own range, grouped by where it physically sits: Scheda madre, Hub / AIO, Scheda video, Alimentatore. Because only you know what is plugged into "Fan #3", **tap a fan's name to rename it**: the names survive restarts, sync across screens, and clearing one restores the sensor's own name. Motherboard headers reporting 0 RPM collapse into one "No signal" line, since an empty socket and a stopped fan are indistinguishable there, while a zero on a graphics card or PSU stays a full row. **Energia** shows your PC's live draw in watts (CPU package and GPU), plus what the whole machine pulls from a PSU that connects over USB: Corsair i-series supplies are now found by asking the device what it is rather than matching a fixed model list, so recent models like an HX1200i report watts where other tools show nothing, and the PSU's own fan joins Ventole under Alimentatore. The number is the supply's output, what your PC consumes, not the wall socket. Alongside sits any power or energy reading from your Home Assistant (solar, a metered plug, the home meter, a UPS), picked in Settings → Smart Home. With sensor history on, **Storico consumi** adds 24 hours of CPU and GPU draw as sparklines, and the same charts join the System tile's History tab. **Batterie** shows the charge of Corsair peripherals through iCUE, any paired Bluetooth device, and a laptop or USB UPS battery, with sleeping devices fading out instead of freezing at a stale percent. Without LibreHardwareMonitor, iCUE or Home Assistant you get a friendly hint, never an error.
- **One tap to switch your hardware sensors on, CPU temperature included.** LibreHardwareMonitor reads CPU temperature, fan RPM and CPU watts through a driver that needs administrator rights, which Xenon's startup task only requests if INSTALL.bat itself was run as administrator, so a normal double-click left those sensors empty. The Fans and Energy widgets now say exactly that and offer an **Enable sensors** button: one Windows prompt, and Xenon fixes the startup task permanently and restarts itself. The same button lives in Settings → Performance → Hardware sensors.
- **Deck keys can show live sensor readings on their face.** The key editor's "Live value" list gains CPU and GPU load, temperatures, fan RPM, watts (including whole-PC draw from a digital PSU) and the battery of a specific wireless device, live on the dashboard Deck, the Virtual Deck popup and shared profiles alike.
- **Xenon AI now knows your fans, watts and batteries.** Ask "a quanto girano le ventole?", "quanto sta consumando il PC?", "quanto produce il fotovoltaico?" or "com'è la batteria del mouse?" on every provider (Gemini, local Ollama, OpenAI, Anthropic). Guardian's history records CPU and GPU power draw too, so trend questions work the way temperature history always has.
- **Xenon AI is now an expert on Xenon itself.** It carries a curated knowledge base covering setup and updates, the hardware-sensors permission flow, the marketplace (installing, ratings, publishing), supporter codes, the Widget SDK sandbox, Deck features, integrations, remote control, privacy and troubleshooting, and consults the right card before answering, in your language, on every provider and in Live voice. Asked to build a custom widget, it consults the actual Widget SDK reference instead of writing from memory. Its marketplace search knows icon packs and sound packs.
- **Widget SDK: a widget can ask you for an address, so NAS, Docker and self-hosted widgets can be shared at all.** An address written inside the widget works on its author's machine and nowhere else. A widget can now declare up to four **labelled blanks** instead, and you type the address when you approve it, port included (`192.168.1.50:32400`, `nas.local`, `https://plex.example.com` all work). The Store's **Installed** list has an **Address** button that reopens the field, prefilled. The widget still cannot pick its own destination: it declares that it needs an address and whether it may leave your network at all (default is your LAN only), Xenon re-checks the value on every request, and an address pointing back at this PC stays unreachable. Documented in the SDK reference and on the Create site, and Xenon AI knows about it.
- **Widget SDK: third-party widgets can read fans, power draw and device battery.** Fan RPM and watts need no new permission: they arrive in the `system` stream a widget may already request (`fans`, `power`, plus a `sensorAccess` flag so an empty state can name the real reason a reading is missing). Wireless peripheral battery gets its own `battery` stream, seeded the moment a widget connects. The fan names you chose are forwarded too, so a widget can tell a pump from a case fan. Documented in the SDK reference and on the Create site, including the traps: a fan reports RPM or a percentage, never both, and every watt value is nullable.
- **Sound packs: shareable soundboards, and Deck profiles keep their sounds.** Bundle audio clips into a **sound pack** (Settings → Widgets & sharing → *Create sound pack*: MP3/OGG/WAV, up to 24 clips / 1.4 MB, sized to stay publishable) and share it as a code. Installing adds its clips to the Deck key editor under a new **Soundboard** category, and a shared Deck profile now keeps its sound keys: clips travel as machine-independent references, so "Stingers › air horn" plays on any PC with the same pack, where before every shared profile arrived silent. Widgets can request the new `soundboard` permission to play pack clips, and only pack clips. Clips are verified by content at install, packs are previewed with per-clip pre-listen, and they appear in Installed for one-tap removal.
- **Icon packs: a new kind of creation you can share, import and publish.** Bundle SVG/PNG key icons into an **icon pack** (Settings → Widgets & sharing → *Create icon pack*: up to 120 icons, 24 KB each) and get a share code.
