Importing adds a section to the Deck key icon picker under the built-in library; picking an icon embeds it into the key, so your keys and any profile you share keep working if the pack is removed later. Validation is fail-closed: an SVG with scripts, external links or embedded content rejects the whole pack and names the offending file, in the builder too. Icon packs are a first-class catalog kind.
- **Star ratings arrive in the gallery: anonymous, no account, no tracking.** Open the Store (Impostazioni → Community → *Apri lo Store*), tap a creation in **Sfoglia** to open it, and rate it 1 to 5 stars. Limited editions and locked supporter drops show no control — you cannot try them without unlocking them — though their cards still show the average where one exists. Averages appear on the cards, in the app and on the website catalog, once an entry has enough votes, so a single vote can never look like consensus. Ratings are tied to your installation's anonymous id, the one supporter codes already use: no login, no e-mail, one vote per install per entry, re-tap to change it. Honest limit: an anonymous id raises the cost of vote stuffing rather than making it impossible; rate limits and the minimum-votes rule handle the rest.
- **Publishing to the catalog is now one web page, no GitHub account needed.** The **✨ Publish to the catalog** button copies your share code and opens the new publish portal on xenon-app.com, prefilled with your creation's kind and name: paste the code, add up to three screenshots, pass an anti-bot check, submit. Every submission still goes through the same moderated queue and is reviewed by a human before it appears. The GitHub form keeps working as an alternative.
- **The gallery flags updates for everything you installed from it, not just widgets.** Every catalog install now records which entry and version it came from, so a republished entry with a higher version appears under **Updates for your content** in the Store, and your Installed list shows each item's version. Themes, Deck profiles, pages, backgrounds, bundles and the new icon and sound packs were invisible to the update check before. Updating is a normal re-import: you see the full preview and re-approve any permissions before anything changes.
- **Everything you have installed now lives in one place: the Store's new "Installed" tab.** Installed widgets and everything else (themes, pages, Deck profiles, backgrounds, Ambient scenes, icon and sound packs) used to sit in two separate Settings lists that never showed the same picture. They are now one list inside the Store, each row carrying the creation's own screenshot when the catalog publishes one. Filter by kind, see what each download added and where it came from, update or export a widget you made, set a widget's address, and remove one item or **everything you have ever installed** in one action. Removal deletes exactly what an import brought with it, clears its assignments and grants, and falls back to the stock theme, page or Ambient scene if the removed content was active; your own creations are never touched. Receipts persist through settings, backup export and import, and restarts; content imported by older versions appears in a labelled legacy group.
- **Settings → "Widget e condivisione" is a lot calmer.** Nine "Export…" buttons in a row, a Limited edition box duplicating a shelf the Store already has, and step-by-step instructions competing with the controls are gone. Sharing is now two buttons: **Esporta…** opens a picker that tells you what each option exports, and **Importa…** is unchanged. Limited edition lives only in the Store; what is left is the sandbox switch, sharing, and a link to the developer docs.
- **Mirroring your PC's notifications is now a switch in Settings → Notifiche, not a button hidden in a widget.** It could only be turned on from the Notifiche widget's empty state, so without that widget there was no way to find it, and the mirror is also what feeds the pop-up alerts and the RGB "notification" light effect: a light set up for incoming notifications could never fire. Both switches, mirror Windows notifications and hide their content until tapped, now sit under the pop-up and sound options and stay in step with the widget's own controls. The widget remains the place to manage muted apps.
- **Limited editions can run themselves from the first claim to the last copy.** A creator chooses the stock, whether copies are individually numbered, whether editions are assigned in order or randomly, and whether claiming works only from Discord or also through the Store and website. Xenon Creator builds the encrypted editions and a private import manifest; the Supporter Hub keeps the real inventory, publishes a signed **Claim my copy** button in the Discord catalog and can expose a matching button on the site and in the app. Claimants pass an anti-bot check, sign in with Discord and must belong to the Xenon server; one Discord account owns one copy per drop, concurrent claims cannot take the same slot, and each owner gets a personal `XL-` code for that creation, valid on up to three devices. Numbering is optional, so the same flow handles ordinary fixed-stock releases.
- **Animated backgrounds have a "Frames per second" dial: smooth looks, a fraction of the cost.** A code-drawn background used to repaint the whole screen as fast as the display allowed. Every animated background is now capped at **30 frames per second** by default (motion speed does not change, the scene is simply painted less often), and a **Fotogrammi al secondo** field next to the background editor takes anything from 10 to 60. Theme creators can ship their preferred rate inside the theme, and since it is your machine doing the work the dial stays available on imported themes and backgrounds too, even when their code is locked. Existing backgrounds pick up the new default; set 60 for the old behaviour.
- **An animated background goes completely still when you walk away.** The dashboard already freezes its decorative animations after a minute of no interaction and when its window is hidden. The code-drawn background, the most expensive layer on screen, was the one that kept going; it now pauses with the rest and resumes on the first touch or keypress.
- **New Deck action: "Lock workstation" (#103).** A key that instantly locks Windows, in the Deck's System actions. (Thanks to the community contribution behind this.)
- **New Deck action: "Launch Steam game".** **Avvia gioco Steam** takes a game's Steam **AppID** (the number in its store page URL, e.g. `1086940`) and launches it through Steam, overlay and all. The "Open app" key can only start `steam.exe` and cannot pass a game to it, so this saves a `.bat` file per game. AppIDs are on the Steam store page URL or on SteamDB.
- **Press F11 to toggle fullscreen in the native app (#103).** The same switch the tray's Fullscreen option flips, so the window is placed correctly on its monitor and your choice is remembered for next launch. On the Xeneon Edge panel, where the kiosk manages its own placement, F11 deliberately stays out of the way. (Thanks to the community contribution behind this.)
- **The app switcher shows each app's own icon.** Every card in "Applicazioni aperte" carries the real application icon next to the name, whether or not it shows a live preview, which helps when several windows of the same app are open. Apps that used to show just a letter (Discord, packaged Store/UWP apps such as WhatsApp) now get theirs: the native helper resolves an icon even when Windows blocks the usual lookup, and pulls the Store tile logo for packaged apps. Only an app exposing no icon at all keeps its initial.
- **The dashboard finally has its own browser-tab icon.** A browser tab or the native window now shows the Xenon "X" mark instead of a blank page glyph.
- **xenon-app.com has been redesigned from the ground up.** Xenon green on dark ink, the same Inter type the dashboard uses, and every product shot in the Xeneon Edge's real 32:9 frame at native 2560×720; the plasma-orb hero and boot animation are gone. The home page is built around the four things people actually open Xenon for (the AI, the Deck, monitoring and Bit), with the community catalog, the creator guide, install steps, support and the supporters' wall each getting a focused section. The copy was rewritten in all five site languages (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH) to say what Xenon does instead of selling it, and to be checkable against the app: the widget grid names the real count and the real widgets, including Fans, Energy and Batteries, which FEATURES.md now documents too. The iCUE embed snippet wraps and has a copy button, and the catalog and creator-guide pages were restyled to match.
- **The home page reads the catalog to know what is open.** The old banner was hand-written for one sold-out drop, so NØVA advertised that everything was gone while POW!, the supporter pack actually available, went unmentioned. The catalog section now builds itself from the same `catalog.json` the app reads: whatever is open leads, with its artwork, tier, copies left or closing date, and a button that does the thing. Sold-out and past drops appear only when nothing is open, and a drop that has not opened yet stays hidden. A drop opening, selling out or expiring no longer needs a site edit.

### 🗑 Removed
- **The in-app no-code widget creator has been retired.** Picking from five fixed templates never produced anything you would want to keep, and it sat in the UI as if it were the main way to build a widget. Widgets you already created with it keep working exactly as before, they simply cannot be re-opened in the wizard. Settings → Crea links to the Widget SDK guide.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **Each Deck profile now keeps its own grid.** Columns and rows belong to the single profile, not to the whole Deck. Installing a profile from the catalog (or importing a shared one) no longer reflows the buttons of your other profiles, and a profile with many keys no longer blocks you from shrinking the grid of a profile with few: the row and column steppers act on the profile you are looking at, and only that profile's own keys set the minimum. Shared profile codes now carry their author's grid shape, so an import reproduces the intended composition instead of guessing it from the key count. Existing Decks keep the shape they have today on every profile.
- **You can link to a single creation in the catalog again.** A link straight to one entry — `xenon-app.com/catalog/#demonic` — is the natural way to answer "where do I get that theme?" on Discord, and it had quietly stopped working twice over. Links posted before the gallery moved to `/catalog/` pointed at `/community/`, which now holds only the catalog data and answered 404, so every entry link ever shared went dead; those links now land on the right entry again, hash and all. And on the new page the address bar dropped the `#demonic` the instant you arrived, so nobody who followed a link could copy or re-share the one they had just been sent. The open entry now owns the URL: click a card and the address bar becomes its link, close it and the link goes away, Back closes it. Every card and the entry view also carry a **Copy link** button, so you can grab a link without opening anything. Filtering and *Show more* still leave your scroll position alone.
- **Widgets keep their identity inside tab groups — no more "1 or none".** Widgets that remember something per-tile — which package a Custom widget shows, a Browser tile's open tabs, a Camera tile's selection, a Slideshow's position, a Second screen's session — identified "their" tile by the surrounding grid slot. Inside a tab group all tabs share one slot, so joining a group changed a tile's identity out from under it: a working Custom widget reverted to "Choose a widget for this tile" the moment you added a tab next to it, two Custom tabs fought over a single assignment (one or none ever showed), and un-assigning one killed both — exactly as reported on Discord. Every per-tile widget now identifies itself the way the Deck always has, by the widget itself rather than its slot, so assignments and tab lists survive grouping, ungrouping, and sitting next to a sibling of the same kind. Standalone tiles keep their state unchanged, and a Browser tile that was already grouped adopts its previously saved tabs instead of losing them. One note: a Custom widget picked *while the tile was already inside a tab group* was stored under the group's key — pick it once more.
- **A failed Discord login finally tells you what is actually wrong.** Connecting Discord could fail with a blank "Could not start login. Try again." no matter the cause, and Discord's own explanation reached neither the screen nor the server log. Every failure now lands on a precise message: a rejected Client ID points at the *Application ID* in the Developer Portal, a rejected Client Secret says to reset it and paste the new one, and a login Discord authorized but this PC could not finish points at VPN, firewall or proxy. The common one, *"invalid_scope"* the instant you click Authorize, names its real causes: the `rpc` access this needs is granted only to the account that **owns** the application (or an OAuth2 tester), so the Discord desktop app must be signed in with it, and Discord refuses it outright for an Activity ("Embedded App"); the redirect is not involved, which is where everyone looks first. Whatever Discord said is shown and logged. The new messages are translated into all 11 interface languages, and the whole Streaming section (Twitch, YouTube, Discord, Spotify) got a proper translation in Spanish, French, German, Portuguese and Russian, where it had been falling back to English. Also: pasting something that cannot be a Client ID is refused at save time with a hint; tapping Connect twice no longer opens two competing consent dialogs; and revoking Xenon under Discord → Authorized Apps now shows "connect in Settings" instead of retrying a dead token forever.
- **Lighting toggles no longer flip themselves back.** Each open dashboard carries its own copy of the settings from when it loaded, and any ordinary save from any surface (moving a widget, feeding Bit, changing a theme) wrote that stale copy over the whole lighting configuration: you would switch "Album → LED" off and, minutes later, Spotify painted the LEDs anyway while the checkbox still showed off. The lighting configuration is now owned by the RGB bridge alone, and a settings save keeps the persisted copy.
- **Sustained thermal alerts now tell you what "its threshold" actually is.** The setting promised an alert when the CPU or GPU stayed over its threshold for 15+ minutes without saying what those were, and they are not configurable. The description now names them: 90°C for the CPU, 88°C for the GPU, the same numbers Guardian uses for spike alerts. When the alert fires is unchanged.
- **Moving or renaming the install folder no longer silently breaks the shared core files.** The dashboard loads a couple of shared script files through a `server/shared` folder link, which kept pointing at the old location after a move: the files came back as 404 on every page load, and the repair tool (`npm run link:shared`, also run on every install) could not heal it, because a link whose destination no longer exists looked absent to its check. The tool now detects and replaces dangling links, so a moved install repairs itself on the next `npm install`.
- **Every weather metric shows its own colour bar again.** Each reading in the weather details carries a small coloured bar telling you whether the value is good, moderate or bad. They were all drawn against the left edge of the whole panel instead of their own card, stacked in one spot: a single stray stripe showing only the last metric's colour, and no bar next to the readings they marked. Each bar now sits on its own card.
- **Importing a theme no longer lets the previous theme bleed through.** When a theme code did not spell out one of the optional palette roles (surface, control, or the success, warning, danger and info status colours), the import kept whatever the previous theme had left there: a dark theme installed after a light pack arrived wearing the pack's cream surfaces, the dashboard rendered light while Settings insisted it was dark, and the mixed-up result was what got saved as that theme's gallery card, reproducing the corruption forever. An imported theme now replaces the palette: any role its code does not declare resets to automatic, derived from the theme's own background and text. Codes that declare every colour, and effect-only codes, behave as before. Re-import a mixed-up theme once to get a clean card.
- **Widgets that save settings no longer ask for their permissions over and over.** A widget granted the *storage* or *API keys* capability could lose that grant on the next settings save: the cleanup that rebuilds the permissions blob only knew the list-shaped grants (data streams, actions, servers) and dropped the yes/no ones, so the widget's saved-settings switch flipped itself off and Xenon kept re-showing the "asks for new permissions" dialog. The cleanup now preserves every capability the dialog can grant, and a test pins the two lists together.
- **The weather details are readable again on light dashboards, in the panel and in the widget.** The full weather panel stays a dark, colour-led island under every theme, so the sky reads as the sky, but its coloured readings (air quality, humidity, UV, PM2.5/PM10, NO₂, pollen, visibility) were painted in colours picked for paper, leaving them at roughly 1.7:1 against the dark glass. The Weather widget had the mirror problem: its detail, hourly and forecast sections sit on the widget's own surface but drew in white, so on a light one they vanished. Both now follow the surface they are actually on, and a custom status colour you picked is honoured wherever it can still be read. The sky, the big temperature and the condition icons are unchanged.
- **A shared widget can no longer be quietly re-badged as "created by you".** That mark decides which widgets you can export and publish, and an *imported* widget could be flipped to your own creation by reinstalling it as a Creator build, which would let someone else's widget be re-exported or submitted under your name. An imported widget now stays imported; your genuine Creator builds and local folders are unaffected. On the catalog side a package id is bound to whoever first publishes it, so a submission reusing another author's id is refused automatically. Your own updates and re-publishes are unaffected.
- **Settings are easier to read and to tap, and the "Aspetto" section is no longer a mess.** The category sidebar is wider with taller rows, a comfortable finger target on the touchscreen, and every settings card has real breathing room instead of its text running into the edges. This reaches **every** section, not just the standard card grid: the integration panels (Smart Home, Cameras, Spotify, Twitch), the top bar, Ambient, Slideshow, the tickers, Backup, Notifiche and the rest. **Aspetto** was reorganised: the near-empty live-preview panel is now a slim full-width strip, the theme gallery, the light/dark/auto switch and the "Personalizza" divider run full width, and the colour, surface, font and top-bar cards sit in two tidy columns with the tall ones paired. The lone **"Accento dall'album"** toggle, which only tints the *interface* accent, now lives in the **Colori** card with wording that makes clear it follows the cover art, so it is no longer mistaken for the separate **"Album → LED"** effect that drives your physical RGB LEDs. Both controls were kept; only naming and placement changed, across all 11 languages.
- **The "Sfondo app" colour no longer looks broken when it is simply covered.** Setting the app-canvas colour (Aspetto → Colori → *Sfondo app*) does nothing visible while a wallpaper, static or animated background is active, because that background sits on top of it, so the picker looked ignored. The control now shows a short note in that exact case, in all 11 languages. The colour was always applied correctly, just hidden.
- **The weather chip in the topbar no longer looks like a stray button.** In both bars the temperature sat inside a raised pill (outline, tinted fill, drop shadow) floating oddly next to the plain clock and date, and in the minimal bar a leftover shadow kept the outline after the fill was removed. The weather now sits flat inline like the time and date, keeping just its animated condition icon: no fill, no outline, no hover background.
- **The per-tile hide button works again in Personalizza, so any widget comes off the dashboard with one tap.** Every tile's hide (eye) and move-to-page buttons had become unclickable while customising the layout: they were painted underneath the invisible drag surface that lets you grab a tile anywhere, so a tap read as the start of a drag. It hit every widget but was most visible on a custom or imported one, which has no other remove control. The controls now sit above the drag surface, and custom widgets stop reacting to taps on their own content while the layout editor is open.
- **Hidden "Rete & Gaming" cards can be brought back again.** In the System tile, System and Network share one merged "Sistema" view, but the Customize panel only listed the hidden *System* cards (RAM, Disk…), so hiding Ping, FPS or Bandwidth removed it with no way back short of a full layout reset. The list now includes hidden cards from both halves, each with a Restore chip.
- **The dashboard server is much harder to knock offline, and a restart reliably brings it back (#100).** A single unexpected error in one background task (a sensor read, a lighting update, the game or media probes) could bring down the entire server, most likely on machines where the Windows/PowerShell sensor layer was already failing; the server now logs a stray error and keeps serving. And a restart from the tray or after an update gave up instantly if the previous instance had not released its port yet, so "Restart" appeared to do nothing; it now waits and retries for a few seconds.
- **An open dashboard no longer keeps your CPU and GPU busy while it just sits there (#99).** A handful of pulsing-dot effects (the topbar's online dot, visible on every dashboard, the live indicators in the Claude, Discord, OBS, Twitch, YouTube, Streamer.bot and Smart Home widgets, and the Ambient clock's breathing glow) animated their glow in a way that forces the browser to re-style and re-paint the page at full display rate, every frame, forever. They look identical but now animate on the GPU's cheap path, so an idle dashboard finally goes quiet in the browser, the native app and on the Xeneon Edge. The Ambient screensaver benefits most.
- **The last of the always-busy animations are gone too (#99).** The Deck's "Lampeggia" key effect and the Store's holographic sheen and loading skeletons kept the render pipeline awake for as long as a blink key stayed latched or the Store stayed open. All three now animate on the GPU's cheap path, looking exactly as before. Since third-party widgets can burn CPU the same way from inside their sandbox, the SDK guide now has a performance chapter naming the patterns to avoid.
- **A Browser widget showing a live camera no longer maxes out the CPU (#99).** A page that changes every frame made the widget's engine render and encode every frame the camera produced, and the dashboard decode all of them, on every screen showing the tile. The stream is now capped at 24 frames per second at the source (above what IP cameras typically send, so the picture is unchanged) and the dashboard skips to the newest frame instead of decoding stale ones; the Second screen mirror got the same treatment. Still pages are unaffected.
- **The calendar no longer ends up with two highlighted days when left open past midnight.** The current day gets a soft outline and the day you are looking at is filled in, normally the same day. At an automatic midnight rollover only the outline followed, leaving yesterday filled and today outlined until you tapped a date. Unless you had manually picked another day, the fill now rolls over with the outline; if you had, your choice stays put.
- **"Nothing playing" no longer gets stuck for good after the PC has been idle a while.** Windows' media service can quietly go blank after a stretch of inactivity, stopping reporting without raising an error, so the reader that keeps one connection open never noticed music started afterwards. The native helper already recovered on its own; its PowerShell fallback now does too, refreshing its connection within about a minute of the stall.
- **The app switcher no longer gets stuck forever on "Loading applications…".** It asked the backend for the open windows and waited with no time limit, so an unresponsive backend left the panel on the loading message indefinitely, with no error and no retry. It now gives up after a sensible wait and shows a clear "Couldn't load applications" message with a **Retry** button.
- **The Settings screen reflects your appearance choices, and "Reset defaults" no longer wipes settings you did not mean to touch (#100).** Settings used to have a fixed frosted look of its own, so lowering panel opacity or the glass and background blur seemed to do nothing while it was open; it now follows the same Aspetto sliders as the rest of the dashboard. And the single **Ripristina default** quietly reset every preference, even your weather location, tickers and integrations, which is how a theme reset could leave the weather guessing your city. It is now split: **Ripristina default** in Aspetto → Temi resets only the look (colours, style, surface, font), while **Ripristina tutte le impostazioni** at the bottom of Settings does the full reset.
- **The desktop app no longer pins a CPU core, and spins your fans, sitting idle on the Xeneon Edge, on PCs with two graphics chips.** With both an integrated and a dedicated GPU, Windows drives the Edge from the *integrated* chip over USB-C while the app drew the dashboard on the *dedicated* card, so the processor copied every frame between the two, non-stop, burning well over a full CPU core even on a still dashboard; left running, the on-screen Deck could stop responding. The app now renders on the chip that actually drives its display. Because that chip has less real-time budget and a full-viewport animated background can alone exceed it, the app tells the dashboard when it is on the weaker chip and an animated background freezes to its current frame there, the same trick already used when you step away. Nothing changes on a single-GPU PC, in a browser, or without an animated background.
- **The desktop app no longer silently stops updating after sitting on the Xeneon Edge for a while.** Because the kiosk window lives on a secondary screen and never takes keyboard focus, Windows eventually treated its web view as a background window and put it to sleep, freezing its timers and its live connection: the clock stopped, the Deck stopped responding, and a tap usually did not wake it. The app now keeps its web view awake regardless of focus.
- **Theme, colours, language and every other setting now really stick.** On some machines a change appeared to save but never reached disk, so a reload, especially on the Xeneon Edge which starts each session with a clean slate, snapped back to the last stored version. The server saves each store by writing a temporary file and renaming it into place, and that rename fails whenever another program holds the file open for a moment (an antivirus scan, the Search indexer, a second backend copy left running); one failed rename aborted the whole save. The server now retries the rename briefly, protecting every store: settings, Deck, notes, tasks, timers, calendar and tokens. Closing a stale second backend is still worth doing.
- **Importing a heavy theme pack no longer leaves the dashboard "deaf", and "Remove all" really removes it.** After importing a large package (animated background, widgets, a font), the dashboard could stop talking to its backend within minutes: the app switcher hung, the Deck went quiet, and removals and edits silently never saved, which is why a removed pack could come back after a restart, stacking duplicate theme cards. Each save was answered with a full copy of the settings, several megabytes once a big pack was installed, that the dashboard never read, tying up one of the browser's six connections until none were left. Saves are now answered with a tiny acknowledgement, and the dashboard drains every reply it does not use.
- **A community widget that reads Discord no longer opens claiming "Discord isn't active" when it plainly is.** The SDK's `discord` feed is pushed only when the voice state changes, so on a freshly loaded dashboard a widget mounting received no starting snapshot and concluded the account was not linked. The built-in Discord widget never hit this because it reads the state directly, which a sandboxed widget cannot. Xenon now hands any widget granted that feed a real snapshot when it starts.
- **An animated backdrop behind the Deck keys now stops when every other animation does.** Performance Mode, game mode and the idle freeze exist to hand the machine back to what you are doing, and a Deck decorated with an animated image (a GIF or animated SVG) ignored all three, repainting through your game. Nothing can reach inside such an image to pause it, so Xenon swaps it for a still frame of itself while animations are off.
- **A Deck key that shows a live value no longer draws it on top of its own icon.** Keys that display something live paint the value across the top of the cap, but the cap still centred its icon in the full height, so the two landed on the same pixels. The cap now keeps that strip clear and centres the icon in what is left.
- **A widget on a dashboard page you were not looking at no longer shows stale information when you swipe back.** Pages you are not viewing stay loaded but are cut off from live data, so a parked page costs nothing; nothing woke its widgets up again, so a widget scrolling back into view kept showing whatever it last saw, which for feeds that report only when something happens could be a long wait. Swiping to a page now brings its widgets up to date immediately.
- **A duplicated tile no longer vanishes the moment you tap Done.** If a copy landed on a page before the original's, it showed up while arranging the dashboard and disappeared on leaving edit mode: still there and taking up space, just drawn as nothing. The layout code looked up "the tile for this widget" without distinguishing original from copies, so it applied the original's settings to the copy, and since a duplicated tile's original is normally hidden, the copy inherited "hidden". Copies now keep their own visibility.

## [v4.5.2] - 13-07-2026
### 🛍️ Store
- **Limited editions and individually sold creations now have their own unlock codes.** The Store accepts two kinds of personal codes: the supporter code (`XS-…`) opens supporter drops for as long as your support is active, and the new per-creation code (`XL-…`) — issued when you reserve a limited edition or buy a single theme — opens exactly that creation, forever. A code used on the wrong kind of drop now says so clearly instead of a generic error. All codes remain personal: they work on up to 3 of your devices (so a PC change never locks you out), and the unlock form now reminds you not to share them — codes used beyond their devices are detected and blocked.

### 🧹 Removed
- **The "Create share card" button is gone from the Share dialog.** Its "real screenshot" backdrop captured the whole desktop (often the wrong monitor), and the card never played a role in publishing to the catalog — gallery entries without screenshots already get an automatic colour-swatch preview. Sharing itself is unchanged: copy link, download file, protect with access codes and Publish to the catalog all remain.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **Logging into a page in the Browser widget now shows up on every screen — no app restart needed (#96).** The Browser widget behind, say, a camera stream needs you to sign in. But your desktop dashboard and the Xeneon Edge each run their own copy of that page (they can be different sizes, so they have to), while sharing one saved login. So when you signed in on one screen and it jumped to the stream, the other screen sat on the login page — the sign-in had actually been saved, its page just never reloaded to notice, and only restarting the whole app got it there. Now, when one screen moves past a shared page (a sign-in redirect, a link), any other screen still sitting on that exact same page follows along automatically and lands on the stream too. It stays out of your way: a screen you're actively using, or one you've browsed somewhere else on, is never pulled around, and typing a new address on one screen doesn't drag the others with it.
- **The setup.exe now really installs all of Xenon on a clean PC — the full installer no longer dies the instant it starts.** On a machine with no Xenon backend, the one-click setup hands off to a console that downloads, verifies and installs the engine — but that console crashed on its very first check (a PowerShell 5.1 quirk: with strict error handling on, redirecting the error output of the "is the backend installed?" task query turns its harmless "task not found" message into a fatal error — precisely and only on the fresh installs the bootstrap exists for). All users saw was a window flashing shut, and only the shell got installed (#95). The check now runs in a way PowerShell can't trip over, so the flow works as advertised: shell installs, console opens, engine downloads and installs, dashboard comes alive.
- **The Media tile's Spotify seek bar now follows what your PC is actually doing — pause stops it, play moves it, instantly.** The bar used to trust only Spotify's online status, which can lag or go silent for a long stretch when Spotify rate-limits the app's status checks — so the bar kept crawling through a pause, or sat frozen on a song that was clearly playing. Since this bar only appears when Spotify runs on this PC, it now takes play/pause straight from Windows' own live media state: pausing stops it the same second, resuming moves it again, even while Spotify's answers aren't coming through. The Spotify widget does the same whenever the music plays locally.
- **Skipping songs from the Media tile now resets the bar to the start — with the right total.** Changing track with the tile's next/previous buttons (or the song ending on its own) could leave the previous song's time on the bar, and even show the new song against the old song's total length, because Spotify keeps answering with the old track for a while. The bar now flips to 0:00 the moment the track changes and reads the song's total duration from Windows directly, so the times are right even before Spotify catches up.
- **Restarting a song with ◀ now rewinds the bar too — even while paused — and seeks made in Spotify itself show up.** Pressing previous mid-song restarts the same track from the beginning, but since the song didn't change the bar just kept counting from where it was. The bar now watches the position your PC reports for the playing track — a restart or an in-app seek moves it to the right spot within a couple of seconds — and every tap on the tile's own play/pause/previous/next asks Spotify for the outcome right away, so a paused song sent back to 0:00 (a case Windows can't see: Spotify freezes its reported position while paused) lands on the bar in about a second instead of several.
- **The song's elapsed time now stays accurate even while Spotify's online service goes quiet.** The time Windows reports for a playing track only refreshes on events (play, pause, seek, track change) — Spotify never updates it mid-song — so whenever Spotify's own status checks were rate-limited, both the Spotify widget and the Media tile could only count seconds blindly from the last answer they got, drifting further from the app's real position (the "0:28 here, 1:10 in Spotify" mismatch). The media reader (native helper v0.5.2 and its PowerShell fallback) now projects that frozen timestamp forward by how long the track has actually been playing, so Windows' position is live — and both bars quietly re-align to it whenever Spotify's answers stop coming, mid-song included.
- **Spotify controls now tell you when Spotify is too busy to respond.** When Spotify is rate-limiting the app, tapping shuffle, like, seek or any other Spotify control silently did nothing. You now get a brief "Spotify is busy — retrying shortly" notice so you know it's Spotify catching its breath, not a broken button.
- **The Spotify widget no longer talks to Spotify while it's hidden behind another tab — which was quietly breaking everything else.** A Spotify widget grouped into a tabbed tile kept polling Spotify all session long even when a different tab (Chat, Discord…) was on screen. All those invisible requests are what tripped Spotify's request limit — the real reason the player kept showing stale state, wrong times and a dead queue. The widget now goes fully silent while its tab is hidden and resyncs the moment you switch to it (the same fix the Cameras and Second-screen tiles got in v4.5.1).
- **The Spotify widget now keeps showing the right song even when Spotify's status service goes quiet.** With music clearly playing, the widget could sit on a ▶ Play button — or worse, on a track from many minutes ago — because it only believed Spotify's online status, which freezes for the whole duration of a rate-limit window. When that status stops arriving, the widget now mirrors what Windows reports for the Spotify app on this PC: the actual song (title, artist, duration, position) and its live play/pause state, switching back to Spotify's own data the moment it answers again.
- **Play, next and previous in the Spotify widget keep working even while Spotify's online service refuses commands.** During a rate-limit window every Web API control gets rejected — but when the music is playing on this PC, the basic transport doesn't need the Web API at all. Those three buttons now fall back to Windows' own media control (the same instant path the Media tile's buttons use), so tapping ⏭ actually skips the song instead of toasting "Spotify is busy". Spotify-only controls (shuffle, like, seek, playlists, devices) still need Spotify to answer.
- **"Up Next" no longer claims the queue is empty when it simply couldn't be read.** A failed queue check (rate limit, a network blip) was displayed as "The queue is empty" — indistinguishable from a genuinely empty queue. A failure now keeps the last queue you had on screen, and if there's nothing yet it says "Spotify is busy" instead of lying about emptiness.
- **UniFi Protect camera credentials (and every other setting) now reliably reach the server on customized installs.** On dashboards with imported themes, Ambient scenes or rich decorations, the settings data had grown past a hidden 64 KB browser transport limit the background save was subject to — so every settings save from that screen was silently dropped before it even left the browser, while the screen's own local copy made everything *look* saved. The most visible casualty was the Cameras setup: "Connect" found all your cameras, but the console password never actually reached Xenon — the tile kept saying "Set up", and coming back to Settings showed "Saved" yet "Connection failed" until you typed the whole password in again. Settings saves no longer use that capped transport, they verify the server really accepted the change, and a save that fails (say, during a server restart) now retries by itself until it lands instead of being lost. The connection tests for Streamer.bot and Wave Link, which flush the settings first, are covered by the same fix.
- **The Cameras tile comes alive right after a successful "Connect".** It used to keep showing "Set up" for up to half a minute (its status-poll interval) even though the connection had just succeeded; the settings page now pushes the fresh credentials through and refreshes the tiles immediately.
- **The UniFi console password and the Home Assistant token no longer linger in the browser's local storage.** They are server-side secrets: they now stay in memory only until the save reaches the server (like the OpenAI/Anthropic keys already did), and the "Saved" placeholders still survive a reload.
- **The Playback tile's cover art no longer vanishes when you reload the dashboard (or restart iCUE) mid-song.** Windows publishes a track's cover a beat after its title, and for browser playback (YouTube in Chrome/Edge) it only re-sends the artwork when the track changes — so a dashboard that (re)connected in between showed the title and channel but an empty "No media" cover for the rest of that video. Xenon now remembers the current track's cover on the server and hands it to every screen — a browser tab, a fresh reload, the Xeneon Edge after an iCUE restart, a second dashboard — so the art stays put through a reconnect instead of falling back to the placeholder. It's tied to the exact track, so a real song change still clears to the new cover (or the placeholder until it loads), never the previous one.

## [v4.5.1] - 13-07-2026
### 🛍️ A proper Store for community creations
- **The community catalog is now a real storefront — designed to make you want to install.** What used to be a cramped wall of tiny cards is now a proper Store: a branded header with the Store name, a "Preview before install" reassurance, and an icon category rail (All, Limited, Themes, Backgrounds, Widgets, Pages, Decks, Packages, Ambient) that reads at a glance. Everything below is grouped into clean, spacious sections by type — each with a count and a "See all" — behind one tidy toolbar with search, category and sort. Long lists page in with "Show more" instead of dumping everything at once.
- **A cinematic spotlight up top — that always leads with something you can actually get.** The Store opens on a big hero banner with full-width artwork, the creation's palette and one clear call to action. It follows a deliberate order: an available limited-edition drop leads when there's one, otherwise a supporter/exclusive creation, otherwise the featured free creation — a sold-out drop never headlines the Store (it stays in its own section below). Product cards are larger and more premium too: rich previews that gently zoom on hover, a glowing lift, a bold tier badge, colour swatches, and a single confident Import (or Reserve) button.
- **Tap any card to open it up close.** Every card in the Store — and every card on the website catalog — now opens a full detail view: a large gallery of all the creation's screenshots with a thumbnail strip, arrows and a "1 / 6" counter, click-to-zoom to fullscreen, alongside the complete description, its colour palette with hex values, all its tags, and the one action (Import, Reserve or Unlock). No more squinting at a thumbnail to decide.
- **The filter dropdowns are properly styled now.** The category and sort menus — in the app and on the website — no longer drop the plain grey operating-system list; they use Xenon's own dropdown, accent-lit and consistent with the rest of the UI.
- **Every card always shows a preview now.** When a creation ships a screenshot you see it; when it doesn't, Xenon draws a live preview from the creation's own colours — a mini dashboard for themes and pages, flowing waves for backgrounds, a progress ring for widgets, a key grid for Decks — so the grid reads as a gallery of looks rather than a row of blank boxes.
- **Two exclusive shelves, treated as equals.** Limited-edition drops and Supporters content each get their own premium shelf — a tinted, bordered section (violet for Limited, gold for Supporters) with its lead line and, for Supporters, a "Become a supporter" button right in the header. Supporter themes and packs are now shown off as a proper collection instead of a small banner, so it's obvious what's exclusive and how to get it: become a supporter and import it with your personal code, which stays yours for good.
- **"How it works" for supporters, explained.** The Supporters shelf now has a "How it works" panel — and the website catalog spells it out inline — covering exactly what supporting gets you: exclusive themes and packs with a fresh drop each month (yours forever once unlocked), a Supporter role on Discord with priority on bug reports and support tickets, and access that lasts in proportion to your contribution. It also tells you what happens after donating — your personal code arrives by email on its own, and if it doesn't, Discord or supportxenon@protonmail.com is the fallback to get registered by hand. Two clear next steps besides that: support, or join the Discord.
- **Drops can be scheduled and retired.** Catalog entries can now carry a visibility window (`activeFrom`/`activeUntil`) plus a manual on/off override, evaluated live on both the app and the website — so a monthly supporter or limited drop appears on time and quietly retires when its window closes (and can be resurfaced any time). It's how "this month's" exclusive content stops being installable by newcomers once the month is over.
- **The Store is one tap from anywhere in Settings.** A solid accent **Store** button now sits in the Settings header, reachable from every category — and it also leads its own section ("Widget e condivisione") as a prominent, accent-lit card above the other options. Either one opens the community gallery full-screen.
- **You'll know when a new exclusive drop lands.** When a fresh Supporters creation or an available Limited edition appears in the Store, Xenon shows a single, elegant card that previews it, tells you what it is, and offers one tap to reserve it or become a supporter. It's deliberately unobtrusive: it appears at most once a day, announces a whole batch of new drops with one card (never a pile of pop-ups), never interrupts a game or the screensaver, and carries a plain **"Don't show me new drops"** switch that turns it off for good — with everything still one tap away in the Store whenever you want it.

### 🔑 Supporter codes are now personal, one-time and automatic
- **Every supporter gets their own code — and it only works for them.** Supporter drops used to rely on shared permanent codes: once one leaked, anyone could unlock everything forever. New supporter drops use a lock whose key never travels inside the shared bundle — entering your personal `XS-` code checks it live against Xenon's supporter service, which hands out the key only if the code is genuine, unspent and yours. A code works on up to **3 of your devices** (reinstalling or re-importing on the same device never consumes anything), and **whatever you unlock stays yours forever**, even after your supporter period ends.
- **Your code arrives by itself, seconds after you support.** Donating on Buy Me a Coffee now registers you automatically: how long you stay a supporter is computed from your contribution, your personal code is generated on the spot and emailed to you, and renewing stacks cleanly on top of the time you have left. The old way — sending your email or a donation screenshot on Discord or to supportxenon@protonmail.com — remains as the fallback if the email doesn't reach you.
- **The Discord Supporter role manages itself.** Link your Discord once — from the button in your code email, or with the `/link` command on the server — and the Supporter role is granted instantly, a reminder arrives a few days before your period ends, and the role is removed automatically when it expires (and comes right back when you renew).
- **Classic offline codes keep working.** Anything previously shared with the permanent `XN-` codes unlocks exactly as before, and creators can still generate that kind of lock for giveaways and friends — the one-time system is for supporter drops, where "one code each" actually matters.

### 🖼️ Custom fullscreen Ambient scenes
- **The Ambient / Screensaver screen can now be a scene built entirely from Xenon's own building blocks.** Alongside the classic clock-and-widgets scene, you can install a custom fullscreen scene that freely places a huge clock, the weather, what's playing, your agenda and tasks, live system and network stats, plus text, images, shapes and gradients — anywhere on the display, each with its own colours and look, and it can even embed community widgets you've installed. These scenes are authored as shareable codes (Claude's Xenon creator tooling can produce one to your description, or find one in the gallery) and installed from Settings → Appearance → Import.
- **Installed scenes are yours to manage.** Every scene you install appears under Settings → Ambient → "My scenes", where you can set any one as the screensaver that shows when the dashboard sits idle, or remove it.
- **Import is lossless, with a live preview.** A scene code carries everything — the layout, every colour and style, the pictures inlined so they arrive intact, and the community widgets it uses bundled right in. On import you see a real thumbnail of the scene first, then get exactly what was built: no missing images, no hunting down widgets.

### ⬇️ One tap really updates everything now
- **On the native app, tapping "Update" finally updates the whole of Xenon — with progress on screen.** Until now that tap only replaced the thin app shell: the dashboard itself (where every feature lives) was never updated on the native app, and if anything failed the "Updating Xenon…" toast just sat there forever with nothing happening. One tap now updates the dashboard first — download, verify, install, with live progress — and then the app itself, showing the download percentage as it goes. Every failure now says so, in your language, instead of silently doing nothing.
- **If an update can't be applied, Xenon now tells you exactly what happened.** The updater has always restored your previous version automatically when something went wrong (a failed download of dependencies, a new version that wouldn't start) — but the screen just spun for six minutes and gave up with a vague message. Now the moment the rollback completes you get a clear explanation ("dependency installation failed", "the new version did not start"…) and a Retry button; and if the page was closed during the update, the explanation appears the next time you open the dashboard.
- **Updates now leave a clean installation.** Files that belonged to an older version but are no longer shipped used to stay on disk forever. Each update now records exactly what it installed and the next one removes what the new version no longer needs — only files the updater itself put there; your data, settings, layouts and everything you created are never touched.
- **Existing installs get rescued too.** If your dashboard predates this release, the app update alone used to leave it stranded on the old version. The new app notices that and offers a one-tap "Dashboard update available" that brings everything current.

### 📦 One download that installs everything
- **The setup you download from GitHub now installs all of Xenon, not just the app.** Downloading `Xenon_x64-setup.exe` used to give you only the thin screen app — which then showed an empty gray dashboard, because the engine behind it was never installed (the actual installer was hidden in the "Source code" zip). The setup now detects a missing engine and installs it for you: verified download, dependencies, startup task, everything. One file, one double-click, done.
- **A permanent download link.** Every release now also carries `Xenon-Setup-x64.exe` — a stable name, so `github.com/marcimastro98/Xenon/releases/latest/download/Xenon-Setup-x64.exe` always fetches the newest version. The website's download buttons and the README now point straight at it: no more guessing which file to pick on the release page.

### 🧰 The installer retries instead of giving up (#87)
- **A component that fails to download no longer requires running INSTALL.bat again.** Downloads and package installs (the dashboard libraries, FFmpeg, the temperature sensors, PresentMon, the helper) fail transiently sometimes; the installer now retries each of them automatically, gives everything that still failed one more pass at the end, and closes with a clear component checklist — [OK] or [MISSING] — so you can see at a glance that everything landed.
- **The installer no longer looks frozen while something is downloading or installing.** The steps that used to sit silent for up to a minute — installing Node.js, FFmpeg or the sensors through Windows Package Manager, downloading PresentMon or the app itself — now show a live spinner with the seconds counting up, so it's always clear the setup is working and hasn't hung.

### 🚀 Releases are now published complete
- **No more broken minutes right after a release.** Release assets used to be built *after* a version went live, so for several minutes the release page existed but the helper, the app installer or the update signatures weren't attached yet — anyone installing or updating in that window hit errors or silently missed pieces. Every asset is now built and attached before the release becomes visible, so updating the second a release drops works exactly like updating a day later.

### 🖥️ Xeneon Edge preview steps aside for Settings (#86)
- **The Xeneon Edge preview now pauses while you're in Settings.** When the browser-only "Xeneon Edge preview" was on, opening Settings squeezed the whole settings panel into the same wide 2560×720 letterbox, making it small and awkward to use. The preview is meant for arranging the dashboard, so it now automatically drops back to your browser's real size while Settings are open and returns to the Edge frame the moment you close them — the preview stays on, it just gets out of the way when you're not looking at the layout.

### 📰 Follow any RSS feed in News and the ticker (#93)
- **You can now add your own RSS or Atom feed by pasting its link.** The News widget used to let you follow curated outlets by name or any topic through Google News; now, on top of that, you can paste any feed URL — your favourite blog, a niche site, a regional paper like `nu.nl` — straight into the "Manage feeds" search box and follow it. Its headlines merge into the same time-sorted stream as everything else and, like every news source, flow into the scrolling ticker. Custom feeds appear as their own clearly-marked chips so you can tell them apart from outlets and topics, and remove them with one tap.

### 🎨 Paste SVG code anywhere you can add a picture
- **Everywhere Xenon lets you drop in an image, you can now paste raw SVG code instead of uploading a file.** If you design your own vector graphics, saving them out to a `.svg` and picking the file every time you tweak something is a chore — so alongside the usual "Choose image" / "Upload" button there's now a "Paste SVG" option that takes the `<svg>…</svg>` markup directly. It's available on a widget's background, ornamental frame and overlays (the 🎨 Decor editor), on the whole-dashboard wallpaper (Settings → Background), and on Deck key faces and the key-grid background. The pasted artwork is used exactly like an uploaded picture and stays crisp at any size because it's kept as vector, not flattened to a bitmap.
- **Safe by design.** Pasted SVG is only ever shown as an image, so it's rendered in the browser's locked-down mode with no scripts or outside requests — the same treatment a `.svg` file you upload already gets.

### 📹 Home Assistant cameras in the Cameras tile (#92)
- **Your Home Assistant cameras now show up on the dashboard — whatever brand they are.** The Cameras tile used to be UniFi Protect only; it now also pulls live snapshots from Home Assistant, and because Home Assistant already speaks to every camera it supports (TAPO, Reolink, ONVIF, generic RTSP/MJPEG, Ring and more) and hands them all back the same way, connecting it brings *all* of those into Xenon at once. It's the practical path to TAPO on the dashboard: let Home Assistant do the camera plumbing, and Xenon shows the picture.
- **One tile, both sources, side by side.** UniFi and Home Assistant cameras share the same grid and the same controls — the layout options (columns, fill/fit, aspect, refresh rate) apply to all of them, and tapping any camera enlarges it with the same rotate, mirror and pinch-style zoom/pan you already had. Home Assistant cameras are marked with a small "HA" badge when both sources are on screen, so you can always tell them apart.
- **Opt-in and private.** Home Assistant is connected once in Smart Home settings; in Settings → Cameras you simply tick which of its cameras to show (and drag them into the order you want) — connecting Home Assistant for control never dumps every camera onto the tile. As with UniFi, your Home Assistant token stays on the server and only the camera images ever reach the screen, through a local-only proxy.

### 💾 Backups now account for your community widgets and scenes
- **Your backup now knows which community widgets and Ambient scenes you have installed — and tells you how to get them back.** A backup file saves everything that lives in your settings (themes, layouts, custom animated backgrounds, Deck, calendars, notes and the rest), but community widgets and Ambient scenes are separate installed packages that were never part of it — so restoring a backup onto a fresh machine left their spots on the dashboard empty with no hint why. The backup now carries a lightweight list of those packages (just their names, never their code), and after you restore it Xenon tells you exactly which ones aren't installed here yet, so you know to re-import them from their gallery or share codes. Your backup stays small and safe to share: it never bundles someone else's widget code.
- **When you import a community widget or Ambient scene, Xenon reminds you to keep its code.** Because these packages don't travel inside a backup, the import code is what lets you reinstall them later. The import screen now says so up front — keep the code somewhere safe, or you won't be able to get the widget or scene back if you ever lose it.

### 🐞 Fixes
- **Live tiles no longer stay black when they live inside a tabbed tile.** The Cameras tile and the Second-screen (mirror another monitor) tile only refresh their feed while they're actually on screen — but when a tile was grouped into a tab (for example Cameras sharing a tile with Discord and Chat), its picture could sit stuck on black even with that tab open, because the tile watched only its own box for visibility changes and missed the moment the tab group around it revealed it. On Cameras this looked especially odd: the grid stayed black yet tapping a camera to enlarge it still loaded a picture. Both tiles now detect their on-screen state directly, so a visible tab starts showing its feed right away, whether it's a standalone tile or inside a tab group.
- **Bit and the Vitals meters now stay in sync across every screen.** When the dashboard was open in more than one place at once — the Xeneon Edge screen, a desktop browser, the native app, an embedded view — refilling a meter on one could quietly get undone, so the bars (and Bit's mood) drifted out of step between screens and sometimes snapped back to an older level. The cause was two screens saving at the same instant and overwriting each other; saves are now applied one at a time, so a refill (or any change) done on any screen always sticks and every screen shows the same thing.
- **The weather widget no longer blanks to "no data" after you change the interface language (#88).** Switching language made the widget refetch the forecast from scratch in the new language, and if the weather providers were momentarily busy at that instant (which happens when you flip through several languages quickly) the tile went empty for a few minutes until they recovered. It now falls back to the last forecast it already had for that place — shown as slightly stale rather than blank — while it fetches the translated version in the background, so the widget stays populated and no extra requests are made to the weather services.
- **On the Xeneon Edge app, the mouse pointer no longer flickers over text (#89).** In the native app the cursor flipped to a text "I-beam" and a text caret as it moved across the dashboard's many labels and fields, which read as constant flicker. The pointer now rests as a steady arrow over text and inputs and stops morphing there — while still turning into the usual pointing hand over buttons and clickable things, so you can always tell what you can tap. Only the native Xeneon Edge app is affected; the dashboard in a normal desktop browser keeps its usual cursors.
- **The System widget can now monitor A: and B: drives.** The disk-space list only ever scanned drive letters from C onward, so anyone who had mapped a volume to A: or B: (for example a drive labelled `B:\`) never saw it in the "drives to monitor" picker. The scan now starts at A, so every mounted drive shows up.
- **The Xenon chat's "Attach file" and "Capture screen" buttons are now translated.** Their tooltips were hard-coded in Italian and stayed Italian in every other language; they now follow your selected interface language like the rest of the chat.
- **The Playback tile no longer stays stuck on "Nothing playing" when music is actually playing.** On some PCs Windows' media service occasionally goes blind after the machine has been sitting idle, and Xenon has a safeguard that notices this and quietly switches to a backup reader so playback still shows up. That safeguard used to stop watching after the first few idle minutes, so if you only started playing something a while after opening the dashboard it could sit empty until you reloaded. It now keeps watching — backing off so an idle PC stays light — and picks the track up within a minute or so once it starts.
- **The calendar's highlighted day now moves to the new day on its own at midnight.** If you left the dashboard open overnight, the "today" marker stayed on the previous day until you tapped a date by hand — which also left the old day and the new one highlighted at the same time. It now advances automatically as the clock passes midnight, with no tap needed.
- **Skipping or seeking in the Spotify player no longer leaves the previous song's time on the bar.** Pressing next/previous (or dragging the seek bar) asked Spotify for the new state immediately — but Spotify takes a moment to register the change, so it answered with the *old* song's position, which then stuck on screen. The player now flips the bar to the start instantly when you skip, quietly re-checks until Spotify confirms the new track (bypassing the snapshot cache), and holds your chosen position after a seek instead of snapping back. Skips made from the Media tile's own controls resync just as fast.
- **The Spotify player no longer disconnects itself under heavy use, and the progress bar reads correctly.** Three related fixes: (1) When Spotify briefly rate-limited us (too many requests in a short window), a token refresh in that moment wiped the stored login and the whole player vanished as if you'd never connected — it now keeps your login through a rate-limit or network blip and simply retries, disconnecting only on a genuine sign-out. (2) The now-playing hero and seek bar no longer blink away on a passing hiccup; a transient error keeps the last known track on screen instead of emptying it. (3) The progress bar no longer shows a brand-new song as `4:05 / 4:05` with the bar full: at every track change Spotify momentarily reports the fresh track already at its end, and on some setups it stays stuck there — the player now recognises that a playing track can't sit at its finish line, starts the bar from the beginning and fills it in real time. We also eased how often the player is polled so heavy listening sessions are far less likely to trip Spotify's rate limit in the first place.
- **The Volume section now explains itself when it can't read your audio.** On a few PCs the System tile's Volume tab came up empty, showing no device names or levels — and never said why. The volume, mute and per-app mixer are all read through a small bundled helper (SoundVolumeView), which some antivirus programs quietly quarantine as "riskware"; when that happens the section had no data and simply sat blank. It now shows a clear "Audio unavailable" notice explaining the likely cause and how to fix it (check your antivirus quarantine or exclude the app folder), and it fills back in on its own the moment the audio can be read again.
- **The website's Hall of supporters now ranks monthly members by everything they've given, not a single month.** A recurring supporter (Buy Me a Coffee membership or GitHub Sponsor) used to be placed on the wall as if they'd only given one month's amount, so someone quietly giving €5 a month for most of a year sat below a single €50 one-off. Their standing now reflects the whole run of their support — roughly their monthly amount times the months they've been a member — so long-time members climb to where they belong. Yearly plans are counted per year, and nothing changes for one-time donations or how names are privacy-masked.

## [v4.5.0] - 12-07-2026
### 🎨 Make each widget your own — pictures, frames and overlays
- **Every widget can now have its own background — a picture, a colour gradient, or both.** Drop an image behind any tile — a landscape, artwork, a texture — with cover / contain / tile fitting plus dim, blur and opacity, or blend two colours into a gradient (on its own or as a tint over the image) so your dashboard content stays readable on top.
- **The panel itself can be a gradient too.** Under Colours, the panel background can now be a two-colour gradient instead of a flat fill — for a tile that fades from your accent into the dark, no background image needed.
- **Decorate a tile with overlay images — even animated ones — and place them exactly.** Add up to four decorations per widget (a dragon curling around a corner, a sakura branch, your team logo…) and **drag each one anywhere on the tile** — not just into a corner — then set its size, rotation, flip and opacity. PNG, WebP and JPEG are supported, and animated GIFs keep moving.
- **Ornamental frames around any tile.** Pick a ready-made frame — Sengoku, Sakura, Neon, Gold or Minimal — or upload your own frame image, and choose how thick it sits.
- **You can see your widget style as you set it.** The per-tile 🎨 editor is now a side panel over a live, un-blurred dashboard, so every colour, background and decoration you pick applies to the real widget in front of you as you adjust it — no more editing blind behind a frosted overlay. **Drag the panel by its header** to move it off the widget you're styling.
- **Everything is customisable two ways.** Tweak it by hand from the dashboard's edit mode — the 🎨 button on each tile now opens a tabbed editor (Colours · Background · Decor) — or receive a fully-styled look inside a shared page or package code. Shared codes bundle your uploaded images inline, so a themed layout arrives complete on someone else's screen, with nothing to download.
- **The Deck gets its own appearance studio.** A new **Customize** button opens a dedicated dialog with a **live preview of your Deck and its music bar**, so theme, key shape, faceplate, the background behind the keys (image *or* gradient) and the now-playing / volume strip styling (backdrop image, gradient and accent colour) all update in front of you as you pick them — no more editing a music colour you couldn't see. Your keys keep their artwork, gradients and animated icons, and the whole look now **travels with a shared Deck profile**, so importing a profile brings its background and music styling too — and a look that arrived from someone else's code stays with that deck: your own exports never re-share it, the same only-your-creations rule as everywhere else.
- **Fixed: a decorated widget no longer jumps while you're editing.** A tile carrying decor could squash its own contents the moment you entered the layout editor (its edit buttons were being pulled into the widget's own layout), snapping back only when you left edit mode. Decorated tiles now stay put while you arrange them.
- **Fixed: picking an image that can't be processed no longer leaves the picker stuck.** In rare cases (a corrupted or blocked picture) the Deck-key and decoration image pickers could silently wait forever; they now fall back to the original image — or tell you it failed — instead. All image pickers (widget backgrounds, frames, overlays, Deck keys and Deck backgrounds) now share one resize engine, so they behave the same way everywhere.

### 🔄 Every screen finally shows the same dashboard (#72)
- **Weather now updates on every screen the moment you change it — on any of them.** Changing the weather city, mode or provider in the browser updated that browser only: the Xeneon Edge (and any other open dashboard) kept showing the previous location's forecast until its next scheduled poll — up to 30 minutes — which is also why the two screens could show two different temperatures at the same time. Every surface now refetches the weather as soon as a change made elsewhere reaches it, and a new refresh interval takes effect everywhere immediately.
- **Notes now stay in sync across screens, live.** The notes widget used to load once at startup and never refresh, so a note typed on the Xeneon Edge simply didn't exist in a browser opened earlier (and vice versa) until a manual reload. Now every save — including the AI's — appears on all open dashboards within a moment, without ever disturbing the note you're typing in.
- **Old snapshots can no longer overwrite your notes.** Saves now carry a revision number, so a dashboard that was closed while holding an outdated copy of your notes (its live connection had dropped) can't silently replace newer content on its way out — the server refuses the stale write and hands the page the current notes instead. And when a screen that fell behind saves an edit, it now merges the newer notes back in first, so a note created on one screen can never be wiped by a keystroke made on another.
- **The ticker now scrolls even with Windows' "Animation effects" turned off.** If you keep Windows' animations disabled (Settings → Accessibility → Visual effects), the news/stocks/football ticker rendered but never moved — on the browser and the Xeneon Edge alike — because it was honouring that system-wide setting. The ticker is something you explicitly turn on, and scrolling is its whole job, so it now keeps moving regardless; it still pauses on hover and freezes in game/performance mode as before.
- **Hiding the Browser tile's toolbar now applies on every screen.** Using "Hide toolbar" in a Browser tile hid it in that browser only — the Xeneon Edge (or any other open dashboard) kept its toolbar showing, because a tile already on screen only read that setting when it first appeared. The toolbar's hidden/shown state now follows across all screens the moment you change it on any of them, just like the weather and notes above.
- **Browser favorites now appear on every screen right away.** Adding or removing a favorite in a Browser tile saved it everywhere, but a tile already open on another screen only rebuilt its favorites bar when it was reopened, so the new shortcut didn't show on the Xeneon Edge until then. The favorites bar now refreshes on every open Browser tile as soon as the change reaches it — same fix family as the toolbar above.
- **A Browser tile's address now shows on every screen, not just the one you typed it on.** A Browser tile that was already open on a second screen could sit blank — no address, no page — while the same tile showed the page correctly on the screen where you set the address (and a reload of the app didn't help). A Browser tab only read its address when it first appeared, so a screen that was already open never picked up an address set elsewhere. Now an open, still-empty Browser tab adopts an address entered on another screen as soon as it syncs and loads the page live — while a tab you're already browsing is never yanked to a different page.
- **A widget you add on one screen now shows up on the others without a refresh.** Adding a widget (Tasks, Timer, Notes, or any other) to a page on one screen saved it everywhere, but a screen already open only nudged its existing tiles around and never actually built the new one, so it stayed invisible on the Xeneon Edge until you reloaded that page. Adding, removing, moving between pages, or grouping a widget on any screen now rebuilds the other screens' pages live — keeping the page you're on — so the change appears at once.
- **Custom (SDK) widgets added elsewhere no longer show "This widget package was removed."** When you installed and placed a community/custom widget on one screen, another open screen knew a widget belonged there but hadn't refreshed its list of installed packages, so it showed the "package was removed" placeholder until you pressed Rescan. Every screen now refreshes its installed-widget list the moment a custom widget is installed or assigned elsewhere, so the real widget appears on its own.

### 🖥️ Preview the dashboard at Xeneon Edge size, right in your browser
- **A new browser-only "Xeneon Edge preview" shows the dashboard exactly as it appears on the device.** Arranging your layout from a desktop browser was awkward because a normal window is a completely different shape from the Edge's wide 2560×720 panel, so tiles never lined up with what you actually saw on the Edge. Turn on Settings → General → "Show it as on the Xeneon Edge" (or add `?edge` to the address) and the dashboard renders at the Edge's real proportions, scaled to fit your window with a tidy letterbox — so you can compose the layout and have it match the device. It's per-browser and doesn't affect the Edge itself.

### 🧹 A proper "remove everything" uninstaller
- **UNINSTALL.bat now offers a genuine clean slate.** The old uninstaller stopped the server and removed the startup task but deliberately left your data, the native app, and everything installed alongside it behind. The new one removes it all: the native kiosk app and its autostart/registry entries, the bundled PresentMon, Xenon Helper, Whisper, adblock and npm dependencies, leftover temp files, the Windows edge-swipe policy, and — after a clear confirmation — your `server\data` and the install folder itself. Shared system apps (Node, FFmpeg, LibreHardwareMonitor, Sunshine, Tailscale, the display driver) are asked about one at a time so nothing another program relies on is removed by surprise. Run it with `-DryRun` to preview exactly what would go without changing anything, or `-KeepData` to keep your settings and notes. It elevates itself so a complete removal works in one click.

### 🖥️ Native app — steps aside for Windows Remote Desktop
- **The kiosk can now hide itself while you're connected via Windows Remote Desktop.** If you remote into your PC with Windows' own Remote Desktop, the full-screen Xenon window used to cover the desktop you came in to use. Turn on Settings → General → "Hide during Remote Desktop" (opt-in, native app only) and Xenon hides the moment a Remote Desktop session begins and reappears the instant you're back at the PC. It only reacts to a genuine Remote Desktop login — Xenon's own remote control (Sunshine/Moonlight) streams the screen you're sitting at, so it's never affected. Requires the native app update that ships this change.
- **The Windows taskbar no longer appears over the dashboard when you turn a monitor off.** If you powered down another display, Windows would move its taskbar onto the Xeneon Edge and draw it on top of Xenon. The kiosk now notices the display change and re-asserts its full-screen placement, so it stays cleanly over the taskbar. Requires the native app update that ships this change.

### 🎵 Media panel — recovers on its own when the native helper can't read media (#80)
- **The Media panel no longer stays blank on machines where the native helper can't see your media sessions.** On some setups the optional native helper answers but reports nothing playing even while music is — leaving the panel empty with no error. This is now fixed on two fronts. The helper itself recovers: when Windows' media service gets into a state where it stops listing sessions (which can happen after signing in, locking, or resuming from sleep), the helper now re-acquires a fresh connection on its own instead of staying blind until the app restarts. And as a safety net, Xenon still notices when the helper keeps coming back empty, double-checks against the built-in PowerShell reader — now even for paused tracks, not only actively-playing ones — and switches over automatically if that reader can see your media. Nothing to configure; if the helper starts working again it's picked back up on its own, and machines where it works normally are unaffected and pay no extra cost.

### 📹 Cameras — arrange your feeds exactly how you want
- **The Cameras widget now lets you choose how your feeds are laid out, instead of stretching them into one long row.** Before, four cameras were forced side by side in a single row that got thinner the wider the tile was, with no way to change it. Settings → Cameras now has a Layout section: pick the number of columns (Auto, or 1–4 — so four cameras can sit in a neat 2×2 square), choose whether each frame fills its box or fits inside it without cropping, and set the shape (16:9, 4:3 or 1:1). You can also reorder your cameras with up/down arrows so they appear in the order you care about. Everything updates live and is remembered across restarts; leaving it on Auto keeps the previous behaviour.
- **You can now straighten a camera that's mounted sideways or upside down.** Tap any camera to enlarge it and you'll find rotate and mirror buttons — the view turns in 90° steps and can be flipped horizontally, per camera, so a ceiling-mounted or rotated camera finally looks right. It rotates what you see on the dashboard; it doesn't move the camera itself.
- **Zoom in on the part of a camera you actually care about.** The enlarged view now also has zoom in/out buttons, and while zoomed you can drag the image to frame it — so you can crop to a doorway, a desk, or a driveway instead of the whole wide-angle shot. The enlarged view shows the exact crop the tile will use, and it's saved per camera and remembered across restarts. It's a digital zoom on the snapshot the dashboard already receives, so it never touches or commands the camera; leaving it at 1× keeps the full frame as before.
- **You can also choose how often the snapshots refresh.** The same Layout section lets you set the update rate (1.5s, 3s, 5s or 10s) — handy for easing the load on a busy console or a slower network. It stays at the previous 1.5s unless you change it.
- **Get a heads-up when a camera sees something.** Turn on Notifications in Settings → Cameras and Xenon surfaces your UniFi Protect smart detections — person, vehicle, package, animal, plus plain motion and doorbell rings — as a dashboard toast, and briefly badges the camera that spotted it. Pick exactly which kinds you care about and set a minimum gap between alerts so one person lingering doesn't spam the screen.
