It's off by default and opt-in per kind; the live connection only runs while a dashboard is open with notifications turned on, and the pop-ups still respect your global Notifications switch. Needs a camera that does smart detections, and a Protect account with permission to read events.

## [v4.4.0] - 10-07-2026
### 🧬 Vitals — meters finally pause while you're away
- **Your self-care bars no longer drain while you're not at the PC.** After 5 minutes without any mouse or keyboard input the meters freeze exactly where they are and resume the moment you're back — vitals now measure time actually spent at the computer, not wall-clock time. No reminder toasts fire while you're away either. Works across both screens at once (browser and the Xeneon Edge kiosk credit the pause exactly once, never twice), turns itself off gracefully if presence can't be detected, and can be disabled under Settings → Vitals ("Pause while you're away") if you prefer the old behavior.
- **Honest numbers**: the refill button and the floating reward now say **+25** — what a refill has always actually granted (4 refills = 1 level). No XP or level was changed.

### 🤖 Bit — smarter, everywhere, and finally polite at night
- **Bit now knows when you're around.** While you're away he sleeps (so do your meters), and when you come back he greets you — with the meters exactly where you left them, because he froze them for you. At night (23:00–07:00) he sleeps too: no roasts, popups or PC actions until morning (Settings → Bit → "Sleeps at night", on by default).
- **Bit remembers.** He tracks your daily self-care streak (days in a row with at least one refill), celebrates when it grows, shows it in his menu (🔥), and keeps lifetime records — including how many times he had to lock your PC.
- **AI-generated roasts (opt-in).** Turn on "AI-generated roasts" and Bit asks your configured Xenon AI provider (Gemini, OpenAI, Anthropic or local Ollama) for a one-liner written for the exact moment — what died, for how long, your streak, whether you're gaming, what's playing. If the AI doesn't answer within a few seconds, he seamlessly falls back to his built-in lines; the escalation ladder never waits on it, and nothing is sent anywhere unless you opted in.
- **Bit can live in the top bar.** A new "Where Bit lives" setting puts a mini animated Bit next to the clock (in both the full and minimal top bar) — live mood colors, blink and all; tap him for his menu. Choose floating corner, top bar, or both.
- **Bit has his own Settings section now.** All of Bit's controls (and the Vitals bars he watches over) moved out of Notifications into a dedicated **Bit** category in the Settings sidebar — with his own pixel face as the icon, so it's impossible to miss.
- **Bit now speaks Dutch.** The full phrase bank — roasts included — was translated, so Dutch users no longer get English lines.
- **Truce and escalation now survive reloads.** "Truce 30 min" / "Quiet for today" hold on every screen (not just the one where you tapped them), and reloading the dashboard mid-episode no longer replays GAME OVER or re-attempts minimize/lock — Bit keeps his bookkeeping.
- **Fixes**: an open GAME OVER card no longer covers Settings or the app switcher; Bit's blink no longer burns frames while the dashboard is idle or when reduced motion is on; disabling Bit now releases his audio engine.

### 🌙 Ambient / Screensaver — wakes up when you do, and remembers your timer
- **The screensaver now understands the whole PC, not just the dashboard.** It used to start whenever the dashboard window itself went untouched — so it kicked in while you were working on another monitor. Now it watches system-wide activity (any keyboard or mouse input, on any screen): it only starts when the whole PC has genuinely been idle for your chosen time, and it clears the moment you do anything anywhere. On the rare machine where system-idle can't be read, it falls back to the old dashboard-only behavior.
- **The screensaver dismisses itself the moment you touch anything.** When Ambient starts on its own after your idle time, moving the mouse, pressing a key or tapping the screen makes it disappear instantly — that first gesture only wakes the dashboard, it doesn't accidentally press a widget underneath. (Ambient scenes you open deliberately from the top-bar button still stay up until you close them, so you can interact with their widgets.)
- **Waking up is fast and reliable now.** While you're away the PC checks for your return every few seconds (instead of every 15), so mouse or keyboard on *any* monitor drops the screensaver within moments. Community ambient scenes now react to mouse and touch exactly like the built-in one, a screensaver you just dismissed can no longer pop straight back up off a stale idle reading, and auto-start keeps working across connection hiccups or if the idle probe ever breaks.
- **Fixes**: the "Start after inactivity" time you pick now shows correctly after a page refresh — the value was always saved, but the dropdown label was snapping back to "Never" and looked like it hadn't stuck.

### ⌨️ Deck — Smart Profiles: the deck follows the app you're using
- **The Deck can now switch profile on its own when you change app.** Open the profile menu in edit mode, tap **⚡ Profili smart**, and pair apps with profiles — `obs64` → "Streaming", `code` → "Work" — with a suggestion list of your open windows. Alt-tab to OBS and the deck shows your streaming keys; leave it and the deck returns to your usual profile (or stays, if you prefer). The switch is purely visual — your saved configuration and manually chosen profile are never touched — and picking a profile by hand always wins. This is the marquee feature of Elgato's Stream Deck software, now on your Xeneon Edge.

### ⌨️ Deck — keys that show live state, values, and change face
- **Far more keys now light up with the real state of what they control.** Besides mic/OBS, keys now follow **Discord mute and deafen**, **media/Spotify playback**, **Home Assistant devices** (a light key glows while the light is on — the deck watches only the entities your keys use) and **running timers**. Most bindings are automatic: give a key a Discord mute action and it simply starts reflecting your live mute state.
- **A key can change its whole face while active.** New "Look while active" fields (FX tab) set an alternate emoji, label and colour shown while the key's state is on — a record key that turns into 🔴 REC, a light key that goes warm yellow.
- **Live values ON the key.** A key face can now display a ticking **timer countdown** (mm:ss, updating only while a timer actually runs) or a live value published by a community widget — pick it under "Live value on the key" in the editor.

### ⌨️ Deck — timers, type-text, and a real soundboard
- **Timer keys**: start (or restart) a named countdown, pause/resume it, or cancel it — the same timers the Timers tile shows, and the key can display the live countdown.
- **Type text**: a key that types a snippet into the app you were using — any characters, emoji included, multi-line too. Perfect for a "brb" message, a canned reply, your email address.
- **Soundboard, properly.** Upload clips right from the key editor into a personal sound library (no more hunting for file paths), pick them from a dropdown, set a per-clip volume, and add a **Stop all sounds** panic key.

### 🎚️ Deck — touch faders: sliders on your keys
- **A key can now be a slider.** Choose "Slider (touch fader)" as the key type and drag with your finger to set **system volume, an app's volume, Spotify volume, an OBS input, Discord mic/output — or a Home Assistant light's brightness**. The fader tracks the real value while idle (change the volume elsewhere and it moves), updates live as you drag, and never fights the page-swipe gesture. Something physical Stream Deck keys simply can't do — this is the touchscreen earning its keep.

### 🖥️ Virtual Deck — your deck as a window on the main PC
- **Open any deck as its own always-on-top window on your main monitor.** Tap **🖥 Apri sul PC** in the deck's profile menu and a compact window appears with the same keys, live states, sliders and countdowns — press keys from your main screen while the Xeneon Edge shows something else. It remembers its size and position, stays above your windows, and closes with the server. View-and-press only: editing stays on the dashboard.

### 🧩 Widget SDK — creators can now build real Deck actions (and much more)
- **Community widgets can contribute keys answered by their own code.** A package can declare up to 8 **handler actions**: they appear in the Deck editor like native actions, with a real config form generated from the params the creator declared (text/dropdown/number — no JSON editing), and pressing the key hands the call to the widget's sandboxed code, which acks back so the key can honestly report success or failure. Each handler is granted individually in the permission dialog, every call is re-validated and rate-limited server-side, and the sandbox is unchanged — widget code still has no network beyond its approved proxy hosts.
- **Widgets can run in the background.** A package with handler actions may ask to run headless (shown clearly in its permission dialog), so its Deck keys answer even when no tile is on screen — capped, sandboxed, and torn down the moment you revoke it.
- **Richer key faces from widgets**: a published state can now carry a short label, an emoji and a colour, and a bound key displays them live — a viewers counter, a "LIVE" badge, a price ticker on a key.
- **Deck codes can carry their widgets.** Sharing a deck profile whose keys use community widgets now offers to embed those packages in the code — the receiver sees exactly which widgets ride along, reviews them like any install, and the keys work out of the box.

### 🔒 Sharing — only YOUR creations can leave your PC
- **You can no longer re-share what someone else made.** Xenon now remembers where everything came from: widgets, Ambient scenes, themes, animated backgrounds, dashboard pages and Deck profiles that arrive via a share code, a package or the community gallery are marked as imported — and every export path refuses to redistribute them. They show up greyed out with an "imported — not shareable" hint in the package dialog and pickers, the export buttons explain why, and for widgets the server itself refuses the export, so it can't be worked around from the page. Your own work — Widget Creator builds, AI-made widgets, and everything you design in the app — stays fully shareable, even after you update your own published widget from the catalog.
- **Fail-closed by default.** A widget whose origin Xenon can't verify (installed before this update, or a folder dropped straight into the widgets directory) is treated as *not yours* until you say otherwise — so nothing leaks by accident. If you genuinely built one by hand, an "I made this" button in the installed-widgets list claims it as your own and re-enables sharing.
- **The installed-widgets list now shows provenance.** Your own packages carry a "Made by you" badge, community installs a "From the community" one, and the Export button now exports *that* package directly (it used to open a generic picker) — and only appears on your own.
- **Fix**: a background that rides inside a shared *theme* is now marked imported too. Installing someone's theme lets you enjoy its animated backdrop but no longer lets you re-share that backdrop as your own — previously only a stand-alone background carried this protection, so a theme was a way around it.

### 📦 "Create a package" — now it really packs everything, and tells you what
- **A package can now carry your whole setup**: theme (custom font included, like a single theme export), pages, **Deck profiles**, your **animated background**, widgets and **Ambient scenes** (finally their own group instead of hiding among widgets). On import, Deck profiles land on your first Deck — or in the Deck presets library if none is on the dashboard — and everything still goes through the same per-part validation and permission review.
- **The dialog finally tells you what you're exporting.** Items are grouped by type with icons and details (page widget counts, Deck key counts, widget permissions), a live summary line spells out exactly what the code will contain ("1 Theme · 2 Pages · 1 Deck profile · 3 widgets"), and imported items are visible but disabled, with a note explaining why.
- **The import review grew to match**: a package now lists its Deck profiles and background too, and shows every action type those Deck keys contain — the same transparency a single Deck import always had.
- **Fix**: widgets and Ambient scenes installed from a package (or a single widget/scene code) now appear in the widget picker and Ambient list **immediately** — no more reloading the whole dashboard before you can add them to a tile.

### 🎛️ Settings — "Widget e condivisione" rebuilt around create → share → discover
- **A new "Create" card opens the page** and gives creators an honest map: the no-code Widget Creator (fast, live preview, but limited to templates) next to the code route (full control via the widget SDK), with the numbered procedure, a link to the SDK guide and a link to the catalog publishing guidelines. A closing hint reminds you where everything else is created (themes in Appearance, pages in the layout editor, profiles on the Deck, scenes in Ambient mode).
- **The stale "zip your widget folder" instructions are gone** — sharing is export codes and the catalog now, and the page says so. All of it in every one of the 11 languages.
- **Publishing lands on the right catalog shelf.** "✨ Publish to the catalog" now pre-selects the correct kind in the GitHub form based on what you exported (theme, background, page, Deck profile, widget, scene or package), so submissions arrive pre-filed under the right filter.

### ✨ Discover — search, filters, updates and one-tap publishing
- **The community gallery grows up.** Search by name, author or #tag; filter by kind and category; entries show their version, tags, up to six screenshots or GIFs (swipe through them) and the publisher's GitHub handle. Screenshots can be WebP (animated allowed) or plain PNG, so a raw screen grab works with no conversion. Nothing changed about safety: installing still goes through the same review dialogs as a pasted code.
- **Widget updates, in-app.** When the catalog lists a newer version of a widget you have installed, an **Updates** section appears in the gallery, an "Aggiorna" button shows next to the package in Settings, and once a day Xenon quietly checks and mentions available updates in a toast. Updating re-installs through the normal validation — and if an update asks for new permissions, you're asked again before it gets them. (Updates now always fetch the freshest published code, so a newly released version never reinstalls the old one.)
- **A starter set to explore from day one.** The gallery now ships with the **Nocturne** pack: a calm sage-on-charcoal theme with its own slow-drifting backdrop, a matching now-playing widget, a fullscreen ambient clock, an eight-key Deck profile (media, mic, volume, a focus timer and a touch fader) and a tidy dashboard page — install any piece on its own, or the whole look in one tap.
- **Publish your creation in two taps.** Every share dialog now has **✨ Pubblica nel catalogo**: it copies your code and opens a prefilled GitHub submission form (name, kind, description, screenshot). The maintainer reviews and merges — that's moderation, not a gate: it keeps the catalog trustworthy for everyone.
- **Manage installed widgets in one place.** Settings → Widget e condivisione now lists every installed package with its version, author and granted permissions, with per-package Update / Export / Remove.

### ✦ Xenon AI — it can now build all of this for you
- **"Xenon, make me a widget that…" now literally works.** The AI can write and install a complete community widget from scratch (sandboxed like every widget — you still approve its permissions before it can see or do anything), compose Deck profiles with the FULL action catalog — typed actions, gestures, live states, sliders, Smart-Profiles rules — search the community catalog and start an install for you (the normal review dialog always opens; nothing applies silently), and open the Virtual Deck window on request.

### 🖼️ Animated backgrounds can now carry real images — pixel-art welcome
- **Your animated background (code) can now include actual pictures, not just shapes drawn by math.** A new **Images** row under **Settings → Aspetto → Sfondo animato** lets you attach up to 6 PNG/JPEG/WebP/GIF files (~300 KB each); your `draw()` code receives them as a fifth parameter and paints them with `ctx.drawImage(assets.name, x, y)` — perfect for pixel-art cities, sprites and textures that would be painful to draw by hand in code. Thumbnails of the attached images show right in the editor, with one-tap removal.
- **The images travel inside the shared code.** Export the background and the pictures are embedded in the code/file itself — the person importing sees "N images · size" plus the live preview before applying, and the result works forever: no image-hosting links that die, no requests to anyone's server. The sandbox is unchanged — a background still can't touch the network, your files or your settings, images included. Large backgrounds share as a file (with a "share without images" fallback for a lighter link). Fully localised across all 11 languages.
- **More room to draw, and a counter so you see the ceiling coming.** The code editor's character limit was raised from 20,000 to 60,000 — enough for an elaborate hand-drawn scene — and a live counter now sits by the editor: muted, then amber as you approach the cap, then red with an explicit note if you go past it (code beyond the limit isn't saved). Before, hitting the limit silently truncated your code; now it never surprises you, and the note points you to the new Images option for the heavy visual detail.

### 🌙 Ambient mode — the Focus screen becomes a real screensaver, and anyone can design one
- **The Focus lock screen has grown into Ambient mode.** The topbar button (now "Ambient") still opens the familiar fullscreen view — big clock, weather, now playing, upcoming events, with the same per-widget toggles — but it's now a proper screensaver too: in **Settings → Ambient / Screensaver** you can have it start on its own after 1–30 minutes without touching the screen (off by default). It politely stays away while you're actually doing something — a game running, the layout editor open, a voice chat with Xenon, any dialog on screen — and any touch or key dismisses it. The whole mode can be switched off entirely if you never want it.
- **Ambient scenes: creators can design the screensaver, and share it like a theme.** A scene is a community creation — a fullscreen animated view with its own design, typography and motion — that you pick in Settings → Ambient instead of the classic widget layout. Scenes are built with the same community widget toolkit (and the same safety: they run isolated in a sandbox with no network and no access to your files, and they only see the data feeds you approve — a new **Weather** feed joins media, system and the rest). They travel exactly like every other Xenon creation: **Export Ambient scene** produces a code or file, importing shows what the scene can see before anything installs, access-code protection works on them, and a package can carry a scene alongside a theme and pages. If a scene you selected is ever removed, the classic view steps back in automatically.

### ✨ Discover — a community gallery, inside the app and on the website
- **A new "Discover" gallery lists themes, backgrounds, widgets, Ambient scenes and packages shared by the community.** Open it from **Settings → Widget e condivisione → Scopri** (or from the Ambient scene picker to browse scenes only): cards show the kind, the author, colour previews for themes and a live animated preview for backgrounds. One tap on Import hands the code to the normal import flow — the same preview and permission steps as pasting a code by hand, never an instant apply. The catalog is moderated (entries are published by the maintainer), fetched over HTTPS with a light cache, and if you're offline the last saved copy is shown.
- **The website gets a dedicated catalog page.** The project site now has its own **catalog page** — reached from a prominent card on the home — that renders the identical catalog with the same search and kind/category filters as the in-app gallery, up to six screenshots or animated previews per creation in a tap-to-zoom viewer, and a copy-the-code button per entry. Creations can be browsed and shared from any browser, and every entry keeps its own link you can post. Want yours listed? A **✨ Submit yours** button and `docs/community/README.md` explain how (the prefilled GitHub form, a pull request, or the Discord).

### ✦ Limited edition — exclusive drops with a real copy count
- **The gallery can now feature limited-edition drops — a fixed number of copies, worldwide.** A limited drop shows how many copies are left (for example "3 of 5 left"), and once they're gone it reads a single clear **Sold out** badge in red. Unlike everything else in the gallery, a limited drop isn't imported directly: it's **reserved on Discord**. Tap **Reserve on Discord** and you're taken to the community server, where each buyer receives their own personal access code to unlock and install the pack.
- **Reachable from both the app and the website.** In the dashboard a dedicated **Limited edition** card under **Settings → Widget e condivisione** opens the drops on their own; they also appear in a pinned "Limited edition" section at the top of the Discover gallery. On the project site the catalog page gains a **Limited** filter, and the home page points to it. Copy counts and the Discord link are curated by the maintainer — the reserve button only ever opens Discord, and installing still goes through the normal locked-import flow with your access code.
- **The first drop — NØVA // NEON DISTRICT — is live and already sold out.** A cyberpunk edition of five: a neon duotone theme, the animated Megacity Drift background, the Orbitron display font, three bespoke widgets, an Ambient scene and a Deck profile — shown off with a swipeable screenshot gallery.

### 📸 Share card — post your setup with a scannable QR
- **Every export dialog gains a "Create share card" button.** It composes a polished 1200×675 PNG — your theme colours, the creation's name, the Xenon wordmark and a **QR code** — ready to post on Reddit or Discord. The QR points to the public gallery page for published entries, or carries small codes directly to a tiny landing page on the project site that shows the code with a copy button and the three import steps (it never points at your PC — codes too large for a QR simply travel as the attached file, and the card says so). Optionally the card can use a **real screenshot** of your screen as its dimmed backdrop; without ffmpeg it just stays with the clean swatch design.

### 🎁 Supporter perks — a thank-you that's actually nice to receive
- **The "Sostieni Xenon" page now explains supporter perks.** Exclusive packs — themes, backgrounds, Ambient scenes — are published as members-only posts on Buy Me a Coffee, protected with the personal access codes introduced in v4.2.0: each supporter gets their own code, and only a valid code can decrypt and install the pack. A dedicated button opens the import dialog directly for those who already have one, and gallery entries reserved to supporters show a 🔒 badge linking to Buy Me a Coffee. Creators who support the project get a ⭐ badge next to their name in the gallery.

### 🧩 For widget authors
- **New `weather` data stream** in the Widget SDK — current conditions, forecast fields, sunrise/sunset — available to widgets and Ambient scenes after the user grants it (docs/WIDGET_SDK.md is updated).
- **New `surface: "ambient"` manifest field** turns a package into a fullscreen Ambient scene; everything else about the package format is unchanged.

### ✨ Pasting background code into Import now points you to the right box
- **If you paste animated-background code into the "Import" dialog, Xenon now tells you where it actually goes instead of just refusing it.** The Import box only accepts a shared preset code, link or `.json` file (the kind of thing "Export background" produces), so pasting a hand-written `draw()` snippet there always failed with a bare "Not a valid preset code" — with no hint that the code itself was fine and simply in the wrong place. Now when what you paste looks like animated-background source, the message points you to the **"Code"** editor under **Settings → Aspetto → Sfondo animato**, which is the field that actually runs your code. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 🫥 Minimal topbar — the side rails now get out of the way on their own
- **In the minimal topbar style, the two edge rails now auto-hide after 10 seconds without a touch, so nothing sits over your dashboard while you're just watching it.** They tuck away against the screen edge, leaving just a slim handle peeking so there's always a visible arrow to bring them back — one tap on that handle (or anywhere along the screen edge) slides them out again, ready to use. The countdown restarts whenever you touch a rail, so they stay put while you're actually using them. If you'd rather keep them always on screen, there's a new switch in **Settings → Aspetto → Barra superiore → "Nascondi le barre laterali automaticamente"** to turn the behaviour off. It's on by default and applies only to the minimal style (the full glass bar is unaffected). Your per-rail open/closed choice is untouched — auto-hide is purely visual and reveals each rail exactly as you left it.

### 🌍 Your language now truly sticks — on every screen (#72)
- **Fixed the chosen UI language not being saved when it matched your browser's own language.** If your PC was already in, say, Dutch, picking Dutch in Settings looked like it worked — but the choice was never actually stored, so the Xeneon Edge screen and the desktop browser could each settle on a different language, and the server kept answering in its own default. The pick is now always persisted and reaches every surface immediately.

### 🌦️ Weather — same forecast on every screen, in your language (#72)
- **The browser and the Xeneon Edge could show two different forecasts for the same PC.** Xenon finds your position via your internet connection; that answer is now remembered on disk, so a slow or failed lookup right after startup no longer sends one screen to a coordinate-based forecast and the other to a rough IP-guessed one. If the lookup fails, the last known position is reused instead of guessing.
- **Weather conditions no longer show up in Italian (or English) on a translated dashboard.** Condition texts ("Partly cloudy", "Rain"…) are now translated in all 11 UI languages, and an unrecognised language falls back to English instead of Italian.
- **Weather answers are now cached per language and place** instead of in a single shared slot, so two screens (or Xenon AI) asking in different languages no longer wipe each other's copy and re-download the forecast over and over.

### 📰 Ticker — keeps scrolling on the Xeneon Edge (#72)
- **The stock/news ticker froze after a minute on the Xeneon Edge.** The energy saver that pauses decorative animations when you haven't touched the screen for 60 seconds was also stopping the ticker — and the Edge is exactly the screen you look at without touching. The ticker is live information, so it now keeps scrolling; it still pauses in game mode, performance mode and under dialogs.

### 🏠 Smart Home — the tile now connects reliably after "Connect"
- **Fixed a Smart Home tile that could stay stuck on "Connect Home Assistant in Settings" even after a successful connection.** You'd enter your Home Assistant address and access token, see the green "Connected · N devices", pick the devices to show — and the tile on the dashboard would keep showing the setup prompt as if nothing had been configured. The cause was a save timing issue: the "Connect" button verified your token by talking to Home Assistant directly, but the token was only written to disk by a separate, delayed background save that could be lost (for example on a machine running both the native app and a browser tab at once), so the tile — which reads the *saved* token — still saw nothing. Now a green "Connected" always means the token was saved, right there and then, and the tile switches to your devices immediately. Choosing or changing which devices to show is also reflected on the tile at once, instead of waiting for the next change in your home. If your address uses `homeassistant.local` and the tile later shows "Home Assistant unreachable", try your console's direct IP (for example `http://192.168.1.50:8123`), which avoids occasional local-name lookup hiccups.

### 🔁 Fixed a repeating screen flash on the Xeneon Edge in iCUE (#78)
- **Fixed the dashboard reloading over and over — the tiles vanishing to just the background for a second, then coming back — when running inside iCUE.** The dashboard reloads itself once on purpose right after the app self-updates, so a page left open picks up the new version. That check would fire on *any* version change, including going *backwards*: if an old copy of the server was ever left running alongside the freshly-updated one (so the two answer in turn), the reported version flip-flopped and the page reloaded in a loop — most visible inside iCUE, whose embedded browser reconnects often. The check now only reloads *forward* to a genuinely newer version and remembers it has done so for the rest of the session, so it can never loop, while a real update still reloads exactly once. If you ever see this, it's also worth making sure only one Xenon server is running (a leftover old one is the underlying cause) — and the native app avoids the flaky embedded-browser path entirely.

### 🌙 Ambient mode — the screensaver now actually starts on its own
- **Fixed the Ambient / Screensaver auto-start never firing after your chosen idle time.** You'd set it to appear after, say, 10 minutes without touching the screen, wait, and nothing would happen. The mode's "am I interrupting something?" guard was permanently tripping on the calendar's day view: that panel lives in the page at all times (hidden by a style, not by the usual on/off attribute), and the guard misread it as an open dialog forever — so the screensaver was always politely "waiting for you to finish". The guard now reads each panel's real on-screen state, so the screensaver starts when you're genuinely idle and still steps aside for a game, the layout editor, a voice chat or any dialog that's truly open.

### 🏠 Smart Home — the device search in Settings works again
- **Fixed the "Search device…" box in Settings → Smart Home doing nothing.** Typing a device or entity name left the full list unchanged, as if you hadn't typed at all. The search was correctly deciding which rows to hide, but a styling rule kept them on screen regardless, so the filter had no visible effect. Typing now narrows the list to matching devices and entities immediately.

## [v4.3.0] - 09-07-2026
### 🎮 GPU tile now shows VRAM too
- **The GPU card in the System widget can now show your video memory, not just the GPU load.** Tap the small ⇄ toggle on the card to flip it between **GPU** (utilization %) and **VRAM** (dedicated memory used) — the big number, the live sparkline and the card label all switch with it, and in VRAM mode you also see the exact amount in use (e.g. `3.9 GB / 15.9 GB`). It's the same at-a-glance card, now answering "is my graphics memory full?" as easily as "how hard is the GPU working?". The two graphs are kept separate, so switching never splices load and memory into one misleading line. The toggle only appears when your GPU actually reports VRAM (NVIDIA cards via nvidia-smi, and AMD/Intel via the sensor library) — on hardware that doesn't, the card stays exactly as before. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 📷 UniFi Protect — your security cameras on the dashboard
- **A new Cameras tile shows your UniFi Protect cameras, live.** Add it from the "+" palette, connect your UniFi console once in **Settings → Cameras**, and the tile shows a near-live view of your cameras — refreshed continuously while you're looking at it. Tap any camera to blow it up to a full-screen view; tap again to close. It's built for a glance: one camera fills the tile, several cameras arrange into a neat grid, and each shows a green/red dot for online/offline.
- **Pick exactly which cameras to show.** After connecting you get a checklist of every camera the console reports, so a busy household can put just the front door and driveway on the dashboard and leave the rest off.
- **Private by design, and light on resources.** Your console password stays on your PC — it's never sent to the browser, and the dashboard only fetches frames through a local proxy. The tile pulls nothing while it's hidden or while a game is running, so an unused Cameras tile costs nothing. Works best with a dedicated local Protect account (Viewer role, two-factor off).

### ⌨️ Deck — a key that runs your own script
- **A Deck key can now run your own scripts — batch, PowerShell, Python and many more.** Add a **Run script** action to any key and point it at a script file: Windows `.bat`/`.cmd`/`.ps1`/`.vbs`/`.wsf`, plus Python, Node.js, Ruby, Perl, PHP, Lua, R, a Java `.jar`, or a shell `.sh` — each runs through its own interpreter (which must be installed on your PC). Until now the only ways to open something were "Open app" (which accepts only programs) and "Open file/folder" (which deliberately refuses scripts, since it opens files with whatever handler Windows has registered and a script would run on a single tap of anything). "Run script" is the explicit, you-chose-it path: you pick the exact file, and it's run the right way (PowerShell through PowerShell instead of Notepad, a `.py` through `python`, and so on). The script shows its console window by default (so an installer or interactive script works), with an option to run it hidden for quiet fire-and-forget tasks. It's no more powerful than launching a program, which the Deck could already do.

### 🔄 The in-app "Update available" button now actually updates the app
- **On the Xenon native app, tapping "Update available" installs the new version in place instead of opening a GitHub page.** The native app has always been able to update itself — download the signed release and relaunch, no reinstall — but a second, browser-style update popup was also showing inside it, and its button just opened the release page in your web browser. That's the popup people were tapping. Now the native app shows a single update path that installs in-app: the tap downloads and applies the update and restarts on its own. (In a normal browser, "Download" still opens the release page as before — there's nothing to self-install there.)

### 🤖 Choose your AI: ChatGPT and Claude join Gemini and local Ollama
- **Xenon AI now runs on four providers — pick the one you want in Settings → Xenon AI.** Alongside Google **Gemini** (still the default) and the free on-device **Ollama**, you can now use **ChatGPT (OpenAI)** and **Claude (Anthropic)**. Each provider sits behind its own official icon, so the choice is clear at a glance. Paste that provider's API key and pick a model from a list that's **pulled live from the provider**, so the newest models it offers always show up without waiting for an app update. Then Xenon talks to it — the whole assistant works the same way it always has: it chats, sees images you attach, and runs every dashboard action by function-calling, so it can control your mic, media, volume, notes, tasks, timers, lighting, the Deck and the rest exactly like Gemini does.
- **Full voice, on every provider.** The voice orb keeps working whichever brain you pick. ChatGPT uses OpenAI's own speech-to-text and text-to-speech; Claude, which has no speech of its own, uses the same free local voices (Whisper for listening, Edge neural voices for speaking) that the Ollama provider uses — so you get spoken conversations without extra setup.
- **Your ChatGPT and Claude keys never leave your PC.** Unlike the Gemini key (which the browser needs directly), the OpenAI and Anthropic keys are used only by the local server and are never sent to the browser or included in a backup — the settings screen just shows a "saved" marker once a key is in place. Fully localised across the interface.

### 💬 Copy any message from the chat
- **You can now copy text out of the Xenon AI chat.** Every message shows a small copy button when you hover it (and it stays gently visible on the touchscreen), so one tap puts the whole reply on your clipboard — handy for saving a command Xenon wrote, a snippet of code, or an answer you want to paste elsewhere. You can also just select the text directly now: the chat used to inherit the dashboard's "no text selection" rule meant for the touch UI, which silently blocked selecting or copying replies. Selection is back on for chat messages only, so the rest of the touch interface is unchanged. Works in the Media tile's Chat tab and in any duplicated chat tile. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 🖥️ Native app now mirrors your dashboard settings reliably
- **Changes you make in the browser now show up on the Xeneon Edge, every time.** On some setups the native app on the Edge could get stuck showing the default theme and the first-run intro while the browser showed your real, configured dashboard — and later theme changes in the browser wouldn't reach the Edge. The cause was a timing one: the native app's live settings link could drop for a moment while the backend restarted at startup, and it never went back to ask "did I miss anything?", so it sat on stale settings (which also left the news/stocks ticker switched off). It now re-checks and catches up every time that link reconnects, so the two surfaces stay in step — the theme, your widgets and the ticker all follow along live.

### 🧩 Make your own widget — no code required
- **A new "Create a widget" wizard lets anyone build a custom dashboard widget without writing a single line of code.** Until now, making a widget meant hand-writing a manifest, HTML, JavaScript and CSS — a job for developers. Now you pick a template — **Clock**, **System monitor** (CPU/RAM/GPU as bars or rings), **Now playing**, **Label**, or **Countdown** — adjust a few options like the title, colour, font and which metrics to show, and watch a **live preview** update as you change them. One tap installs it, and it shows up in the widget picker just like any other. You can reopen a widget you made and tweak it again anytime. Reach it from **Settings → Widget e condivisione**, from an empty custom-widget tile, or straight from the widget picker.
- **Safe by the same rules as every other widget.** A created widget runs in the same locked-down sandbox (no network, no access to your files or settings) and still asks for its permissions before it does anything — nothing is granted automatically. You're only ever filling in options; there's no place for arbitrary code to sneak in, so importing or making a widget never weakens the boundary that keeps widgets contained. Fully localised across all 11 languages — and the whole Share & Import surface (which was still showing English in Spanish, French, German, Portuguese and Russian) is now translated too.

### 🧩 Adding a custom widget always lets you choose again
- **Adding a "Custom widget" from the "+" palette now always shows the widget chooser, instead of silently dropping in whatever you picked last time.** If you'd set a custom tile to, say, a clock and later removed it, adding a new custom widget would bring the clock straight back with no way to pick a different one — the tile remembered its old assignment. Now a freshly added custom tile always opens the "Choose a widget for this tile" list, so you can pick any installed widget. (Tiles already on your dashboard keep their widget across reloads as before; this only affects newly added ones.)

### 🧩 Custom widgets that show your tasks, notes or calendar now fill in immediately
- **A custom SDK widget that reads your task list, notes or calendar events now shows them the moment it loads, instead of looking empty until you next change something.** These three data feeds are only sent out when they change, and a sandboxed widget can't fetch on its own — so a "to-do list" widget added to the dashboard would sit blank until you happened to add or complete a task, even though the tasks were right there. The dashboard now hands each newly connected widget the current tasks, notes and events up front, exactly as it already did for CPU, media and audio, so these widgets paint real data straight away.

### ✅ Custom widgets can now add and complete your to-dos
- **A custom widget can now edit your task list — add a task, tick it off, or delete it — not just display it.** There's a new "tasks" permission a widget can ask for: grant it and a to-do widget can write to the very same list your Tasks tile shows, so anything it adds appears everywhere at once. It's the safe, opt-in path (the widget still runs sandboxed with no network, and asks before it can touch your tasks), and the text of every task you add is length-limited and cleaned up server-side just like the built-in Tasks tile. This turns a read-only "to-do viewer" widget into a real, interactive one you can type into.
- **Fixed custom widgets that use a newer data feed or control being unable to keep that permission — the grant was silently thrown away when saved.** The list of capabilities the dashboard would remember for a widget had fallen behind the ones it actually offers, so approving a widget's access to (for example) your tasks, notes, calendar, OBS, Spotify, Discord or Home Assistant was discarded the moment it was saved — the widget kept asking to be approved and never worked. The remembered set now matches exactly what a widget can request, so any permission you grant sticks. (A to-do widget that stayed empty and couldn't be written to was the visible symptom of this.)
- **When a widget you already use is updated to ask for a new permission, it now stops and asks you to review it, instead of quietly running without the new capability.** Previously only new network/webhook permissions triggered a re-check; a widget that gained, say, the ability to add tasks would install the update but keep running under its old (narrower) permissions, so the new feature silently did nothing. Now any added data feed or action prompts a quick "this widget asks for new permissions" review — approve it and the new feature works; nothing extra is ever granted behind your back.

### 👀 See what a shared code contains before you apply it
- **Importing a theme, background or page now shows a preview first — not an instant, silent change.** Deck profiles, packages and widgets already showed you what was inside before applying; now themes, backgrounds and pages do too. A theme shows its accent/background/text colours, its style (Liquid Glass or Pixel Retro) and whether it carries a font; a background shows a small live preview of the animation; a page shows how many widgets it adds. Each waits for an explicit **Apply**, so an imported code can no longer change your look the instant you paste it.

### ✨ A gentler animated-background editor
- **The background code editor now previews as you type and tells you when something's wrong.** Edits used to apply only when you clicked away, and a mistake in the code left the background silently black with no explanation. Now the preview updates live while you type, and a clear error message appears under the editor if the code fails — so you can fix it instead of guessing. Renaming or saving a theme, and replacing a starter background, now use tidy in-app dialogs instead of the browser's clunky pop-ups, which are awkward on the touchscreen.

## [v4.2.0] - 07-08-2026
### 🎚 Total theme control — shape, glass and every colour, on the whole dashboard or a single widget
- **Settings → Appearance is now a full theme editor.** Beyond the three base colours you can shape the entire look: corner roundness (from sharp corners to soft pills), the glass blur and saturation, the panel border and shadow strength, plus two more colours — muted text and the divider/line colour, each with an "Auto" that hands it back to the skin's own value. Every one of these is part of your theme, so **Save current theme** keeps them, a shared theme code carries them and a full backup restores them — nothing is left behind. The animated backgrounds (aurora, neon grid, static premium) now travel inside a theme too. Defaults are exactly today's look, so nothing changes until you reach for a slider.
- **Per-widget styling grew to match — style one tile down to the last detail.** The tile paint panel used to offer only accent, panel colour, opacity and font; now each widget can also set its own corner roundness, glass blur and saturation, muted-text colour and border/shadow strength — or keep following the global theme. It all rides inside a shared **page preset**, so sending someone your page sends your per-widget styling in full.
- **Xenon AI can now build a whole theme for you.** Ask for a vibe, "a warm minimalist look", "soft pastel and very rounded" — and Xenon composes a complete theme (skin, colours, roundness, glass, opacity, borders), applies it live and saves it as a named card in the gallery so you can jump back to it. It can also switch between Liquid Glass and Pixel Retro on request.

### 🌌 Your own animated background — pick one, ask for one, or code it
- **Settings → Background can now paint a live, full-screen animated backdrop behind your dashboard — and you don't need to write a line of code to get one.** Until now backgrounds were the built-in aurora/grid/static looks or an uploaded image/video; you couldn't invent your own motion. Now there are three easy ways in. **Pick one from the gallery:** nine one-tap ready-made backgrounds — drifting stars, flowing waves, pulsing neon dots, a nebula, aurora bands, matrix rain, confetti, orbiting particles and a plasma field. **Ask Xenon:** just say "crea uno sfondo animato con particelle blu che fluttuano" (or "make me a drifting-starfield background") and the assistant writes it and applies it live. **Or import one someone shared** with the new *Import/Export background* — a compact code that carries just the backdrop, so you can swap it in without importing a whole theme. For tinkerers, the code editor is still there with a built-in "how it works" guide (the `draw(ctx, t, w, h)` contract, what you can use, and a worked example). However it's made, it runs in the **exact same locked-down sandbox as community widgets** — an isolated frame with no network and no access to the dashboard, your files or your settings — so even an imported or AI-written background can only draw pixels, never touch anything (still, only import backgrounds from people you trust). It's a real part of your look: it's saved, survives restarts, self-pauses when the tab is hidden, and travels inside a **theme code** and a **package** too. Turning it on takes over the backdrop, so the aurora/grid/static controls clearly show they're paused. Fully localised across all 11 languages.
- **Performance & game mode now pause your custom background too.** Game mode and the "pause animations" performance setting already froze the built-in aurora/grid; a code-defined animated background, however, kept running its own animation loop in the background — so an animated backdrop could keep taxing the GPU during a game. Now it's paused right along with the built-ins (hidden under performance mode, frozen under game mode) and resumes the moment they clear.

### 📦 Package — share your whole setup in one code
- **A new "Export package" turns your theme, your page layouts and your community widgets into a single shareable code or file.** Until now you could share each piece on its own — a theme, one page, a Deck profile — but not the whole picture. Now **Settings → Appearance → Share & Import → Export package** opens a checklist: tick your colours & style, the pages you want, and any community widgets you've installed, and Xenon bundles them into one link/file. The person you send it to imports it from the same place, sees exactly what's inside before anything happens — the theme, how many pages, and every widget named with what it can do — and confirms. The theme is applied, the pages are added, and each widget is installed the safe way: it stays hidden and reaches nothing until they turn on Community widgets and approve its permissions, and every action a widget runs is still re-checked by Xenon. Only import packages from people you trust. Fully localised across all 11 languages.
- **An imported package now names its theme after the package.** When you import a package, the theme it carries is saved to your gallery under the package's own name instead of a generic "Custom theme 2", so the card is recognisable at a glance. (Importing a stand-alone theme already did this — now packages match.)

### 🐛 "Accent from album art" now stays off when you turn it off
- **Disabling the album-art accent finally sticks across restarts.** If you turned off Settings → Appearance → *Accent from album art*, it worked for the session but came back enabled after a PC restart — so the dashboard kept re-tinting itself from the cover art no matter how many times you switched it off. The setting was being saved by the browser but silently dropped by the server when it wrote its copy to disk, so the reloaded copy always fell back to the default (on). The server now keeps your choice like every other appearance setting, so off means off — through reloads and restarts.

### 🔒 Protect any shared export with access codes — and share a single widget on its own
- **The access-code protection now covers every export, not just themes.** When you share a theme, a page, a Deck profile, a widget, an animated background or a whole package, you can tap **Protect with access codes**, choose how many codes you want (say 10), and Xenon generates that many unique keys and a single protected file. Give a different code to each person: they paste your file or link, enter their code, and it unlocks — anyone without a valid code simply can't install it. The protection is real, not a checkbox: the export is encrypted on your machine and only a matching code can decrypt it, all locally with nothing sent to any server. It gates *who* can install; each code keeps working and can be passed on (it doesn't expire after one use). Save the codes when they're shown — you can copy them all or download them as a text file.
- **New "Export widget" shares one community widget on its own.** Until now a widget could only travel inside a full package; now you can hand someone a single widget as its own code or file. They see its name and exactly what it can do before confirming, and it installs the safe way — sandboxed, hidden and reaching nothing until they turn on Community widgets and approve its permissions, with every action still re-checked by Xenon.
- **Share & Import is clearer about what it does.** The panel now spells out that it both shares *and* imports — themes, pages, Deck profiles, widgets, backgrounds or whole packages — and the Import button reads "Import (link or file)" so it's obvious what to paste. Only import from people you trust. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 🎨 Themes, reorganised — pick a style, save your look, and a theme now means everything
- **Settings → Appearance now opens with a clear Themes gallery instead of three overlapping controls.** Before, the top of the tab was confusing: a "Theme" switch that actually meant light/dark, a separate "Dashboard style" toggle, and a row of "Quick presets" that were only colours — three things that all sounded like "theme". Now the gallery holds the two real styles, **Liquid Glass** and **Pixel Retro**, each with a live mini-preview (Liquid Glass shows your own palette). The old Ocean/Ember/Violet/Mono presets are gone because they were just Liquid Glass with different colours — and colours are edited right below, in **Colori**. Everything else (light/dark mode, colours, surface, custom font) sits under a clear **Personalize** heading, so the tab reads top-to-bottom: pick a style, then make it yours.
- **A "theme" is now your whole look, not just colours — save it, switch between saved looks, share it.** A theme now captures the entire visual identity of the Appearance tab: mode, style, colours, album-accent, panel opacity, background dim/blur and your custom font, all in one. Tap **Save current theme** to keep the look you've built as a card in the gallery, so you can import a friend's theme, try it, and jump straight back to your own — both live side by side, switchable with one tap, removable when you're done. **Export** packages the full look into a shareable link/code/file (fonts embedded when small enough), and **Import** applies all of it and adds it as its own card — without touching your other settings. Built to grow: everything you save or import lands in the same place. Fully localised across all 11 languages.
- **Tapping a base style now returns to its stock look.** Liquid Glass and Pixel Retro are skin-only, so tapping one while a saved custom theme was active used to change nothing visible and leave the gallery highlight stuck on the custom card. Now tapping a base style resets to that style's own default colours and surfaces — it visibly switches, and the gallery selection follows. To keep a look you've built, save it as a theme first (that's what the gallery is for).
- **Contextual profiles can now switch to a whole saved theme, not just a base skin.** In Settings → Performance → Contextual profiles, the "Style" column used to offer only Liquid Glass and Pixel Retro. It now also lists every theme you've saved, so you can set "when I game → Pixel", "when I code → my minimal theme" and so on — the full look (colours, background and surfaces), applied when the activity starts and restored to whatever you had when it ends. Saving, renaming or deleting a theme updates that dropdown immediately.
- **Deleting the theme you're using now drops you back to Liquid Glass.** Removing a saved theme card always persisted correctly, but if it was the look currently on screen the dashboard kept those colours until you picked another theme — which read like the delete hadn't taken. Now deleting the active theme returns the dashboard to the stock Liquid Glass look right away (deleting any other card leaves your current look untouched, as before).

### 🎨 Style any widget on its own — its colours, opacity and font, or the global theme
- **In the layout editor every tile now has a paint button that opens a small style panel: give that one widget its own accent, panel colour, panel opacity and font — or leave it following the global theme.** Until now a widget could only look like everything else; the whole dashboard shared one accent and one background. Now you can make your Now-Playing tile glow in album red while the system monitor stays green, dim a single panel so a background photo shows through it, or set a widget in the pixel VT323/Press Start font while the rest stays clean — each choice is scoped to that tile and nothing else. It's a real toggle: "Follow theme" hands the tile straight back to the global look with one tap. Every override is saved with your layout, so it survives reloads and restarts, rides along in a full backup, and travels inside a shared **page preset** — send someone your page and they get your per-widget styling too. Works on standalone widgets, duplicated copies and tab-groups alike.

### 🔤 Your own font — upload a typeface and make the whole dashboard yours
- **Settings → Appearance now has a Custom font control: upload a WOFF2, WOFF, TTF or OTF file (up to 8 MB) and the entire dashboard switches to it instantly.** Until now the look was fixed to Inter (with the Pixel Retro skin as the only alternative) — colours and backgrounds were yours to change, the typography wasn't. Now the font is a real, saved preference like everything else: it survives reloads and PC restarts, and "Remove" puts you back on the default Inter. It travels too — a full backup carries the font file so it comes back exactly on a new machine, and even a shared **theme code** embeds the font, so a friend who imports your theme gets your typeface, not just your colours (fonts too large to fit in a share code stay in the backup, with a heads-up). The Pixel Retro skin keeps its own arcade fonts when it's on.

### 🌫 Voice chat can now stay out of your way — transparent "edge-glow" mode
- **New in Settings → Xenon AI: "Transparent voice chat".** The voice assistant used to take over the whole screen with a dark room and the orb, so you couldn't watch your other widgets while talking to it. Turn this on and voice chat becomes ambient instead: your dashboard stays fully visible, only the edge of the screen lights up in your accent colour — gently while it listens, quicker and brighter while it thinks and speaks — and what you said and Xenon's reply appear as small, legible glass captions along the bottom. It's off by default, so nothing changes unless you choose it, and the classic full-screen orb is one toggle away. Works the same for both turn-based and Live voice, respects reduced-motion, and is localised across the app's languages.

### 🎙 Dictate straight into the chat — a single mic in the message box
- **The Xenon AI chat now has one microphone button, right next to Send.** Until now the only way to talk to Xenon was the full-screen voice orb, which covers the whole dashboard while you speak — so you couldn't glance at your other widgets mid-sentence. Tap the mic in the chat box, say your message, tap again, and your words drop into the input as text for you to review, edit and send. It never takes over the screen. It uses the same reliable voice pipeline as the orb, so it works on the Xeneon Edge touchscreen too, and it politely steps aside if the microphone is already in use by a voice session.
- **The chat box no longer shows a second, redundant microphone.** The composer used to carry two mics — one that dictated into the text box and another that launched the full-screen voice orb — which was confusing. The orb trigger has been removed from the chat box; the full voice conversation is still one tap away from the ✦ Xenon button in the top bar.

### 🌤 Weather — Fahrenheit now means imperial everywhere
- **Picking °F now switches wind, precipitation and visibility to imperial too.** Choosing Fahrenheit used to convert only the temperature, leaving wind in km/h, rain in mm and visibility in km — so a US forecast read "93°F" next to "20 km/h". Now selecting °F shows wind in mph, precipitation in inches and visibility in miles across the tile, the full weather screen, the hourly timeline and the lock screen; °C keeps the metric units as before. The change is instant, no reload needed.
- **A specific manual location no longer quietly caps the forecast at 3 days.** If you set the weather to a Manual city and typed something more specific than a plain city name — a full address or a place like "Bücherei Wien Hütteldorfer Straße 130d" — the forecast silently fell back to a 3-day source and ignored your chosen provider and "7 days" setting, even though the location itself showed correctly. Xenon now recovers the real coordinates for that place behind the scenes, so MET Norway and Open-Meteo can run and you get the full forecast you picked (up to 7 days) for exactly the same spot. You never have to deal with coordinates — just type the place as you always did.

### 🧩 Custom widget — "Add" now works right after you drop the tile in
- **Picking a community widget no longer forces you out of edit mode first.** When you added a Custom widget tile from the "+" palette, it appeared already in layout-edit mode showing its package picker — but tapping **Add** (or the "Turn on" / "Rescan" buttons) did nothing, because the invisible drag surface that lets you move a tile was sitting on top of those buttons and swallowing the tap. The only way through was to leave edit mode, which wasn't obvious. Those setup buttons now sit above the drag surface, so you can choose your widget and approve its permissions right where the tile lands — while everything else on the tile still drags normally.
- **The "+" widget menu no longer slides items out from under your cursor.** On a shorter window the Add-widget menu scrolls, and clicking an item near the bottom — most often **Custom widget** — used to make it jump away the instant you pressed, so the click never landed and you had to chase it. That was the menu scrolling the item you'd just focused into view. Items now stay put when you click them (and the menu reserves room for its scrollbar so a whole column can't shift sideways either), so every tile in the palette is clickable on the first try, mouse or touch.
- **The widget picker now groups your widgets by pack.** When you choose which community widget a Custom tile shows, the list is grouped under a header per pack (the widget's author), so widgets that arrived together — say a "Pixel pack" — sit together instead of scattered through one long flat list.
- **A placed community widget now looks exactly like a native one.** Once you pick a widget for a Custom tile, the host's own little header — the puzzle badge, the "Custom widget" label and the swap button — is gone: the widget fills the whole tile and draws its own look, just like the built-in tiles do. The "choose another widget" control now appears only while you're editing the layout (as a small overlay), so nothing extra shows during normal use.

## [v4.1.0] - 07-07-2026
### 🎛️ Razer Chroma & Elgato Wave Link — control your gear from Xenon
- **Xenon now talks to Razer Chroma and Elgato Wave Link.** Two of the most-requested "can it control my hardware" integrations are here — done the right way. Both apps expose a private local connection on your PC that a browser widget can't reach on its own (by design — that sandbox is what keeps third-party widgets from touching anything on your machine). Xenon's backend does the talking for them and hands the controls to the dashboard, the Deck and the Widget SDK as proper, you-approve-them actions — exactly how Home Assistant, Discord and Streamer.bot already work.
- **Razer Chroma: your keyboard follows your theme.** Turn it on in Settings → Illuminazione and Razer Chroma joins the lighting system like any other device — so the same ambient, album-art and reactive effects that already drive your WLED/Hue/Nanoleaf lights now light up your Razer keyboard, mouse and headset too, tinted to your accent colour. You also get direct Deck keys and SDK actions to set a specific device to any colour, or turn it off. When you're done, control hands straight back to Synapse.
- **Elgato Wave Link: ride your mixes from the Deck.** Enable it in Settings → Streaming and your Wave Link channels become Deck keys and SDK actions — set an input or output volume, mute/unmute a channel (local mix, stream mix or both), flip monitoring, switch the monitor mix. The channel picker fills with your actual Wave Link mixers, and a live stream mirrors the mixer state so a widget can show real faders.
- **Build your own.** Because both are exposed through the Widget SDK, anyone building a widget can request the `chroma`/`wavelink` actions (and the live Wave Link mixer stream) in their manifest — the user grants them once, and the widget drives real hardware without ever touching localhost. This is the supported way to do local-hardware control from a widget.
- **Safe and quiet by default.** Both are **off until you turn them on**, so Xenon never probes for hardware you don't use. Each has a "Test connection" button, and if Synapse or the Wave Link app isn't running everything degrades gracefully — no errors, nothing breaks. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 🎚️ A real audio mixer on your dashboard — Wave Link faders + OBS mic control
- **A new Wave Link mixer widget with live faders.** Add it from the "+" palette (Streaming) and every Wave Link channel — Mic, Game, Chat, Music… — shows up as a real fader you can ride from the touchscreen, with a per-channel mute and the output bus below. A **Stream / Local** switch at the top picks which mix the faders control: the stream mix is what your viewers hear, the local mix is what *you* hear. There's also a one-tap monitor A/B switch. The faders move in real time with Wave Link and Wave Link moves with them — this is the live mixer the Deck actions were already feeding. Enable it in Settings → Streaming; if the Wave Link app isn't open the widget just says so.
- **The OBS widget can now control your microphone (and every audio input).** The OBS tile gained an **Audio** section: each OBS audio source — your mic, desktop audio, aux inputs — gets a mute toggle and a live volume fader, mirrored straight from OBS and updating the instant you (or OBS) change it. So the "mute my mic before I stream" and "the mic is too loud" moments are now one tap on the dashboard, no Alt-Tab into OBS. Setting an input's volume is also available as a new Deck key (**OBS: input volume**).
- **Both are opt-in, live-only and lightweight.** The mixer only connects while its tile (or a Deck key) is on screen, and closes itself when nobody's watching — nothing runs in the background for people who don't stream. Fully localised across all 11 languages.

### 💡 Control your whole RGB lighting from the Deck, a widget, and third-party widgets
- **A new Lighting tile on the dashboard.** Add a **Lighting** widget from the "+" menu (System) and control your whole rig without opening Settings: a master on/off switch, a live colour field that glows in whatever colour your lights are showing (and gently breathes while an animated effect is running), one-tap colour swatches plus a full colour picker, effect buttons (solid, breathing, cycle, wave, aurora, candle, palette), an "Auto" button that hands control back to your configured lighting, and a per-device list where each light can follow the dashboard or be set to its own colour, animation, temperature, album-art or off. It reflects the live state and, like the rest of the dashboard, goes completely still when you're not looking at it.
- **Your lighting is no longer trapped in Settings.** The full RGB system — the iCUE bridge plus every external provider (WLED, Philips Hue, Nanoleaf, OpenRGB, Yeelight, Home Assistant lights, Razer Chroma) — can now be driven straight from a Deck key. New Deck actions under a **Lighting** category: turn all lights **on/off** (or toggle), set a **fixed colour** across the whole rig (the "my theme is purple, keep everything purple" button), pick an **ambient effect** (solid, breathing, cycle, wave, aurora, candle, palette), snap back to **auto**, or control **a single device** (follow the dashboard, fixed colour, animation, temperature, album art, or off). A Deck-driven change persists exactly like changing it in Settings, so it survives a restart.
- **They appear only when you actually have lights.** Like the Chroma and Wave Link actions, the Lighting category shows up in the Deck editor only once you've got controllable lighting configured; otherwise it stays as a single hint row pointing you to Settings → Illuminazione, so the feature is discoverable without cluttering the picker for people who don't use RGB. The per-device picker fills with your real devices. Fully localised across all 11 languages.
- **Widgets can drive it too.** The same lighting controls are exposed through the Widget SDK's `lighting` permission, so a third-party widget can request them in its manifest and control your whole rig — you approve it once — without ever reaching localhost.

### 🧩 Widget SDK — third-party widgets can now use much more of Xenon
- **A big jump in what a widget can read and do.** The philosophy is the opposite of a closed ecosystem: expose as much of Xenon as can be done safely, and gate each capability behind a permission the user approves. The SDK went from 5 data streams and 7 action categories to **16 streams and 14 action categories**. A widget can now *read* your system stats, media, audio, stocks, football scores, news, Claude Code usage, the live state of OBS / Discord / Streamer.bot / Home Assistant, and your tasks, notes and calendar events — and *act* on media, volume, mic, the whole RGB lighting system, Razer Chroma, Wave Link, Spotify, OBS, Discord, Home Assistant, Twitch, YouTube and Streamer.bot. Every one of these is a separate permission shown in the install dialog, and every action is re-validated by the same gate the Deck uses.
- **Safe by design, generous on purpose.** The dangerous primitives stay out no matter what a widget asks for — no launching apps or files, no arbitrary keystrokes, no arbitrary Home Assistant service calls, no shell. Sensitive reads (Home Assistant state, your notes) are clearly labelled in the permission dialog so you grant them knowingly. Nothing a widget does can reach your machine except through these approved, validated channels.
- **The docs can't go stale anymore.** The list of everything the SDK exposes is now generated straight from the code, and a test fails the build if the documentation ever drifts from what's actually available — so a widget developer always reads an accurate, up-to-date capability list. Full reference in `docs/WIDGET_SDK.md`.

### 🧰 Installer — a clearer, better-looking one-click setup
- **INSTALL.bat now greets you with an animated Xenon banner and the details that matter.** Setup used to open on a bare line of text. It now "powers on" a crisp, properly aligned "XENON" wordmark — scanned in left-to-right with a bright leading edge — then shows the exact version you're installing, the display it's for, the dashboard address and the project link, plus a short summary of what it will set up (only if needed). It reads like the futuristic product it is, and it degrades to a clean static banner when there's no console to animate in (silent/unattended installs).
- **The "how do you want to use Xenon" choice is no longer confusing.** Option 2 read "iCUE widget", which made it look like the dashboard only works inside Corsair iCUE. It's now labelled **iCUE / Browser** and spells it out: the same dashboard runs inside iCUE *or* in any web browser at `http://127.0.0.1:3030`. The Native-app option (recommended) is unchanged.
- **A tidier finish.** The closing screen now confirms the installed version, restates the dashboard address for iCUE or a browser, and keeps the admin tip only when it actually applies. Purely cosmetic — the install steps themselves are exactly as before.

### 🖥️ Native app — set your own interface scale, and zoom with Ctrl + wheel
- **You can now zoom the native app with Ctrl + mouse wheel (and Ctrl + / -).** Until now the full-screen app ignored the usual zoom shortcuts, so the dashboard was stuck at whatever size the Windows display scale produced. Zooming now works just like it does in any browser.
- **Choose your own interface scale in Settings.** Settings → General (shown only in the native app) has a new **Interface scale** slider: drag it to make the whole dashboard larger or smaller — from 60% to 160% — completely independent of the Windows display scale. Your choice is remembered and re-applied every time the app opens. The Ctrl + wheel zoom is there for quick, in-the-moment adjustments; the slider is the setting that sticks. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🧠 Local AI (Ollama) — safe on every PC, with a clear reason when it isn't
- **The local AI will never overload your PC.** Xenon now knows how much video memory (or RAM) each local model really needs, and it refuses to download or run a model your machine can't handle — no more downloading gigabytes only to crash on the first message. If your hardware genuinely isn't up to it, it tells you plainly ("your hardware isn't suitable — nothing was downloaded; use Xenon AI in the cloud instead") rather than failing in a confusing way. The automatic "Auto" model choice is now more cautious too, so the model it picks for you actually runs smoothly.
- **A real explanation when a local model crashes.** If a local model still fails on the GPU — a known driver/model bug can throw a raw "CUDA error: illegal memory access" — Xenon now shows a plain-language explanation of what happened and what to try (update your GPU driver and Ollama, or pick a lighter model), instead of dumping the cryptic error at you.
- **Automatic recovery to a lighter model.** If a local model crashes the GPU or runs out of video memory *before it has done anything*, Xenon automatically retries your message on a smaller model you already have installed and answers anyway, with a short note telling you it switched. It never re-runs an action that had already started, so nothing happens twice.

### 🎇 Static background — a premium look that costs nothing to run
- **A new kind of background: gorgeous and completely still.** Settings → Sfondo now offers a **Static background** with three curated looks — **Nebulosa** (soft accent light pools with depth), **Prisma** (a modern mesh gradient with violet and cyan highlights) and **Halo** (a single cinematic accent glow into deep black). Unlike the animated Aurora, nothing moves: the picture is painted once and then left alone, so on-screen it costs about as much as a plain colour. Ideal if you want the dashboard to look high-end without the native app or browser using any real CPU/GPU to keep animating — a common request from people running Xenon on the desktop next to games and other apps.
- **It tints to your accent, in light and dark.** Each look reads your accent colour, so it always matches the rest of the dashboard, and every one has a tuned light-theme variant. A fine, invisible grain is layered on top to keep the gradients perfectly smooth on the Xeneon Edge panel (no visible banding).
- **Picking a static look takes over the backdrop completely** — it pauses both the animated Aurora and the neon Grid, because "zero animation" is the whole point — and the Settings panel makes that clear, disabling those controls with a note. If you have a custom image/video background set, the static look is hidden behind it and Settings now tells you so instead of appearing to do nothing. Choose **Nessuno** to go back to the Aurora at any time. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🔋 Lower resource use — the dashboard goes quiet when you're not looking
- **When you're not using it, Xenon now stops animating — completely.** On an always-on second screen the dashboard kept every little animation running forever (the blinking clock colon, the ✦ logo shimmer, the "no media" equaliser bars, live dots, the Vitals heartbeat, Bit, ambient Deck keys…), and each one keeps the graphics compositor busy every single frame — the constant few-percent CPU/GPU some of you spotted in Task Manager for a screen nobody was touching. After a short spell without interaction, or whenever the window is hidden, all of that motion now pauses at its current frame so the graphics chip can go idle. It resumes instantly the moment you touch, move over, or look back at the display — the dashboard looks identical while you're actually using it. This is automatic and needs no setting; Performance mode still turns everything off on demand, and the new Static background removes the single biggest animated layer entirely.
- **The "no media" music tile no longer animates for nothing.** Its little equaliser bars and the soft rotating glow used to loop forever even though the tile only ever shows that placeholder when *nothing* is playing — motion visualising silence, costing GPU around the clock. It's now a clean, still equaliser glyph: identical at a glance, zero per-frame cost whenever no track is playing (which, for many people, is most of the time).
- **The dashboard's background "heartbeat" now goes quiet too — even on an empty dashboard.** Some of you measured 1–3% CPU with animations off, Performance mode on, or even with *no widgets at all*. The culprit wasn't the widgets: the backend re-sent the "what's playing" update every 2 seconds and the status update every 3 seconds even when nothing had changed, and every one of those woke the app up to redraw a picture that was already correct. Both updates are now sent **only when something actually changed** (a track starts or pauses, the mic mutes, a game launches…), the same change-only rule the volume stream already followed. On an idle PC the dashboard now genuinely sits still between real updates — the live graphs, clock and everything you see keep working exactly as before, changes still appear instantly, and a freshly added Media or Microphone tile fills in immediately from the last known state.

### 🇳🇱 Dutch — Xenon now speaks Nederlands
- **Added a complete Dutch (Nederlands) translation.** Xenon already shipped in ten languages; Dutch makes eleven. The whole interface is translated — every settings panel, widget, control, toast and greeting — not just a handful of labels. Pick **Nederlands** in Settings → General → Language and the dashboard, including the new Display panel, switches instantly. (Bit, the guardian pet, still speaks English for now — its lines are a separate, hand-written set.)

### 🔆 Display control — set your monitor's brightness right from Xenon, no iCUE
- **New Settings → Schermo panel adjusts your screen's actual hardware brightness, contrast and colour.** Xenon now talks to the monitor over DDC/CI — the same channel iCUE uses — so you can dim the Xeneon Edge (or any other monitor) straight from the dashboard, without opening iCUE or reaching for the monitor's own buttons. Brightness and contrast come as simple sliders; an advanced "Colour balance" section adds per-channel red/green/blue white-point trim on panels that support it (the Xeneon Edge does), and a separate Backlight slider appears on the monitors that expose one (on a normal LCD, brightness already controls the backlight).
- **It adapts to whatever screen you're on, and to what that screen can do.** Every monitor is detected by its real name (your Xeneon Edge shows up as "XENEON EDGE"), and only the controls a given screen genuinely exposes are shown — a display that doesn't speak DDC/CI simply says so instead of offering dead sliders. On a multi-monitor setup you get a picker to choose which screen to control, and your choice is remembered, so the panel always lands on the display you actually run Xenon on. Values track your finger live and are written straight to the monitor. Fully localised across all 10 languages.
- **One tap to undo everything.** Because these settings live in the monitor itself, a **Restore factory defaults** button sits under the sliders — if a tweak (especially the RGB white-point) ever looks wrong, one tap puts that screen back exactly as it came, and the sliders snap to the restored values. It's shown only for monitors that support the reset, so you can always get back.

### 🌤 Weather — pick how many days the forecast shows
