- **Choose 1 to 7 days in the "next days" forecast.** The forecast was fixed at three days. Settings → Meteo now has a **Forecast days** option to show anywhere from a single day up to a full week — pick a short list to keep the tile compact, or the whole week to plan ahead. The change is instant, no reload needed, and applies to both the dashboard tile and the full weather screen.
- **It just works on the recommended sources.** Open-Meteo (the default) and MET Norway provide the full seven days; wttr.in only publishes three, so on that source the forecast simply shows the three it has. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🛠️ Fixed
- **Long dropdown menus no longer look cut off on the Xeneon Edge.** A picker with many entries — the Deck key's Action list, which now spans Spotify, Home Assistant, Razer Chroma, Wave Link and more — grew tall enough to fill the whole short display top to bottom, so the first and last rows sat flush against the screen edges and read as clipped. Every floating dropdown now keeps a clear margin from the top and bottom of the screen and scrolls inside that space, so it always shows as a tidy, bounded menu with its rounded corners visible — no matter how long the list.
- **The weather now really refreshes as often as you set it.** If you chose a 10- or 15-minute refresh in Settings → Meteo, the weather still only updated roughly every half hour. The server kept its own copy of the forecast for 10 minutes, which lined up exactly with the shortest refresh you could pick — so every second check landed a moment too early and got the old copy back, quietly doubling the real interval. The server now holds the forecast for a shorter time than any refresh setting, so a 10-minute choice updates every 10 minutes as expected.
- **The Volume tile no longer shows up empty until you reload.** On some layouts the master volume control could appear blank — no level, no device — until you refreshed the page. Live audio updates are only sent when something actually changes, so a Volume (or Microphone) tile that finished loading a beat after the first update had nothing to show and, on a quiet system where the volume never changed, stayed that way. Both tiles now fill in with the current level the moment they appear, no refresh needed.
- **The "return to Xenon" button no longer looks malformed on the desktop (native app).** After swiping up to reach the Windows desktop, the round Xenon button that stays on screen had a stray shape peeking out behind it — partly Windows still drawing its own drop shadow and Windows 11's rounded-corner window backdrop (with a faint light border) around the button's square frame, and partly the dashboard's own floating "Layout" button poking through the round button's transparent corners. The window backdrop is now squared-off and shadow-free while the button is showing, and the dashboard underneath is hidden, so it reads as a clean, floating round button with nothing behind it.
- **Returning from the desktop no longer drops you into layout-edit mode (native app).** Tapping the round button to come back could land the dashboard straight in the layout editor. A finger tap fires a release then a click; the button hid itself on the release, so the click that immediately followed fell through onto the floating "Layout" button behind it and toggled editing on — every time. That stray click is now absorbed, so returning simply restores the dashboard.

## [v4.0.1] - 06-07-2026
### 🛠️ Fixed
- **Saving a layout could blow every widget up to full screen.** If a dashboard page was still open from before the v4 update (typically the one on the Xeneon Edge screen itself), it kept running the old pre-v4 code against the new server. The next time that stale page saved anything, it re-submitted your layout in the old 12-column format — and the server, believing it was upgrading an old layout, doubled every tile's position and size again. One or two rounds of that and every widget ended up full-width and taller than the screen. The server now recognises a save coming from a stale page and keeps your stored layout, presets and newer settings intact instead of letting them be overwritten or reset; the dashboard gained the mirror protection too, so a stale copy left in a browser's storage can't sneak the corrupted layout back in either. **If your layout was already affected: reload the dashboard page on every screen, then rearrange (or reset) it once in the Layout editor — from then on it sticks.**
- **Dashboards left open across an update now reload themselves.** From this version onward, every open dashboard page (browser tabs, the Xeneon Edge screen, the native app) detects when the server comes back on a new version and reloads onto the matching new interface automatically — no more stale pages running old code against a new backend. (Pages still running v4.0.0 or older don't have this detection yet — reload those once by hand after this update.) The reload politely waits while you're editing the layout or typing.
- **Choosing "Native app" in INSTALL.bat now actually installs the native app.** Picking option 1 (Native app) during setup did nothing on a normal download: the installer only looked for a locally-built app bundle — which exists only on a developer's machine after building it — so for everyone else it silently gave up and just opened the dashboard in the browser instead. It now downloads the signed native-app installer straight from the latest release (the same one the dashboard button uses), installs it, and launches it — so option 1 delivers the full-screen app as promised. (If you're offline or the installer isn't attached yet, it tells you and points you to install it later from Settings.)
- **The "Install the native app" button now actually installs it — and shows real progress.** The one-click install from a browser or the iCUE widget silently failed to even start (the installer was launched in a way Windows PowerShell couldn't run), so the button just sat on "Installer launched" forever. It now launches correctly and, since the install runs silently with no window, reports each step live — downloading, installing, done — with a clear reason if something goes wrong (the installer isn't on the release yet, the download failed, …) instead of leaving you guessing.
- **The install progress could freeze on "Downloading the installer…" even when the install succeeded.** The installer's progress file was written in an encoding the dashboard couldn't read back, so the live feedback never advanced past the first step — the app would quietly install and open on the Edge while the button still looked stuck. The progress now reports every step correctly.
- **After the native app installs, it now tells you what to do next.** The install used to end on "Installed! Opening on the Edge" and then just sit there, looking frozen and leaving you unsure where the app went. It now clearly marks the button as done and adds a short next step tailored to where you are: from the iCUE widget it explains the native app runs on the Edge on its own and you can close iCUE (reopen it any time to come back); from a browser it points you to the full-screen app on your Edge display.
- **The native app no longer waits forever when the Xenon backend isn't running.** The app is a display for the local Xenon widget: if nothing answered right after launch, its startup screen just spun on "Waiting for the Xenon service…" with no clue why. The app now starts the widget's login task by itself when the backend is down — covering a backend that crashed or didn't start at login — and if the widget genuinely isn't installed, after a minute the startup screen says so and tells you exactly what to install, instead of spinning silently.
- **The "Try the native app" button comes back after you uninstall.** The dashboard decided whether to offer the native app from a saved marker that uninstalling never cleared, so once you'd installed it the offer stayed hidden even after you removed the app. It now checks whether the app is actually on your PC, so uninstalling makes the install button reappear on its own.
- **The swipe-up "return to Xenon" button is clearer.** In the native app, swiping up to peek at the Windows desktop leaves a small round button to jump back to the dashboard. It now shows the Xenon logo on a clean face instead of a vague dark orb, so it reads at a glance as the button it is.

## [v4.0.0] - 06-07-2026
### 🎨 Design — sharper cards, a calmer background, and an optional Pixel Retro skin
- **Every card on the dashboard got a quiet quality pass.** Tiles now read as gently lit objects instead of flat translucent rectangles: a hairline top light, a subtle top-lit surface wash, crisper borders and new two-layer shadows (a tight contact line plus a soft ambient) that give real depth without the muddy glow. The Liquid Glass material itself is calmer too — less milky, a crisper edge, a shorter sheen. Nothing moved and nothing was redesigned away: it's the same dashboard, executed more cleanly, in both dark and light themes.
- **The animated background grew up.** The old drifting colour blobs are replaced by an elegant depth scene: a faint accent bloom high above the horizon, a soft corner vignette, and two large ambient light pools that drift extremely slowly in your accent colour — premium and never distracting, like a lit room your tiles sit in. Your existing intensity and speed sliders still control it, it still steps aside for a custom wallpaper, and it still pauses in game/performance/idle mode. The static part costs nothing per frame.
- **New: a full "Pixel Retro" dashboard style.** Settings → Aspetto → **Stile dashboard** now offers two visual languages: the default **Liquid Glass**, and **Pixel Retro** — a complete '80s/'90s CRT console transformation. Terminal pixel typography, your accent colour as the phosphor ink, hard square corners and chunky offset shadows everywhere, buttons that physically "press" into their own shadow, pixelated album art, a static pixel starfield sky, and an optional **CRT scanline** overlay with its own toggle. It's one tap to enter, one tap back, it syncs like every other setting, and it deliberately adds zero animation of its own — the whole skin is pure paint.
- **The Deck keeps its console identity inside a tab.** When a Deck lives in a tabbed tile, the hosting glass card no longer makes it look like a gadget floating in a glass box: while the Deck is the active tab, the tile itself becomes a matte chassis mount (the tab bar reads as the device's faceplate strip) and the console docks into it edge-to-edge — in Pixel Retro too, where the mount repaints in the CRT navy.
- **Personalise the minimal top-bar island.** With the **Minimal** top bar selected, Settings → Aspetto → **Barra superiore** now lets you shape the floating island exactly how you like it. **Position** anchors the whole capsule to the **left, centre or right** — so it can sit clear of the widget beneath the middle (handy when, say, your weather panel wants the room). And a new **island elements** editor lists every segment — **time, date, weather, vitals, page dots** — each with a drag handle to **reorder** them left-to-right and an eye button to **show or hide** it. Rearrange, trim it down to just the clock, or push the weather to the front — it's yours. Everything syncs across your dashboards like every other setting. The full glass bar is deliberately left untouched: these controls only appear in Minimal mode, so Full stays the clean, fixed classic bar. Fully localised.

### 🧠 Xenon AI — it remembers you, thinks in longer conversations, and speaks the moment it has something to say
- **Xenon now remembers you between sessions.** Tell it your name, that you've got an RTX 4090, that you support Napoli, how you like your dashboard — and it keeps that, quietly, across reloads and restarts, so it stops asking the same things twice and answers with context it used to forget the instant you closed the tab. It writes a fact when you share something durable ("ricordati che…"), drops it when you ask it to forget, and never stores secrets or one-off task details. Everything lives in a small local file on your PC — nothing leaves the machine. You can see exactly what it remembers, delete any single item, turn the whole thing off, or wipe it clean, in Settings → Xenon AI → Memoria personale. On by default, fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Long conversations stay coherent.** Xenon used to simply forget the oldest turns once a chat got long, so it could lose the thread of what you'd been talking about. Now, as a conversation grows, the earlier part is quietly condensed into a running summary that travels with the chat — so it keeps the context of a long back-and-forth instead of dropping it. It happens in the background and never slows down your reply.
- **One-tap undo for the AI's changes.** When Xenon changes something you might regret — overwriting your notes, clearing all your tasks or events, adding a task — a small "Undo" appears under its reply in the chat. Tap it and the previous state comes straight back. It's there for the moments that matter and quietly absent for harmless actions.
- **Follow-up questions about a file you shared now work.** When you attach a document or image and then ask a follow-up ("and what does the second page say?", "translate that"), Xenon keeps the file in mind for the next couple of turns instead of forgetting it the instant it answered once — so you don't have to re-attach it to keep talking about it.
- **Multi-step requests actually finish.** Asking Xenon to do several things in one go — "build me a streaming page and set up the deck for it", or a chain of actions — used to get cut off after a few steps. It now has room to carry a request through to the end (with a firm time limit so it can never hang), so complex asks complete in a single turn.
- **Optional "advanced reasoning" for hard questions.** A new switch in Settings → Funzioni AI lets your written questions use a stronger model when you want more careful answers to complex things. It's off by default and only affects typed chat — voice stays on the fast model so spoken replies never lag — and if the stronger model isn't available on your key, Xenon quietly falls back to the fast one instead of failing.
- **Ask Xenon to compare your PC's history over time.** With Guardian on, you can now ask things like "was my GPU hotter yesterday than today", "what was my worst day this month" or "how has my CPU temp trended this week" — Xenon reads the recorded history for that one sensor (today vs yesterday, last 24 hours, weekly and monthly averages, the month's peak day) and answers from the real numbers, all computed locally.
- **Xenon starts speaking sooner.** Spoken replies used to wait until the entire answer had been turned into audio before you heard a single word — noticeably slow on longer answers. Now Xenon speaks the first sentence the moment it's ready and prepares the next one while that plays, so the voice starts almost immediately and flows naturally. The music-ducking and on-screen text still appear cleanly as one, and tapping to interrupt still stops it instantly.
- **New: "Voce Live" — a real-time, talk-over-it voice mode (beta).** Turn on Voce Live in Settings → Xenon AI and the voice button opens a genuine full-duplex conversation: Xenon streams its answer as it thinks, and you can cut in and talk over it at any moment — it stops and listens instantly, no button, no waiting for it to finish. Under the hood it uses Google's Gemini Live realtime model and can still run every dashboard command by voice (volume, timers, lighting, media, notes, and the rest), remembering you and carrying the conversation's context just like the normal chat. It's **off by default** and clearly marked beta: it needs a Live-capable Gemini API key and uses more of your Gemini quota, and headphones give the best experience (on open speakers the mic can hear the assistant). If the Live model isn't available on your key — or there's no microphone — Xenon quietly falls back to the normal turn-based voice, which stays the default. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **A new proactive heads-up when your PC runs unusually hot.** On top of the existing "over the limit for 15 minutes" alert, Xenon now learns what "normal" looks like for your CPU and GPU during a session and quietly flags it when a temperature climbs well above that baseline — even while it's still under the danger threshold — so you catch a developing problem (a fan that's stopped spinning, a runaway background process) early. It's deliberately calm: it only speaks up once an hour at most, ignores harmless warm-ups, and never doubles up with the existing thermal alert. Toggle it in Settings → Momenti proattivi, fully localised.

### ✦ Claude Code usage — a living reactor for your token consumption
- **A new Claude Code widget for the dashboard.** Add it from the "+" palette (System) and it shows a plasma reactor at a glance: a glowing core that tints to the model you're currently running — Opus, Sonnet, Haiku or the frontier models each get their own colour — with particles streaming into it and a live pulse while Claude is actually working. Around the core sit clean readouts: tokens used **today** and **this week**, your **cache-hit rate**, and the **equivalent API value** of everything you've run. It's built for the people who use Claude Code on their PC and want to see, in one glance, how much they've spent and what they're working on.
- **See every Claude that's running, and what each is doing.** If you have several Claude Code sessions open at once, they all show up — one row each, with the project and git branch it's in, the model it's using, and **what it's currently working on** (its last prompt). The dashboard on your Xeneon Edge doubles as a quiet control tower for all your parallel work.
- **Inviting even before you've run anything.** On a PC with no Claude Code history yet, the widget no longer shows a lonely line of text in an empty box. It now renders a "standing by" reactor — a resting core with the Xenon spark at its centre and zeroed readouts laid out exactly like the live view — plus a short note that your usage, projects and models will light it up as soon as you start a session. The tile looks complete from the first moment, and stays continuous the instant real data arrives.
- **100% local, no key, no signup.** Everything is read straight from Claude Code's own session files on your PC (`~/.claude`) — there is no account, no API key and nothing ever leaves the computer. It works for everyone on every plan, even offline, and it's read only while a dashboard is actually open. The reading is throttled and only re-scans the session being written right now, so it stays feather-light.
- **A weekly "fuel gauge" you set yourself.** Because there is no official way to ask Anthropic how much of your plan is left, the reactor's remaining-budget ring is one *you* choose: tap the reactor and pick a plan estimate (Pro / Max 5× / Max 20×) or type your own weekly token ceiling — the ring then depletes as the week goes on. Prefer not to set one? Leave it on **Auto** and the reactor instead charges up with the week's activity against its own recent peak. It's honest about being an estimate, and you can change it any time.
- **Grow the tile to see more.** Kept small it's just the reactor and the four headline numbers; make it taller and it fills in a **30-day history** (with the cheap cache-served tokens stacked under the fresh ones, so an efficient day reads at a glance), a **per-project split** of where your tokens went, and a **per-model split**. Resizes cleanly from a compact tile up to a full column.
- **Kept deliberately light and private.** No new dependencies. The reactor is a single canvas that runs at a modest frame rate, only animates while it's on screen, and — like the animated background — **freezes the moment the dashboard goes idle** so it never keeps your GPU busy when nobody's looking; it respects "reduce motion" too. Reading the session files is throttled and only re-scans the session being written right now, and the aggregate is pushed over the existing live stream only when it actually changes. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🧲 Layout editor — dragging that always works, and widgets that go where you put them
- **Dragging a tile now works every time.** The root cause of tiles that randomly refused to move is fixed: the drag was bound to a small grip element that could silently die whenever a tile re-rendered (after adding a widget from the "+", merging tabs, rebuilding a page…), leaving the tile stuck until a reload. The drag is now anchored to the tile itself, which survives every re-render — and tiles added from the "+" palette are draggable the instant they land.
- **Drag from anywhere on the tile.** In Layout mode the whole tile is the drag surface (with a small grip pill on top as the cue) instead of a narrow strip on the left edge — far easier on the touchscreen. Tile tabs and the edit buttons (resize, + Tab, save, hide, ×) stay tappable, and a tile placed on a rebuilt page can no longer come back "placed but frozen".
- **Place widgets where *you* want.** The layout grid is now twice as fine in both directions (24 columns and half-height rows), so tiles snap to positions and sizes much closer to exactly where you drop them — no more "it jumped half a tile away". Resizing from the corner uses the same finer steps.
- **Clearer feedback while you drag.** The tile lifts with a shadow and an accent-coloured dashed placeholder always shows the exact slot it will land in; dropping onto the centre of another tile still merges them into a tabbed tile, with the same highlight as before.
- **Tiles can no longer be crushed into an invisible sliver.** A tile could be corner-resized down to a single row — and while it was alone on a page (stretched to fill the screen) that was easy to do by accident. Then, the moment you added a second widget next to it, the taller neighbour forced the row height and squashed the one-row tile down to a thin strip that looked like it had vanished. Tiles now have a sensible minimum height: the resize handle stops before it collapses them, and any tile already saved too short is restored to a readable height automatically.
- **Shortened widgets now scroll their content instead of clipping it.** When you made a widget shorter than its content, the detail views for **Borsa** (stocks) and **Calcio** (football) simply cut off at the tile's edge with no way to reach what was below. Their detail views now scroll: the top row (back button and title) stays put while the price, chart, match hero, recent results, fixtures and league table scroll underneath — so a compact tile stays fully usable. The **Claude Code** widget got the same treatment: when several Claude sessions run at once, the running-sessions list now scrolls within the tile instead of overflowing it.
- **Your saved layout is preserved to the pixel.** Existing layouts, duplicated copies, tab-groups, saved presets and even shared preset codes are converted to the finer grid automatically the first time they load — every tile keeps its exact position and size, on every page.
- **With the minimal top bar, tiles can now rise level with the clock island.** The top strip beside the floating clock/weather pill is no longer reserved: the grid uses the full screen height, and only a tile that actually sits under the pill tucks its content just below it — so widgets at the pill's sides reach all the way to the top edge.
- **The clock island always keeps its distance from the widget beneath it.** With the minimal top bar, the floating clock/weather pill could end up sitting on top of a widget's header after you swiped to another page or restarted the dashboard — the "tuck under the pill" clearance was only recalculated for the page you were already looking at. It's now recomputed every time a page settles into view, so the top widget always clears the pill on every page, after every swipe and every restart.
- **The edit toolbar no longer buries your widgets — and you can drag it anywhere.** With the minimal top bar, entering Layout mode dropped a full-width editor panel over the whole top strip of the screen — exactly on top of the first row of tiles and their move/resize/hide buttons, making them impossible to reach. The panel is now a compact capsule that starts **collapsed to a slim bar** (Personalizza · Reimposta · Fine); expand it only when you need the presets, hidden-widget and top-bar sections. A grip handle on the left lets you **drag the whole toolbar with the mouse or your finger** to wherever it's out of your way — it always stays fully on-screen, and its position (and collapsed/expanded state) is remembered per device.
- **You can now reorder your pages.** In Layout mode, two new ‹ › buttons next to the page dots move the page you're looking at left or right — so "I want page 3 to become page 2" is two taps. The page follows you as it moves, and every widget on it stays exactly where it was.
- **Deleting a page can no longer make widgets "appear" on another page.** A widget living inside a tabbed tile kept a stale memory of the page it had been on *before* joining the tab. Deleting the tab's page then left that widget alive on the old page — suddenly popping up where you never put it, colliding with that page's tiles and shuffling their positions and sizes. Widgets in a deleted page's tabbed tiles are now removed with their page (restorable from the "+" palette like every removed widget), a widget's remembered page is kept truthful whenever it joins or moves with a tabbed tile, and a deleted page's internal grid is fully torn down instead of lingering. Together these stop the "deleted a page / imported a backup and my layout exploded" family of bugs.
- **Pages with duplicated widgets no longer mis-fit their height.** The row-height calculation ignored duplicated copies, so a page whose tallest tile was a duplicate stretched its rows and pushed that tile below the bottom edge (and pointed new widgets at the wrong free spot). Copies now count like every other tile, so those pages fit the screen exactly.
- **Adding a widget no longer shrinks and shuffles the whole page to make room.** If the free gap you'd left was even slightly smaller than the new widget's default size, the widget was silently pushed onto a new row below the screen — which compressed every tile on the page to fit the extra row. The new widget now shrinks itself into the gap you left (you can resize it afterwards); a new row is only added when the page genuinely has no usable space.
- **Resizing and dragging no longer randomly "snap back".** With more than one surface open (the Xeneon Edge screen plus a browser window, or the native app), a background settings sync could re-apply the saved layout in the middle of your drag or resize — killing the gesture and reverting the tile, which read as "I resized it and nothing happened". The live sync now waits until you close the layout editor before applying changes from other surfaces.
- **A widget sitting alone on a page can finally be made shorter.** When a single tile filled its whole page (the Weather widget was the usual victim), the grid stretched the row height without limit so the page always filled the screen — so shrinking the tile just made each row taller and it sprang straight back to full height, as if the resize did nothing. Now a lone tile at its normal size still fills the page exactly as before (so nothing looks different on a fresh install or after an update), but the moment you corner-resize it shorter it stays shorter, leaving free space below that you can drop another widget into. Pages holding several widgets are untouched — they keep filling the screen exactly.
- **A freshly reset dashboard can no longer erase your saved settings.** Reinstalling the native app (or clearing browser storage) starts that surface from a blank slate — and that blank surface could save its factory defaults over your real theme, pages and preferences before it ever read them from Xenon. Now every surface always *reads* your saved settings first and only ever saves after that merge, so a wiped app or browser picks your configuration back up instead of destroying it. (Your Deck layouts, API keys, watchlists, teams and feeds were already protected server-side.)

### 🎛 Deck — a real Stream Deck on your dashboard: readable editor, honest grid, hardware feel
- **The key editor is finally a studio, not a scroll.** Editing a key used to mean one narrow 460px column with ~15 stacked sections and tiny labels — and Save was at the very bottom. It's now a wide two-pane editor: your key's **live preview sits on the left and never leaves the screen** (before, it disappeared entirely on the Xeneon Edge itself), with saved key presets and the style clipboard right under it; the form on the right is split into three clear tabs — **Azioni** (type, tap/double/hold triggers, action steps, LED reaction), **Aspetto** (icon, colour/gradient, backdrop photo) and **Effetti** (label styling, tap feedback, ambient animation) — with bigger labels, one card per section, and a **Salva bar always docked at the bottom**. A new key opens on Azioni, an existing one on Aspetto. Every field, option and behavior is exactly the one you had — nothing was removed, and saved keys stay byte-identical.
- **The grid no longer drifts out of alignment.** Two real bugs made auto-fit occasionally disagree with what the screen drew — the JS measured the key well *including* its padding while the CSS square-cap maths uses the content box, and the JS assumed a fixed 10px gap while the real gap is 7/10/13px depending on key size. Both sides now compute on the same numbers (plus a half-pixel tolerance so a 1px resize can't flap the column count), so the keys the deck *says* fit are exactly the keys that *do* fit, at every tile size and key count. And tapping S/M/L (or toggling auto-fit) while editing now previews the exact fitted grid instantly — before, the editor snapped back to the stored canonical shape (e.g. 4×2 giant caps right after choosing "S") and only corrected itself once you left edit mode.
- **Edit mode you can read.** The edit toolbar is now two tidy rows — grid controls (key size, auto-fit, columns/rows, music dock) on one, the whole-device look (theme, shape, faceplate) on the other — each scrolling smoothly sideways on narrow tiles instead of wrapping into a cramped pile.
- **Edit mode you can touch.** Keys in edit mode now keep the exact same size as the live deck: the toolbar shrinks the key area, so cramming the full grid into it used to scale every cap (and its delete badge) down to fingernail size. The editor now shows the rows that fit at the real cap size — every placed key always stays reachable — and the now-playing dock steps aside while editing to give the grid its space back (the Musica pill still shows and toggles the setting).
- **It looks and feels like real hardware now.** Empty slots render as **unlit LCD keys** — dark moulded caps waiting to be assigned, exactly like a powered Stream Deck fresh out of the box — instead of dashed ghost outlines. Every press ends with a **specular glint**: a light band sweeps across the key's glass as it springs back under your finger, on top of the existing tactile depression and springy release. The chassis gained a machined edge light and a proper contact shadow so it reads as an object sitting on the dashboard. All of it is cheap (transform/opacity one-shots) and fully disabled by Performance Mode and "reduce motion".

### 📈 Borsa — live stock, index and crypto tracking with charts, favorites and alerts
- **A new Borsa widget for the dashboard.** Add it from the "+" palette and it shows a live watchlist — each row with the name, price, day change (green up / red down) in a tinted pill and a little sparkline of today's move. Tap any row and it opens a full detail view with a clean gradient price chart you can switch between **1 day, 1 week, 1 month and 1 year** (with a hover crosshair showing the exact price and time), plus the day range, the 52-week range, the exchange and whether the market is open.
- **Add stocks by searching, not by guessing the ticker.** Just type a company name — "Apple", "Facebook", "Tesla", "FTSE MIB" — and pick the right result from a live dropdown (it shows the symbol, the exchange and the type). No more silent "nothing happened" when you didn't know the exact code: every symbol you add always appears in the list, and anything the market can't price yet is shown clearly so you can remove it with one tap.
- **Works out of the box, no signup.** By default it reads from Yahoo Finance with **no API key**, and it covers what an Italian user actually wants: **Borsa Italiana** (`FTSEMIB.MI`, `ENI.MI`, …), world indices, US stocks, crypto (`BTC-EUR`) and currencies — all in one place. Want richer or more official data? You can paste an optional free **Twelve Data** or **Finnhub** key in Settings; without one, everything still works.
- **Favorites with rise/fall alerts.** Add any symbol to your watchlist straight from the widget. When one of your favorites moves sharply during the day (past a threshold you set — 2% by default), Xenon pops a discreet toast and flashes your RGB lighting, so you notice a big move without staring at the screen. Alerts respect the master Notifiche switch and never repeat the same move twice in a day.
- **A scrolling ticker bar.** A new opt-in **ticker** streams your stocks (and, as they arrive, football scores and news) across the bottom edge of the screen — configurable to the top, or hidden, with an adjustable speed. It's built to be glanceable and calm: it **freezes automatically in Performance and Game mode** (and while a modal is open or the dashboard is idle), so it never competes with a game for the GPU.
- **Ask Xenon about it, by voice or text.** The assistant can now answer "how is Apple doing", "how's the FTSE MIB today", "read me my watchlist" and "add Tesla to my stocks" — it reads the live prices and can add favorites for you, in whatever language you're speaking.
- **Kept deliberately light.** No new dependencies, charts drawn as plain SVG, quotes fetched only while a dashboard is open and pushed over the existing live stream, everything cached and rate-limited. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH). *(A News feed for the same widget/ticker is coming next.)*

### ⚽ Calcio — follow your teams with fixtures, results, live scores and league tables
- **A new Calcio widget for the dashboard.** Add it from the "+" palette, follow your clubs, and each row shows the club crest, its latest result (win/draw/loss colour-coded) and its next fixture at a glance. Tap a team to open a full detail view: a match hero (the live or upcoming game with both crests and the score), the last handful of results, the upcoming fixtures, and the **live league table** with your team highlighted.
- **Follow whole competitions too, not just clubs.** Search "Champions League", "Serie A", "World Cup", "Europa League", "Premier League" (and the other top leagues and cups) and follow the *competition* itself — its row shows the next match and latest result across the whole tournament, and its detail view gives the recent results, upcoming fixtures and the full standings. Great for a tournament like the World Cup where you want the whole bracket, not one team.
- **Add by searching, not by knowing a code.** Type a club or competition name — "Napoli", "Arsenal", "Champions League" — and pick it from a live dropdown that tells you whether it's a club or a competition. Everything you follow always appears in the list.
- **Works out of the box, no signup.** By default it reads from TheSportsDB with **no API key** — fixtures, results, crests and standings for Serie A and every major league. Following your teams live? Paste an optional **TheSportsDB Premium** key in Settings and the widget shows **live scores while matches are being played**; without one, everything else still works.
- **Goal & full-time alerts.** When a team you follow scores or a match ends, Xenon pops a discreet toast and flashes your RGB lighting, so you catch the moment without watching the screen. Alerts respect the master Notifiche switch and never repeat, and never spam you on startup.
- **On the ticker too.** Turn on the football source and your teams' live scores and next fixtures scroll across the ticker bar alongside your stocks — with live matches highlighted.
- **Ask Xenon about it, by voice or text.** The assistant can now answer "how did Napoli do", "when does Inter play next", "read me the Serie A table" — it reads the live fixtures, results and standings, in whatever language you're speaking.
- **Kept deliberately light.** No new dependencies, crests loaded lazily with a clean initials fallback, data fetched only while a dashboard is open and pushed over the existing live stream, everything cached and rate-limited. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 📰 News — a live headline stream from the outlets and topics you follow
- **A new News widget for the dashboard.** Add it from the "+" palette and it shows a single, time-sorted stream of headlines merged from everything you follow — each with the outlet, how long ago it was published and (when available) a thumbnail. Tap a headline to open the article.
- **Follow outlets and topics.** Open the manage panel and search a curated list of major outlets (ANSA, la Repubblica, Corriere, Il Post, Sky TG24, Gazzetta, BBC, The Guardian, The Verge, TechCrunch and more), or type any subject — "tecnologia", "elezioni", "AI", your city — to follow it as a topic. Your followed feeds show as removable chips.
- **Works out of the box, no signup.** By default it reads outlet **RSS feeds** and, for topics, **Google News** in your language — no API key. An optional **NewsData.io** key (Settings → News) enriches topic results with more articles and images; without it everything still works.
- **On the ticker too.** Turn on the news source and your latest headlines scroll across the ticker bar alongside your stocks and football.
- **Ask Xenon about it.** The assistant can now answer "what's in the news", "any news about AI", "latest headlines" — it reads your followed feeds or fetches a topic on demand, by voice or text.
- **Kept deliberately light.** No new dependencies (a small hand-rolled RSS reader, like the calendar's ICS parser), thumbnails loaded lazily with a graceful fallback, article links opened only after an https check, data fetched only while a dashboard is open and pushed over the existing live stream. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH). *This completes the Borsa / Calcio / News trio for the widget and ticker.*

### ⚙️ Settings, reorganized — find things faster, and support the project
- **A sidebar you can actually scan.** The settings categories are now grouped under clear section labels — your personal preferences first (General, Appearance, Background, Notifications, Lock screen), then **Widgets** (Weather; Stocks, Football & News; External calendars), then **Integrations** (Xenon AI, Lighting, Smart Home, Spotify, Streaming, Browser, Second screen, Remote control) and **System** (Performance; Widgets & sharing). The modal is now titled plainly "Settings", with a subtitle that says what lives inside.
- **A new "General" page.** Everyday preferences — language, clock format, first day of the week, page-swipe gestures, startup, backup and the tutorial — moved out of Appearance into their own General page, so Appearance is purely about how the dashboard looks. The language picker got its own labelled setting instead of hiding inside the theme presets.
- **Stocks, Football & News untangled.** What used to be one endless wall of controls is now four tidy cards — Ticker bar, Stocks, Football, News — each with its own heading and explanation. OBS moved in with the rest of Streaming instead of being a lone category.
- **A proper "Support Xenon" page.** A new heart-marked entry in the sidebar opens a warm support page: a clear "buy me a coffee" hero explaining that Xenon is free, ad-free and built by one person, a Discord card inviting you into the community, and quick links to star the project or report a bug. The always-visible donate/Discord pills in the sidebar footer stay.
- **Clearer wording and more breathing room.** Group titles and hints were rewritten to say what a setting actually does, spacing between cards was opened up on regular displays (the Xeneon Edge keeps its dense tuning), and the external-calendars entry now sits with the other widgets instead of dangling at the bottom. Everything localised in all 10 languages.

### 🎬 OBS widget — works with a local OBS out of the box
- **The OBS tile no longer needs you to type an address.** If OBS is running on the same PC, just add the OBS widget and it connects on its own — the live scene preview and your scene list appear, and the Go live / Record controls work, without opening Settings to fill in the host. (Set a host, port or password in Settings → Streaming only for a remote OBS or one that uses a WebSocket password.) Previously, leaving the host blank still let Record work but left the preview black and the scene list empty with a "Configure OBS in Settings" note — that mismatch is fixed.

### 🎮 Vitals — game-style self-care meters that remind you to drink, eat, move and rest your eyes
- **A new Vitals widget for the dashboard.** Add it from the "+" palette and you get a little retro game HUD living inside a glass tile: pixel-art sprites and chunky segmented bars for **Hydration 💧, Energy 🍗, Stamina 🚶 and Focus 👀** (plus an optional Posture meter) that slowly drain the longer you sit at the PC. The HUD adapts to its tile — shrink it and the rows compact themselves down to a tiny at-a-glance strip.
- **Tap a vital and it coaches you first.** Tapping a bar (or a top-bar chip, or a reminder toast) opens a small card that explains what that meter tracks and what actually helps — "drink a glass of water now, don't wait until you're thirsty", the 20-20-20 eye rule, and so on. Then *you* decide: hit **"Fatto! +100"** once you've done it and the bar springs back to full with a pixel burst and a floating "+100" — like picking up a health pack. All the explanations are localised in EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH.
- **It nags you the fun way.** When a vital drops below 25% (and again at zero) a game-style toast pops up — "Stamina drained, stand up and take a walk 🚶" — and tapping the toast opens the same coaching card. Reminders respect the master Notifiche switch, have their own toggle, and each threshold fires once per drain, so it nudges without pestering.
- **Level up your self-care.** Every refill earns +25 XP toward a little **LV badge** on the widget, complete with a LEVEL UP! toast — a tiny nudge that makes looking after yourself feel like a combo streak. The header also shows a beating pixel heart and how long you've been at the PC this session, and a **"Today" ribbon** at the bottom collects one coloured pixel per refill — your self-care combo history for the day (the coaching card shows each vital's daily count too). It resets at midnight with everything else.
- **Mini indicators in the top bar.** An opt-in toggle puts tiny pixel chips — icon plus a micro bar — right next to the clock and weather, so your vitals stay glanceable even without the widget on screen (they follow the minimal-topbar island too). Tap a chip to refill on the spot.
- **Yours to tune.** Each vital can be switched on or off individually, with its own drain interval (water every 45 minutes, food every 3 hours, a 20-20-20-style eye break…) in Settings → Notifiche → Vitals. Levels are computed from real timestamps, so a reload or restart never resets your bars — refilling on one screen carries over to the others — and **every new day starts fresh**: at midnight all bars quietly refill, so an always-on Xeneon Edge never greets you with a wall of zero alarms in the morning.
- **Turning the PC on is a fresh start too.** The meters only measure time you actually spend at the PC: hours the machine was powered off no longer count as neglect. Booting up (or restarting the Xenon engine) refills every bar — previously a late-night session that ran past midnight meant waking up to five empty, alarming meters.
- **Kept deliberately light.** No new dependencies: the sprites are inline pixel-art SVG, the decay math rides the existing 1-second clock tick with change-detected DOM writes, animations are cheap transform/opacity one-shots that respect "reduce motion". Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 👾 Bit — the pixel guardian that roasts you into taking care of yourself
- **Meet Bit.** An opt-in 8-bit tamagotchi (Settings → Notifiche → Vitals → Bit) that lives in a corner of the dashboard and mirrors your Vitals: green and bouncy when you're doing fine, worried when a meter runs low, furious — shaking, brows down, steam puffs — when one hits zero, and a floating ghost when *everything* is dead. Tap him for a quick menu: your worst meters with one-tap access to the coaching card, a **"Truce 30 min"** snooze and a **"Quiet for today"** mute.
- **He roasts you — and never repeats himself.** When a vital sits at zero, Bit starts talking: a typewriter speech bubble plus a toast, drawn from a bank of over 250 hand-written lines in Italian and English ("Hydration: 0%. You are officially freeze-dried.") with a no-repeat shuffle so you hear the whole repertoire before any line comes back. Three tones to pick from — **Gentle, Sarcastic or Savage** — and the meaner tiers only ever *add* lines on top of the kinder ones.
- **Ignore him and things escalate.** Every step is its own opt-in, and it's a ladder: after ~5 minutes at zero the dashboard **drains its colour** and retro glitch pulses flicker across it; at ~8 minutes a full **CRT "GAME OVER" screen** takes over — blinking pixel title, the roast of the moment, a green **FIX IT** button and an "INSERT SELF-CARE TO CONTINUE" footer; at 10 minutes Bit **jumps out of the dashboard onto your real monitors** as a pixel popup in the corner (all screens at once if three or more vitals are dead); at 15 minutes he can **minimize every window** (30-second warning first — nothing is ever closed); and at 20 minutes, as the declared nuclear option, he can **lock the PC** after a dramatic 60-second countdown (the normal Windows lock — log back in and nothing is lost).
- **Strict but never dumb.** The PC-invading steps only fire when you're *actually at the PC* — a new system-idle probe checks real keyboard/mouse input, because tapping the Xeneon isn't proof you're at your desk — and every opt-in is re-checked server-side with hard cooldowns, so nothing can act beyond what you enabled. During games Bit holds a **truce** (on by default): he stays silent and hands-off, but keeps receipts and greets you after the match ("You were racking up points. Your Hydration was writing its will."). Refill a meter and he switches instantly to praise, chiptune fanfare included.
- **Reliably there when you enabled him.** Bit now appears as soon as the dashboard picks up your saved settings — previously, on surfaces whose browser storage gets reset by a PC restart, an enabled Bit stayed invisible until you re-toggled him in Settings. He also waits for the boot handshake before judging your meters, so switching the PC on never greets you with the whole escalation ladder at once.
- **His rage can spill onto your RGB lights.** New opt-in (Settings → Notifiche → Vitals → Bit → "Fai lampeggiare i LED quando si arrabbia"): when a meter hits zero and Bit loses his temper, your RGB lighting flashes red for a few seconds — the anger jumps off the screen and into the room. Off by default, one tap to enable, and completely silent if you have no lighting configured. It rides the existing event-flash engine, so it costs nothing until it fires.
- **Pixel by design, light by design.** Bit is always 8-bit — Press Start 2P titles, VT323 speech, crisp sprite — whatever theme you run, and he fits the Pixel Retro skin like he was born there. Zero new dependencies: sprites are inline SVG, sounds are a tiny WebAudio square-wave synth, the idle probe rides the existing persistent PowerShell worker, and with Bit disabled not a single timer runs.
- **You decide how fast he escalates.** A new **Escalation timing** block under Settings → Notifiche → Vitals → Bit lets you set, in minutes, how long a vital must sit at zero before each rung fires — dashboard decay, the GAME OVER screen, the monitor popup, minimize-all and the PC lock. If Bit felt too aggressive (Focus, for instance, empties in just 25 minutes), push the invasive steps out to 45, 60 or 90 minutes; the defaults (5 / 8 / 10 / 15 / 20) are unchanged, so nothing shifts unless you touch it.
- **Fixed: Bit could over-react to a stale meter right after a reboot.** A vital's "how long at zero" was read straight from its last-refill timestamp, so on a fresh boot an old stamp could look like the meter had been dead for *hours* — skipping the whole ladder and jumping straight to minimizing your windows or locking the PC even when everything was actually full (and the dashboard could get stuck desaturated). Bit now ignores any meter that's about to be refilled by the daily/boot reset, so the escalation only ever starts from a real, present-tense zero, and a refill always restores the colour.
- **When Bit acts on your PC, he says so — out loud, on the PC.** The messages that accompany a minimize-all or a PC lock now clearly own the action ("That was me: windows minimized." / "PC locked, courtesy of Bit."), with a much bigger, richer set of lines across all three tones. And the **lock now flashes a labelled "BIT // XENON VITALS" popup on every monitor a few seconds before the screen locks**, so it's never a mysterious Windows lockout — you always know it was him and why.
- **Bit now speaks all ten dashboard languages.** His entire repertoire — every roast, warning and bit of praise, 120+ lines each — was written natively in **Italian, English, Korean, Japanese, Simplified Chinese, Spanish, French, German, Portuguese and Russian**, not machine-translated word-for-word: the jokes and idioms are adapted so they actually land in each language, while keeping the same three tones. Previously anyone not on Italian or English heard Bit in English; now he talks to you in yours.
- **The colour-drain is now gradual — all the way to black & white.** Instead of snapping to a fixed grey, the dashboard now loses its colour *progressively* the longer a vital sits at zero: a faint tint at first, deepening minute by minute until, if you keep ignoring it, the whole screen goes full monochrome. The instant you refill, the colour eases straight back.
- **Fixed: Bit's monitor popup was appearing blank.** The pixel popup on your real monitor showed its "BIT // XENON VITALS" header and sprite but *no roast* — an empty card. When multi-language support added a font option, the popup's body-text font accidentally shared a name with it and got quietly discarded, so every line silently failed to draw. The roast now renders again.
- **Fixed: Bit's red LED flash never fired.** With "Fai lampeggiare i LED quando si arrabbia" enabled, the anger flash did nothing unless your RGB lighting happened to already be active for another reason — the flash was thrown away whenever the lighting bridge wasn't already connected. It now brings the lighting up on demand and paints the flash the moment it's ready, exactly like it was meant to.

### 🖥️ A real Xenon app — full-screen on the Xeneon Edge, no browser or iCUE needed
- **Xenon now installs as a native Windows app.** Instead of opening a browser tab or embedding the dashboard inside iCUE, there's now a proper full-screen app that takes over the Xeneon Edge like a dedicated device screen — borderless, no title bar, edge to edge. It starts by itself at login and puts the same dashboard you already know right on the panel.
- **It finds the Edge and stays there.** The app detects the Xeneon Edge among your monitors (by its 2560×720 panel) and pins itself to it. If Windows reshuffles your displays, you unplug and replug the Edge, or the PC wakes from sleep, it quietly moves back to the right screen on its own. If the Edge isn't connected yet, it waits and hops over the moment it appears.
- **A tray icon to control it — and nothing cluttering your taskbar.** A small Xenon icon sits in the system tray with Show, Hide, Restart and Exit — hiding or exiting the app never stops the dashboard itself, which keeps running for the browser and iCUE. The app stays out of the main taskbar and Alt-Tab, running quietly in the background on the Edge; you drive it entirely from that tray icon.
- **Exactly the same dashboard — never a second copy.** The app doesn't ship its own UI: it loads the very same dashboard from your local Xenon, so every feature, theme and future update shows up here with zero extra work. A brief branded splash waits for Xenon to be ready, then hands over to the live dashboard.
- **External links open in your real browser.** Buttons like Support the project, Community Discord, Report a bug and the AI setup links now open in your default web browser, instead of doing nothing or trying to load inside the kiosk. The app window itself always stays on the dashboard — any link to an outside site is handed off to the browser, so the full-screen kiosk can never wander off onto a web page.
- **The app keeps itself up to date — one tap.** When a new signed version is available, the native app shows a small "update available" toast on the dashboard; tap it and it downloads, installs and relaunches on its own. Nothing happens without your tap, and updates are cryptographically signed, so the app only ever installs a genuine Xenon build.
- **Install the native app straight from iCUE — no reinstall dance.** If you set Xenon up as an iCUE widget (or open it in a browser), a compact **"Try the native app · Beta"** pill now sits in the Settings header; tap it and a small panel explains why the dedicated app is nicer — full-screen edge-to-edge, sharper, independent of iCUE, auto-starting on the Edge — with a one-tap **Install** button and an honest "it's in beta" note. It's tucked into the header so it never crowds the settings menu, and it only appears where it's useful: running the native app already, the pill simply isn't there.
- **Swipe up to peek at the desktop — iPhone-style.** In the native app, a quick swipe up from the bottom of the screen slides the kiosk away and reveals your Windows desktop on the Edge, so you can reach a file or a setting without closing anything. What stays behind is a small, rounded **"return to Xenon" button** floating at the top-centre of the screen — comfortable to hit with a finger, with the desktop and taskbar completely usable around it. Tap it and the dashboard springs straight back to full-screen. It now works reliably by finger: on a touchscreen Windows 11 claims edge swipes for its own gestures (taskbar, Start, notification centre), so a native install run as Administrator reserves the touchscreen edge swipe for Xenon — the installer sets the one policy Windows actually honours and restarts Explorer so it applies immediately, no sign-out needed (uninstalling gives Windows its gestures back; mouse, keyboard and the taskbar itself are unaffected). The gesture also listens a little above the very edge, so starting the flick a finger-width above the bottom works even on installs that skipped the admin step. The first time the app runs it shows a small tip explaining the gesture, and a new **Settings → General → Native app** switch lets you turn it off entirely. It's native-app only (the browser and iCUE surfaces are unaffected), it never fires while you're editing the layout or scrolling a list, and the app quietly parks its "keep me on the Edge" watchdog while you're on the desktop so it never yanks itself back up mid-task. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Touching the Edge no longer steals your mouse.** Windows moves the system cursor to every touchscreen tap — so tapping the dashboard mid-game yanked the pointer onto the Edge. In the native app the cursor now snaps straight back to where it was on your main screen the moment your finger lifts: tap a song, mute the mic, flip a page — your mouse never leaves the game. Real mouse clicks on the dashboard are untouched, and if you ever *want* the old behavior there's a "Keep mouse on its screen" switch in the tray menu (on by default, remembered across launches).
- **…and it no longer steals your game's focus either.** Tapping the dashboard used to activate the kiosk window, so the game behind you lost focus — full-screen games could even minimize to the desktop. While a game is detected, the native app now makes itself un-stealable: tap, swipe and slide all you want, the game stays front and focused. Typing still just works — tap the AI chat, notes or a search box and the keyboard behaves exactly as before, then the focus hops back to the game the moment you leave the field. Automatic (it follows the same game detection that pauses ambient effects), with a "Keep games focused" switch in the tray if you ever want it off. Together these two make the Edge genuinely game-safe — and it's a native-app exclusive: the stock iCUE dashboard, a browser tab and the iCUE iFrame all still teleport your cursor and take the game's focus on every touch, because only a real native window can tell Windows how to treat it.

### 🧰 One always-on engine behind every surface
- **The dashboard is simply there.** Xenon's local engine starts automatically and invisibly when you log in — no terminal, no window to keep around — and serves the dashboard to every surface at once: the browser tab, the iCUE iframe widget and the new native app all show the same live Xenon, always in sync.
- **It runs in *your* session — on purpose.** During the beta the engine briefly ran as a Windows system service, and that quietly broke the features that touch your desktop: Deck keys that open apps and websites did nothing, the media panel stopped seeing what's playing, hotkey keys and screen capture went dead. Windows isolates services from your screen, apps and audio — so the engine now deliberately runs inside your login session, where all of that works. If a beta install left the old service behind, running the installer once removes it automatically and everything springs back to life.
- **The installer asks how you want to use Xenon.** On setup you now choose **Native app** or **iCUE widget**. Both set up the same background engine; picking Native also installs the full-screen kiosk app, while iCUE installs nothing extra and just points you at the dashboard URL to add inside iCUE. Either way you can switch later from the dashboard.
- **Picking Native ends with the app on screen — not a browser tab.** The installer (and the one-tap install from Settings) now launches the freshly installed full-screen app as its final step, which also arms its start-at-login. The browser only opens when you chose iCUE mode or the native app couldn't be installed, so a Native setup never dumps you in a browser you didn't ask for.
- **Running the installer again is now safe.** Re-running INSTALL.bat used to be able to leave you with a black screen and no dashboard at all: the old backend takes a few seconds to fully shut down, and a replacement started inside that window crashed on the still-occupied port. The installer now waits for the old backend and its port to actually clear before starting the new one, and the native app's splash screen only hands over to the dashboard after the backend answers twice in a row — so it can no longer latch onto a dying server and get stuck on black.
- **Clean install and removal.** The one-click installer sets everything up (and ensures the app's web runtime is present); uninstalling removes it tidily and never touches your notes, events, settings or other data.

### 🧱 One codebase behind four surfaces
- **A feature added once appears everywhere.** Under the hood Xenon is now organised as a single workspace with a shared core, so a change made once to the dashboard shows up in the browser, the iCUE iframe, the native app and the native iCUE widget without being copied around. It's invisible day to day — it just means fixes and new features land consistently across every way you use Xenon. (The native iCUE widget remains in development.)

### 👆 Swipe between pages — now optional
- **Turn page-swiping on or off.** A new **Settings → Appearance → Navigation** switch lets you disable swipe- and drag-to-change-page if you'd rather only move between dashboard pages with the page dots — handy on a busy touchscreen where an accidental swipe would flip the page. It's on by default, and the dots and keyboard arrows keep working either way. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 💡 Lighting — four new effects, your own palettes, more lights, and fixes across every provider
- **Four new ambient animations.** Alongside Solid, Breathing and Rainbow, your lights can now play **Wave** (a rainbow that physically scrolls across the LEDs of your Corsair strips, fans and coolers — bulbs get the classic hue cycle), **Aurora** (a slow northern-lights drift through greens, blues and purples), **Candle** (a warm, organic flame flicker), and **Palette** (see below). Every moving style now has a **speed slider**, Breathing and Candle have their own colour, and the per-device modes gain Aurora and Candle too (Wave and Palette stay global — per device they would render identically to Rainbow). Same efficiency contract as before: the render loop only exists while a moving style is actually painting, most ticks cost nothing thanks to on-change writes, and idle overhead stays zero.
- **Your colours, in motion: the Palette style.** Pick **2 to 5 colours of your own** in a new in-page palette editor (add, remove, or tap any swatch to recolour it) and your lights blend through them in a loop — tricolore for match night, your team's colours, a sunset. On per-LED Corsair devices the palette paints as a **moving gradient across the LEDs**; bulbs and lamps blend through the stops in sync.
- **Event flashes now have a duration.** Timer, notification and reminder flashes each get a **0.5–10 s slider** next to their colour and style — a long red pulse for a finished timer, a blink-and-gone for notifications.
- **Two new light families — and a bridge into your smart home.** **Yeelight** (Xiaomi Wi-Fi bulbs/strips, LAN Control) joins the network scan alongside Govee and LIFX. And if you use the **Home Assistant** integration, every colour light HA manages — IKEA, Zigbee, Tuya, anything — can now follow your dashboard's colours and effects too: press *Search* and your HA lights appear as devices, no extra token or setup, riding the connection you already configured. **OpenRGB** returns as well for power users (ASUS Aura, MSI, RAM, motherboards…), tucked into a collapsed *Advanced* group: add it by IP with its SDK server running — it is never auto-scanned, and Corsair devices are always left to iCUE.
- **Philips Hue: ready for the future.** The bridge now speaks Hue's **current API** (the one new bridges are moving to) with a self-signed-certificate-aware secure channel, and **falls back automatically** to the classic API on older bridges — no re-pairing, nothing to configure, same button-press setup.
- **Xenon AI drives the new effects.** *"metti l'aurora sulle luci"*, *"candle mode"*, *"cycle my lights through red, white and green"* — a new `set_animation` ability lets the assistant set the style, colour, speed and even the palette colours, by voice or chat, in your language.
- **Fixed — WLED strips no longer switch off when the dashboard lets go.** Turning the bridge off (or exiting an effect) now **restores the state your strip was in before** — the preset that was running, or its previous on/off and brightness — instead of always going dark. The strip's LED count is also re-read periodically, so re-flashing a strip to a different length no longer confuses the album gradient.
- **Fixed — network scan can no longer mislabel devices as Nanoleaf.** The scanner now requires a real Nanoleaf answer before claiming a device on that port, so another service on the same port can't swallow your colour writes silently.
- **Fixed — a wedged iCUE can no longer stall the lighting engine.** The release path (handing your LEDs back to iCUE) now has the same hard timeout as every other SDK call, so an unresponsive iCUE service degrades gracefully instead of freezing the bridge.
- **Cleanup — the never-shipped "volume flash" effect is gone from the AI's vocabulary** (it had been a silent no-op); the album-cover effect (`musicAlbum`) is properly exposed instead. Old saved settings keep loading unchanged.
- All of it lands on **every surface at once** — browser, iCUE iframe and the native app share the same Settings → Illuminazione hub — and it's fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH), covered by new unit tests (effect math, per-provider protocol builders, the previously missing OpenRGB parser test).

### 🏝️ Minimal top bar — a second, ultra-clean chrome for the dashboard
- **Choose how much chrome you want.** A new **Settings → Appearance → Top bar** switch offers two styles: **Full** (the classic glass bar) and **Minimal**, which floats the controls over the edges so your **widgets fill the whole screen, top to bottom**.
- **In Minimal, the actions move to the screen edges.** Lock, Focus and Xenon dock into a slim glass rail on the **left edge**; Layout, Settings, App (and your app favorites) into a matching rail on the **right edge** — vertically centred, icon-only, touch-sized. Each rail has a small chevron pull: tap it and the rail slides away leaving just the tab, tap again to bring it back. **The rails start tucked away** so your widgets have the whole screen, and **whether each one is open is now remembered by Xenon itself** — the choice sticks across restarts and even a fresh reinstall, so the native app on the Xeneon Edge always comes back exactly the way you left it instead of popping the rails open on its own.
- **Widgets reclaim the full height.** Because the minimal chrome floats instead of taking a bar, the dashboard grid runs edge-to-edge — the left- and right-most tiles now stretch the entire height of the display. Only the tile directly beneath the clock is trimmed slightly at the top so the capsule sits in clear space above it, never covering a header.
- **Clock, date, weather and page dots become one tidy island.** A single floating capsule at the top centre shows the time, today's date, the tappable weather chip and the dashboard page dots — each set off by a hairline so it reads as an organised row, not a cramped huddle. Everything you glanced at the big bar for, in a compact, legible island.
- **A cleaner time, everywhere.** The AM/PM marker lost its heavy bordered box — in both the full and minimal bars it now rides the top of the digits as a quiet, letter-spaced superscript, letting the clock breathe.
- **Nothing is lost, everything still works.** The buttons are the same controls, just re-docked — the Xenon button keeps its accent glow, the settings update dot still appears, the weather chip still opens the full forecast, and switching to Full restores the classic bar exactly. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **The layout editor is true‑to‑life in Minimal too.** While you edit, the grid stays exactly where it runs (it isn't nudged down to make room for the toolbar), so a tile you shorten shows live whether it will tuck under the clock island — what you see is what you get. The editing toolbar floats over the top instead, and the edge rails step aside while editing so you can grab every tile's move grip and resize corner right up to the screen edge.
- **Adding a widget is now a clean centered dialog.** The "+" (add a widget, or add one as a tab) opens a tidy centered modal with a title and a close button instead of a small pop‑out that hung off the button — so it's always fully visible, never clipped by the toolbar or a screen edge, and dismisses with the ✕, a tap outside, or Esc. Same categorised, icon'd list as before.

### 🔔 Notifications reborn — a top heads-up, and a Dynamic Island in Minimal
- **Notifications now arrive at the top, like your phone.** Every in-app notice — a calendar reminder, a finished timer, a Windows or Discord ping, a stock alert, an update prompt — now drops in from the **top centre** of the screen and springs open, instead of sliding up from the bottom corner. It's where your eyes already are, and it reads instantly.
- **In Minimal top bar, it becomes a Dynamic Island.** When you're running the Minimal chrome, an arriving notification takes the place of the floating clock/date/weather capsule: the little island gently recedes and the notification **grows straight out of it** — a compact pill unfolding into the full card — then folds back into a capsule as it leaves and the clock slides back in. Apple-style, right on the Xeneon Edge.
- **Same glass, same gestures.** It's the same premium liquid-glass card with the source's own accent and icon, and every interaction you already had still works: hover or press-and-hold to pause it while you read, and swipe it sideways to flick it away. Newest sits at the top; motion is fully calmed under "reduce motion".
- **Notifications can now play a sound.** A new **Suoni di notifica** toggle in **Settings → Notifiche** gives every pop-up a short, soft cue — a gentle rise when a notification lands, a bright three-note chime when a timer finishes, a two-note fall for a warning, and so on — plus it now controls the calendar reminder's alarm. Each cue is synthesized on the fly, so there are no sound files to download and it works offline. Routine confirmations (a saved setting, "memory cleared") stay silent on purpose, and the toggle is separate from Bit's own 8-bit voice so you can tune notifications and the guardian pet independently. On by default, and it follows the master notifications switch. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🎙️ "Hey Xenon" — open the voice assistant hands-free
- **Say "Hey Xenon" and the voice chat opens — no tapping.** A new opt-in toggle in **Settings → Xenon AI** turns on a local wake word: while the dashboard is on screen, saying "Hey Xenon" opens the same voice session as the 🎙 button. It understands accented pronunciations too ("ehi zenon" works just as well), and it stays out of the way while a voice chat is already running.
- **100% private and offline, off by default.** Detection runs entirely on your PC with the same local Whisper engine the voice chat can already use — no cloud service, no account, no API key, and **no audio ever leaves the computer or gets stored**. The listener only runs while a dashboard is actually open, and muting your microphone silences it like everything else. If Whisper isn't installed yet, the settings row offers a one-tap download.
- **Genuinely lightweight.** A tiny audio gate listens for short spoken phrases and ignores everything else — long conversations, music or streams cost nothing, so the wake word never turns into a background CPU drain. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🧩 Widget SDK — anyone can now build a Xenon widget (beta)
- **The dashboard is now a platform: third parties can build widgets for it.** A widget is just a small folder — a `manifest.json` plus an HTML page — dropped into `server/data/widgets`. Enable the feature in **Settings → Widgets & sharing**, add the new **Custom widget** tile from the "+" palette, and pick which installed widget that tile shows. You can add several Custom widget tiles, each hosting a different community widget, and a built-in **"Install example"** button sets up a working reference widget (live clock, CPU/GPU/RAM readout, media keys) with one tap.
- **Sandboxed and permission-gated by design.** Community widgets run in an isolated sandbox with **no network access and no reach into the dashboard**: they can't call the internet, can't read your settings, and can't touch anything outside their own tile. Everything goes through a small, versioned message bridge — a widget only *sees* the data streams you approve (system sensors, now playing, volume, status) and can only *do* the low-risk actions you allow (media keys, volume, mic mute, lighting, open a link), each one re-checked by the server like a Deck key. Before a widget first renders, a clear permission dialog shows exactly what it requested — with a plain-words reminder to only install widgets from people you trust. Everything is off by default.
- **Documented and versioned from day one.** The full developer guide — package format, sandbox rules, the complete bridge protocol and the security model — lives in `docs/WIDGET_SDK.md`, and the message contract carries an API version so future Xenon releases stay compatible with existing widgets. It's the first step of the Xenon widget ecosystem (a shared gallery comes next); the feature is marked beta and fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Widgets can now talk to the internet — safely, through Xenon.** A widget that declares the servers it needs (say, a crypto-price API or your NAS) can ask Xenon to fetch for it: the permission dialog lists every server by name before you allow it, the sandbox itself stays completely offline, and Xenon only relays requests to the approved hosts — with hard limits (https for anything public, no redirects, bounded sizes, rate-limited) and loopback permanently unreachable. This unlocks real data widgets (prices, feeds, home devices) without ever handing widget code a network connection.
- **Widgets can plug into the Deck.** A widget package can now ship **Deck macros** — named multi-step actions (e.g. "Quiet mode" = mute volume + mute mic) that appear in the Deck key editor under a "Widgets" category, restricted to the same low-risk action set and re-checked by the server on every press — and **publish live states** that any Deck key can reflect via the new "Reflect a widget state" binding, lighting up exactly like a Streamer.bot smart key. The bundled example widget now publishes a "playing" state you can bind a key to.
- **Widgets can receive local events (webhooks).** Any local tool — Streamer.bot, AutoHotkey, a script — can push an event to a widget with a simple `POST http://127.0.0.1:3030/sdk/hook/<widget>/<event>`; the widget receives it live only if you granted that event in its permission dialog. Together with published states, this turns a few lines of widget code into custom smart Deck keys driven by anything on your PC.

### 🎨 Share your look — export & import themes and page layouts
- **Send your theme or a dashboard page to a friend with a link.** A new **Share & Import** panel in **Settings → Widgets & sharing** lets you export your current **theme** (colours, appearance, surface look) or the current **page layout** (its widgets and arrangement) as a compact, self-contained **link** or a downloadable **.json file**. They copy it, you paste it, done — no accounts, no cloud.
- **Import in one step.** Paste a preset link or code (or pick a .json file) in the same panel and it applies instantly — an imported theme recolours the dashboard, an imported page is added as a new page. Opening a preset link on the machine running your dashboard jumps straight into the import dialog. Everything is re-checked on the way in, so an imported theme or page can only ever change colours and widget arrangement — it can never carry anything that runs on your PC.
- **Choose which page to share, and see exactly what's going out.** When you have more than one page, **Export page** now opens a picker listing every page — with its widget count, the one you're viewing marked "current", and empty pages disabled — so you export the one you mean instead of whatever happened to be on screen. The share dialog then shows a clear **Theme** / **Page** label and the name of what you're sharing.
- **A Community Hub built around sharing.** The Community Hub on the website now explains the export → share → import flow in three steps and links straight to the **Xenon Discord**, where you and other users can swap themes and layouts. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Share your Deck profiles too — safely.** A fully programmed Deck profile (keys, folders, styling, photo faces and all its actions) can now travel the same way: a **Share** button next to each profile in the Deck's profile menu, and an **Export Deck profile** button in Settings → Widgets & sharing → Share & Import. The recipient pastes the link or picks the file, and — because a Deck profile *contains actions* — gets a clear **review step first**: what the profile is called, how many keys it has, and exactly **which actions it contains** ("Open app ×2, Webhook ×1, …"), with a plain-words reminder to only import from people they trust. Every imported profile is rebuilt from scratch through Xenon's own validators — unknown or malformed actions are simply dropped, nothing can auto-run on import, and each action is re-checked by the server the moment its key is tapped, exactly like a key you created yourself. Profiles with photo key-faces are shared as a file (they're too big for a link), with a one-tap **"Share without images"** alternative; importing with no Deck on the dashboard saves the profile to your Deck presets instead of failing. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 💬 Join the community — Xenon is getting a Discord
- **There's now a Discord community for Xenon.** A place to share your themes and layouts, swap ideas, ask for help and report issues more easily. You'll find a **Community Discord** link in **Settings** (next to "Support the project" and "Report a bug"), and a friendly one-time invite appears when you open the dashboard — with a **"Don't show again"** button so it never nags. Both open the same invite, styled with the Discord logo. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### ⚡ Lighter on your GPU — the animated background rests when you're away
- **The animated background (Aurora + neon grid) now pauses itself when you're not interacting.** Those layers drift continuously, which keeps your GPU busy drawing frames even when the picture barely changes — and on a laptop where the dashboard is drawn by the discrete GPU but the Xeneon Edge is driven by the integrated GPU, every one of those frames is copied between the two cards, keeping the discrete GPU awake (and warm) for nothing. After about a minute without any touch, mouse or key input — or whenever the dashboard tab is hidden — the animation now freezes in place, and resumes instantly the moment you touch or move. The dashboard looks exactly the same while you're using it; it just stops working the GPU when no one is watching.
- **New "Rendering GPU" panel in Settings → Performance.** It shows which graphics card your browser is actually drawing the dashboard on. If that turns out to be your discrete GPU (the common cause of the dashboard running the GPU hotter than expected on laptops), it explains the one-time Windows setting — Settings → System → Display → Graphics → set your browser to "Power saving" — that pins the browser to the integrated GPU, so rendering and display are on the same card and the constant frame-copying stops. Purely informational; it never changes anything on its own. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🎬 Smart context profiles — the dashboard follows what you're doing
