- **The dashboard can switch itself to match your activity.** Set up a profile per activity — **gaming, coding, writing, streaming, content creation, meetings** — and Xenon applies it automatically the moment that activity starts: it can **jump to a chosen page**, set a **lighting effect**, and switch the active **Deck profile**. Start a game and your gaming page + RGB come up on their own; close it and everything goes back. Configure it under **Settings → Performance → Context profiles**, one dropdown each for Page / Lighting / Deck per activity.
- **It reverts when you're done — and never fights you.** When the activity ends, the dashboard restores what was showing before (after a short grace so a quick Alt-Tab out of a game doesn't flip things back and forth). It only acts on transitions, so you can always swipe to another page or change lighting by hand at any time — if you've moved something yourself, it leaves your choice alone instead of snapping it back.
- **Built on the detection you already have, off by default.** It reuses Performance Mode's activity detection (including your custom "which apps count as gaming/coding/…" lists), so there's one consistent notion of what you're doing — no extra background monitoring. Each dimension is optional (leave Lighting on "—" to not touch your RGB), there's a one-tap **Clear profiles**, and the whole feature is opt-in and fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **It can switch the whole dashboard look too.** Each profile now has a fourth **Style** dropdown: pick **Pixel Retro** for gaming and the dashboard flips to the full 8-bit CRT skin the moment a game starts, then returns to **Liquid Glass** when you quit (or the other way around — writing in retro, everything else in glass). It rides the same polite revert as the rest: if you switch the style yourself mid-game, your choice wins.
- **Docker Desktop (and other dev tools) no longer count as a game.** Opening Docker Desktop maximised could look exactly like a borderless full-screen game to the detector — which then triggered your gaming profile (Pixel Retro skin, auto-optimization) even with an empty "which apps count as gaming" list. Docker Desktop, Rancher Desktop and Podman Desktop are now excluded from game detection outright, alongside the browsers, editors, terminals and streaming tools already ignored — so both Performance Mode and Context profiles only fire on real games.

### ✨ Proactive moments — the dashboard speaks up when it's worth it
- **Game session recap.** When you close a game after a real session (10 minutes or more), the dashboard greets you back with a one-glance summary: **how long you played, your average and peak FPS** (when the FPS reader is installed), and the **highest CPU/GPU temperatures** the session reached. One toast per session, nothing while you're playing.
- **Sustained heat alerts.** Xenon already warned about a temperature *spike*; it now also notices the sneakier problem — a GPU or CPU that has been sitting **above its safe threshold continuously for 15+ minutes** (a blocked fan, an airflow problem, a runaway background app) — and tells you plainly: "GPU has been at 91°C for 16 minutes". Deliberately hard to nag: at most one alert per hour per sensor, and only for heat the dashboard actually observed.
- **A smarter morning greeting.** The morning greeting splash now includes **today's first calendar events** in a small glass card — and, if you use the spoken Ambient presence, Xenon reads your day ahead out loud with the greeting: weather, plus "You have 3 events today. First up: …".
- **You're in charge of every one of them.** A new **Proactive moments** group in **Settings → Performance** has an individual switch for each moment type (heat alerts, session recap, morning agenda). Everything is computed locally from data the dashboard already reads — no AI required, nothing leaves your PC, zero cost while no dashboard is open. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🔕→🔔 Windows notifications — your whole PC's pings, on the dashboard
- **A new Notifications tile mirrors Windows Action Center.** WhatsApp, mail, Teams, Discord, game launchers — every toast Windows shows you also appears as a live feed on the Xeneon Edge, with the app's real icon, who wrote, the message and the time. Add it from the "+" palette (Productivity); no more turning your head or Alt-Tabbing to see what just pinged. This is the heart of Xenon's notification hub, and no competing dashboard does it.
- **Private by design, off by default.** Notifications are read locally from Windows (the same WinRT listener the OS itself uses) — nothing is installed, nothing ever leaves your PC, and the reader only runs while a dashboard is actually open. Everything is controlled from the tile itself: one tap to turn it on, an eye button for **"hide content until tapped"** (shows only the app name until you tap — handy when the panel is visible to others), and a **per-app mute** on every row with a manager to unmute later.
- **Pop-up toasts for every notification.** Beyond the feed, each new notification also slides in as a toast — carrying the app's own icon and an accent colour pulled from that icon (with a graceful fallback), so a WhatsApp ping and a Discord DM are recognisable at a glance. Toasts respect "hide content" (they mask the text the same way) and skip muted apps. Prefer the feed alone? Turn pop-ups off in **Settings → Notifiche** (one place for both Windows and Discord), and turn notifications off entirely there to also stop the background reader.
- **Works with or without the native helper.** The Xenon Helper (now v0.4.0) reads notifications natively; without it, a PowerShell fallback does the same job automatically. If Windows blocks notification access, the tile says so and points at the exact Windows setting — never a dead end. At most the last 30 notifications are kept, and it's fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **A completely redesigned notification pop-up.** The on-screen toast has been rebuilt as a premium, liquid-glass card: each notification is haloed by its app's own colour with a glowing gradient edge, a lit app icon, a crisp title/message hierarchy and a luminous auto-dismiss bar. It **springs in**, adapts to light or dark theme, and you can now **swipe it away** with a finger (or press-and-hold to keep reading — the auto-dismiss pauses). Reduced-motion is fully respected. The same polished look is used for every in-app notice.
- **One switch in Settings to turn notifications off — and it actually saves work.** A new **Notifiche** section in Settings gives you a single master switch: turn it off and you stop seeing *everything* — pop-ups and feeds, Windows and Discord — and the background readers/watchers stop too, so it's genuinely lighter on your PC (not just hidden). A second toggle, **on-screen pop-up alerts**, keeps the feeds in the tiles but silences the toasts if you find them distracting. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Notifications can now drive your RGB lighting.** If you set a colour for the **Notifiche** event under Settings → Illuminazione → Effetti evento, your lights now actually react when a notification arrives (Windows or Discord) — a blink, pulse or solid flash in your chosen colour — instead of the effect sitting there doing nothing. It only fires when you've enabled that event effect, and stays out of the way during full-screen gaming.

### 🔔 Discord — your DMs and mentions, mirrored on the dashboard
- **The Discord widget now has a Notifications tab.** Turn it on and every notification Discord would show you — a **DM**, a **mention**, a message in a channel you watch — also appears as a live feed on the dashboard, with who wrote, the message, their avatar and the time. Glance at the Xeneon Edge instead of Alt-Tabbing into Discord to see what just pinged. The most requested notification source from the community (issue #61), and the first piece of Xenon's notification hub.
- **Private by design, off by default.** Notifications are read from your own Discord desktop app over the same local connection the voice controls already use — **nothing is installed, no bot is added, and nothing ever leaves your PC**. The switch lives on the Discord card in **Settings → Streaming**, and an optional **"Hide content until tapped"** mode shows only who wrote, keeping the text masked until you tap the notification — handy when the panel is visible to others.
- **One-time permission, explained in place.** Reading notifications needs one extra permission on your Discord link. If you enable the feature while already connected, both the settings card and the widget tell you plainly to disconnect and reconnect Discord once — a fresh connection picks the permission up automatically. Zero cost while the dashboard is closed (the connection isn't even open), at most the last 30 notifications are kept, and it's fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Unread badge on the Notifications tab.** When a notification arrives while you're on another tab of the Discord widget (Controls, Channels, Soundboard), the classic red counter appears on the **Notifications** tab so you never miss a ping — it clears the moment you open the tab.

### 🎧 Discord — clearer login errors
- **When connecting Discord fails, the dashboard now tells you why.** Previously any Discord connection problem showed the same generic "Could not start login. Try again." — unhelpful when the real cause is fixable. The card now shows a specific message per case: whether **Discord desktop isn't running**, the **Client ID is wrong or your desktop Discord is signed in with a different account than the one that created the app** (the most common cause — Discord's voice control only works when you authorize with the account that owns the application), the **authorization was denied or timed out**, or the **Client Secret / redirect URL is wrong** (it must be exactly `http://localhost`). Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🎧 Discord — soundboard on the dashboard (Deck key + widget), with preview
- **A Deck key can now fire a Discord soundboard sound.** Add the new **Discord: soundboard** action to any Deck key, pick one of your soundboard sounds from the live list (your servers' sounds and Discord's built-in ones, grouped by server), and tapping the key plays it into the voice channel you're currently in — the same as clicking it in Discord's own soundboard panel. It runs through the local Discord connection you already set up for voice control, so there's nothing new to install and no extra permission to grant. Works alongside the existing Discord mute/deafen/push-to-talk/join keys, and is fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH). Thanks to the community on issue #61 for showing it was possible over Discord's local channel.
- **A new Soundboard tab in the Discord widget.** The Discord dashboard tile now has a third tab — **Soundboard** — showing all your sounds as a grid: tap one to play it into your current voice channel, right from the dashboard. A short hint appears when you're not in a channel yet (you can still preview from there).
- **Preview before you play — audition any sound locally.** Both the Deck picker and the widget tiles have a small **▶ preview** button that plays the sound only for you (from Discord's own audio, no voice channel needed), so you can tell what a sound is before assigning it to a key or blasting it to everyone. (Server-uploaded sounds preview; some of Discord's tiny built-in defaults may not.)
- Because Discord doesn't officially document this soundboard control, it's best-effort: if a future Discord update changes it the action simply does nothing (no error, no crash), and the list is empty until Discord is running and connected.

### 📈 Sensor history — see your PC's temperatures and load over time
- **A new History tab in the System tile.** The System panel now has a **History** tab showing the trend of your **CPU and GPU temperature and load, and RAM usage** as clean sparkline charts, so you can see how your machine behaved over the last **24 hours, 7 days or 30 days** at a glance — each chart marks its latest value and its peak. It's the kind of screen that tells you, for example, that your GPU has been running hotter this week than last.
- **PC Screen Time — which apps and games you actually use.** The History tab now also shows a **screen-time breakdown**: your most-used apps for the chosen period (24 hours, 7 days or 30 days) as a ranked bar list with the time spent in each, a **total active time**, and how much of it was **gaming** (games are marked with a 🎮 and counted separately). It's the "Screen Time for your PC" view — see at a glance that you spent 6 hours in your game this week and an hour in the browser. Same privacy as the charts: it's measured from the app already in focus, updates while History recording is on, and **never leaves your PC**. Time while the screen is locked doesn't count.
- **Turned on with one switch, no AI needed.** A new **Sensor history** option in **Settings → Performance** starts the recording. It's **off by default**, costs almost nothing (one lightweight sample every few minutes of data the dashboard already reads), and **everything stays on your PC** — nothing is uploaded. Previously this history existed only as part of the Xenon AI "Guardian" feature; now you can have the charts on their own, whether or not you use the AI. (If you already use AI Guardian, the same history simply appears in the new tab.)
- The History tab appears once recording is enabled and is fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### ⚡ Efficiency pass — the new features stay light, even on modest PCs
- **Calendar feed subscriptions no longer refresh into the void.** Subscribed Outlook/Google calendars used to be re-downloaded every 15 minutes even with no dashboard open anywhere; they now follow the same rule as everything else — refreshed only while a dashboard is connected, and quietly brought up to date the moment one opens after an idle stretch.
- **The Claude Code reader got even lighter.** It no longer re-lists and re-checks every session file on disk at every refresh — a full sweep happens at most once a minute, and in between it only re-checks the session actually being written. When nothing changed and no session is live, it also skips re-computing the whole usage history. Heavy Claude users with hundreds of sessions will feel this the most.
- **The Claude reactor animation wastes nothing.** Its canvas is no longer re-allocated on every frame (only when the tile actually resizes) — on top of its existing self-pausing behavior when off-screen or idle.
- **The native app sips even less power.** The background watchers that keep your mouse and your game's focus safe now wake less often, and the focus guard re-checks the window style only when the foreground actually changes (or every couple of seconds as a safety net) instead of on every tick of a gaming session — better CPU idle time and battery on low-end machines, with no change in behavior. And when you hide the app from the tray, both watchers drop to a once-a-second nap: a hidden kiosk can't be touched, so there's nothing to guard.
- **Live updates are sent only when something actually changed.** Borsa, Calcio and News now compare each refresh against the previous one and stay silent when nothing moved — a closed market or a quiet news night costs your dashboard zero repaints, on every surface at once.
- **Feeds you don't use cost you nothing.** The News and Claude Code feeds now refresh only while their widget is actually on your dashboard (or the ticker streams that source) — if you never added them, you never pay for them, and adding the widget fills it right away. Borsa and Calcio deliberately keep refreshing even with their widget hidden, because their price-move and goal alerts must keep firing.
- **The Claude Code reader now reads only what's new.** While Claude works, its session transcript grows continuously; instead of re-reading the whole file (potentially tens of MB) on every refresh, the reader now picks up just the newly appended bytes. Together with the scan throttle above, watching even a heavy Claude session costs almost zero disk I/O.

### ⚡ Lighter on your PC — FPS monitor only runs when the dashboard is open
- **The in-game FPS reader (PresentMon) now runs only while a dashboard is actually open.** It needs a Windows performance-tracing session with administrator rights to measure real frame rates, and until now it stayed active in the background the whole time it was installed — even with no dashboard on screen. It now starts when you open the dashboard and stops shortly after you close the last one, so nothing is measuring your PC when you aren't looking at it. A brief grace period means a quick page refresh on the Xeneon Edge won't cause it to restart needlessly. Real FPS and game detection behave exactly as before while the dashboard is open (full-screen game detection was never affected).

### 🔒 Security — updates are now cryptographically verified before they run
- **The in-app updater no longer trusts the download alone.** Until now, "Update now" trusted the connection to GitHub (HTTPS) and nothing else — in principle, anyone able to tamper with that download could have slipped modified code onto your PC. From this release on, every published version carries a **signed fingerprint** (a SHA-256 checksum signed with a private key that only the release pipeline holds), and the updater checks the downloaded package against it — using a verification key **built into the app** — before a single file is unpacked. If the package doesn't match its signed fingerprint, or the fingerprint is missing or forged, the update refuses to proceed with a clear reason (`integrity_missing`, `signature_invalid` or `integrity_mismatch`) and your running installation is left untouched — you can always fall back to a manual download.
- **Nothing changes in how you update.** Same "Update now → Apply & restart" flow, no setup on your part; the verification happens silently in between. Note: if you click "Update now" within the first minute or two after a release is published, the signed fingerprint may not be attached yet — the updater will decline with `integrity_missing`; just try again shortly after.

### 🔄 Updating from the dashboard now refreshes the native helper too — one click, everything current
- **"Update now" no longer leaves the Xenon Helper behind.** The in-app updater installs the new app, but the optional native helper (`xenon-helper.exe` — it speeds up media reads, the game-mode probe and the notification icons) ships separately from each release and used to update only when you re-ran the installer. Now, right after an update, the dashboard notices if its helper is older than the version it needs and **refreshes it automatically in the background** — so a single click keeps the whole install current, exe included. Nothing changes for you: if the helper is already current (or you never installed it) it does nothing, and while the fresh helper is being fetched everything keeps working through the built-in PowerShell fallback. The updated helper is in use from the next time the dashboard restarts.
- **And that automatic refresh is cryptographically verified.** Because the dashboard runs the helper, it now installs a downloaded helper **only if its fingerprint matches the release's signed checksum** — the same Ed25519-signed manifest and built-in verification key that already guard app updates. A helper that doesn't verify (a tampered or man-in-the-middled download) is refused and the dashboard simply keeps its current helper, so this automatic path can never be tricked into running a swapped binary.

### 🛟 Reliability — a failed update now puts everything back exactly as it was
- **An update can no longer leave your installation half-updated.** Until now, if something went wrong mid-update — most commonly the dependency install failing on a flaky network — the updater restored your old files but could leave the app's internal libraries in a mixed old/new state, and files added by the new version behind: a tree that neither fully worked nor cleanly matched the previous version. The updater now takes an instant snapshot of the app's libraries before touching them and, on any failure, restores your files, removes anything the update had added, and puts the libraries back **exactly** as they were — no network needed to recover.
- **An update only "counts" once the new version has actually started.** After swapping the files in, the updater now waits for the updated dashboard to come up and confirm its version before deleting the safety backup. A new build that fails to boot — previously the worst case, leaving you with a dead install and no backup — now rolls back automatically to the version you were on, restarts it, and verifies it's serving again. If an update fails for any reason you simply keep using your current version, and the downloaded update stays staged so you can retry with one tap.

### 🖼️ A proper "What's New" — the headline features of the version you're on, with pictures
- **A curated welcome that shows what actually changed.** Instead of dumping the entire (very long) release notes, Xenon now greets you after an important update with a clean, hand-picked highlights card: the few headline features of the version you're running, each with a short blurb and a **screenshot or a short video**. Tap an image to view it fullscreen; clips play inline. It's built to show off what's new at a glance, not to make you read a wall of text.
- **It reappears until you've seen it, then gets out of the way.** The card shows at startup every time until you tap **"Don't show again"** — then it stays gone until the *next* important release brings genuinely new highlights. A pure bugfix release in between won't re-nag you: the previous highlights aren't "used up" by a small patch.
- **Separate from the update nudge.** This is for people already on the new version; the existing "update available → download / update now" prompt (for people still behind) is unchanged and stays its own thing.
- **Safe and localisable.** Highlight text can be written per language (it falls back to English), and any embedded media is loaded only from GitHub's own attachments — never arbitrary websites — with a graceful "open on GitHub" fallback if something can't load. Fully localised chrome (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🖼️ The update-available dialog now shows the pictures too
- **Screenshots and videos, not just text.** The "update available" popup (shown when you're behind) used to render release notes as text only, dropping any screenshots or clips. It now shows GitHub-hosted images and videos inline — images open fullscreen on tap, videos play with normal controls — so it's easier to see what an update brings before you install it. Same GitHub-only, fail-safe media handling as the What's New card above.

### 🔒 Security — your OBS & Streamer.bot passwords stay on your PC
- **Streaming passwords no longer travel to the browser.** The passwords you set for **OBS** and **Streamer.bot** (Settings → Streaming) are only ever needed by the dashboard's own background connection — yet until now they were also sent to the browser page along with the rest of your settings. They now stay server-side, exactly like your Home Assistant token and remote-control credentials already did. Once a password is saved, its field shows a **"saved"** indicator instead of the value; type a new one anytime to change it, and everything keeps working with no reconnection needed. A small, behind-the-scenes hardening with no setup on your part.

### 🚫 Browser widget — optional one-click ad-blocker
- **You can now block ads inside the Browser tile.** A new **Browser** section in **Settings** adds a single **Block ads** switch: flip it on and the dashboard downloads **uBlock Origin Lite** once (~10 MB) and loads it into the tile's browser — no manual install, no browser extension store. It's **off by default** (the tile stays as lightweight as before) and applies to every Browser widget at once, since they share one browser.
- **Honest about what it can and can't do.** It blocks the large majority of ads — banners, pop-ups and much of what you see on YouTube. Two things it can't fully stop, and the setting says so plainly: **YouTube video ads** and **Twitch ads**, because Twitch stitches its ads directly into the video stream on its servers where an ad-blocker can't reach them.
- **Turns on and off instantly.** Toggling the switch reloads any open Browser tiles right away, so the change takes effect without restarting anything. Turning it back off returns the tile to a clean, extension-free browser. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🖥 Browser & Second screen — smoother streams, real touch scrolling, quality at your fingertips
- **Both live tiles stream noticeably lighter and smoother.** The Browser and Second-screen tiles used to wrap every video frame in a text encoding that inflated it by a third and cost the dashboard extra decoding work on every single frame. Frames now travel in their raw binary form end-to-end — about 25% less data per frame and less main-thread work per paint — which translates directly into smoother motion and lower CPU while a stream is on screen. An already-open dashboard from an older build keeps working unchanged.
- **Web pages now scroll like a phone under your finger.** Touch on the Browser tile used to act like a mouse — dragging a page selected text instead of scrolling it. A finger is now forwarded to the page as *real* touch input: drag to pan, flick for inertial scrolling with momentum, tap to click — exactly like a phone browser, because it's the page's own native touch handling doing the work. A mouse keeps behaving like a mouse.
- **Change the second screen's smoothness without leaving the tile.** A new tune button on the Second-screen tile opens a compact panel with one-tap **FPS (15/30/60)** and **quality (Low/Medium/High)** presets — the stream re-tunes on the spot, so you can trade sharpness for fluidity while actually watching the result. It's the same setting as Settings → Second screen, so the two always stay in sync.
- **No more mystery black rectangle on your desktop.** On some PCs, opening the Browser widget could leave a ghostly black, click-through rectangle sitting in the top-left corner of the main monitor — the Windows compositor occasionally "leaking" a frame of the invisible browser engine the tile runs behind the scenes, and nothing short of restarting the compositor would clear it. The engine's hidden windows are now parked far off-screen, so even a leaked frame can never appear on any monitor.
- **Remote control setup speaks up instead of going quiet.** Installing Sunshine/Tailscale now shows a live elapsed-time indicator (winget can genuinely take minutes — it no longer looks hung), a failed install is reported honestly instead of being mistaken for success, and the control panel's Disconnect / Block / Kill-switch / screen-switch actions now say "Errore di rete — riprova" when they fail instead of silently re-enabling the button. The monitor list also refreshes itself within a minute when you plug in or remove a display, instead of staying frozen until reload.

### 🖥 Browser widget — hide the toolbar for full-screen video
- **A new button hides the Browser tile's toolbar so a video fills the whole tile.** The tab strip, address bar and favorites bar take up space at the top of the tile — great for browsing, in the way when you're watching a maximized video. A new **hide-toolbar** button (next to Expand) collapses all of it; the page immediately grows to fill the freed space and re-renders at the larger size. A small, unobtrusive button in the top-right corner of the tile brings the toolbar back with one tap. It works the same in the tile and in full-screen Expand mode, the choice is remembered per Browser widget across reloads, and it's fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH). Thanks to the tester on issue #58 for the suggestion.

### ⚡ Efficiency pass — quieter in the background, same dashboard up front
- **Widgets on pages you're not looking at now go idle.** The dashboard keeps every page ready so swiping is instant, but that also meant a Spotify, Discord, Twitch, YouTube or system tile parked on page 2+ kept polling — and kept calling Spotify's or Twitch's servers — even while you looked at page 1. Those background pages now pause their polling (and the Twitch chat connection) until you actually swipe to them, cutting needless network and third-party API calls with no visible change. A community-built Widget SDK tile likewise stops receiving data while it's off-screen.
- **Less repeated work while music plays.** The now-playing album art (a sizeable image) was being re-sent to the dashboard every two seconds even when the song hadn't changed; it's now sent once per track, which noticeably lightens the constant background chatter on the local connection while keeping the art exactly as responsive. The Spotify player state is also briefly cached and de-duplicated on the server, so the now-playing strip and the full Spotify widget being open at the same time no longer double your calls to Spotify (which is what used to trip Spotify's rate limit).
- **Fewer background processes and less idle CPU.** The per-app audio mixer is read a little less often and only refreshes the on-screen list when something actually changed; and the countdown-timer and clock displays stop doing per-frame work when nothing is counting down. Subscribed calendar feeds are re-fetched with proper "has this changed?" checks so an unchanged calendar isn't re-downloaded every 15 minutes, and the Home Assistant / OBS / Streamer.bot connections now back off gradually instead of retrying at a fixed rate when the service is offline.
- **Two hands-free reliability fixes.** The "Hey Xenon" wake word could get stuck (and stop responding until you restarted) if a voice capture was interrupted at just the wrong moment — the dashboard now cleans up an abandoned recording automatically and the listener recovers on its own. And a voice recording in progress is now always stopped when the server shuts down, so it can never leave your microphone busy.

### 📝 Notes — keep several, switch in a tap
- **Notes is now a proper multi-note pad.** The scratchpad used to be a single sheet; now you can keep as many notes as you like and flip between them from a tidy row of tabs across the top of the tile — one tap to switch, a **＋** to start a new one. Each tab titles itself from the note's first line, so you can tell them apart at a glance.
- **Pin what matters, drop what doesn't.** A pin keeps an important note first in the row; a delete button clears the current one. A live word count and the familiar "saving / saved" indicator sit along the bottom, so you always know it's captured — and it still auto-saves the instant you stop typing.
- **Nothing to migrate, nothing lost.** Your existing note becomes your first note automatically. It all works the same whether Notes lives as the Agenda "Notes" tab, as its own tile, or duplicated across pages, and Xenon AI and your backups keep working with your notes exactly as before. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🌍 Five more languages, and a cleaner language picker
- **Xenon now speaks Spanish, French, German, Portuguese and Russian too.** On top of Italian, English, Korean, Japanese and Chinese, the interface is now translated into five more languages. The everyday dashboard — greetings, the clock, weather, music, microphone, system and network readouts, calendar, tasks, timers, notes, the lock screen, the guided tour and the core of Settings — reads in your language; anything not yet translated falls back cleanly to English, so switching is always safe.
- **The language picker is now a dropdown.** The row of language buttons in Settings became one compact dropdown that lists each language in its own name (Italiano, English, Español, Français, Deutsch, Português, Русский, 日本語, 한국어, 中文), so the list stays tidy as the set grows.

### 🚀 App switcher — a real quick-launch dock, and favorites that finally stick
- **Starred apps now stay starred.** Favorites used to live only in the browser's local storage, which Windows clears on a restart or a new profile — so a favorited app quietly "forgot" itself and came back unstarred. They're now saved with your dashboard settings on your PC, so a star survives reboots and shows up the same on every dashboard. Existing stars are migrated over automatically.
- **The favorites bar is now a quick-launch dock.** It shows all your favorites, all the time — not only the ones currently open. Tap a running app to jump to it; tap a closed one and it **launches** (a small green dot marks what's already running). **Drag the icons to reorder** the dock however you like.
- **Search and close, right in the switcher.** Type in the new search box to filter the open windows by app or title when you have a lot going on, and **close a window straight from its card** with the × button (system-critical apps are safely refused, never force-killed).
- **Keyboard-friendly, like a real Alt+Tab.** Arrow keys move between windows and Enter opens the highlighted one — on top of the existing touch controls. Fully localised.

### 💾 Backup & saving — a backup that finally carries everything, and saves you can trust
- **The backup file now carries your whole Xenon.** Export used to cover layout, Deck, calendar, tasks, timers, notes and settings — but not everything you'd miss on a new PC. The backup (format v2) now also includes **Xenon AI's personal memory**, your entire **sensor history / PC Screen Time** recording, and your **custom background image** (embedded right in the file when it's an image; very large videos are skipped rather than producing a giant backup). Old v1 backup files still import exactly as before.
- **Importing a backup no longer silently wipes your Borsa, Calcio and News API keys.** Secrets never travel in a backup — so on import the dashboard is supposed to keep the ones already configured on your PC. It did for Gemini, Home Assistant, OBS, Streamer.bot and remote control, but the optional stock/football/news provider keys slipped through and were being emptied. Fixed: every locally-saved key now survives an import.
- **After an import, Xenon tells you exactly what needs reconnecting.** API keys and logins can't be carried inside a backup file (by design — a backup must be safe to keep on a cloud drive). The backup now records *which* services you had connected (never the secrets themselves), and after restoring on a new PC a toast lists precisely what to re-link — "Da ricollegare: Spotify, Gemini API, TheSportsDB" — instead of each feature just failing quietly later. If a restored background can't be carried over, the dangling reference is cleaned up instead of leaving a broken background.
- **A partially-failing import is now honest.** If one section of a backup can't be restored, the rest is applied anyway and the dashboard tells you which part didn't make it — previously the import stopped mid-way and left you in a silent half-restored state with a generic error.
- **Your settings now sync live between screens.** With the dashboard open on the Xeneon Edge *and* in a browser (or the native app), a change made on one surface used to reach the others only on their next reload — and until then, their next save could overwrite it. Every surface now picks up another surface's save within a moment over the existing live connection, so your screens stay in agreement.
- **Every saved file is now flushed to disk before it replaces the old one.** All of Xenon's stores were already written crash-safely (the old file is swapped for the new one in a single atomic step); now the new data is also physically flushed to the drive first, so even a power cut at the worst possible instant can't leave an empty settings/deck/notes file behind.
- **Fixed a rare race that could log you out of a streaming service.** Two connected services refreshing their sign-in tokens at the same moment (say Twitch and Spotify, both expiring together) could overwrite each other's freshly-renewed token — and one of them silently lost its login. Token saves are now queued one-at-a-time, so this can't happen anymore.
- **Hue and Nanoleaf pairing keys no longer leave the server.** The pairing tokens created when you connect Philips Hue or Nanoleaf lights were travelling inside the settings sent to the browser page — and would have ended up in an exported backup file too. They now stay server-side like every other credential: blanked on the wire and in the backup (the lights still show as paired), with the real keys kept safely on your PC. After restoring a backup on a new machine, the post-import summary simply tells you to re-pair your lights.
- **Less disk churn from lighting and history.** Rapid lighting changes (slider drags, AI colour sweeps) used to rewrite the full settings file once per tweak — they're now batched into a single write. And the sensor-history recorder no longer writes to disk every 5 minutes when there's nothing new to record.

### 🐛 Fixes
- **Browser pages you closed no longer haunt Windows' Alt+Tab.** Pages opened in the Browser tile could keep appearing in the Windows Alt+Tab switcher even after you'd closed their tab on the dashboard — ghosts that never went away. The cause: certain pages (pop-ups, login windows, links that open a new window) could slip out of the dashboard's tracking, so closing the tab never closed them in the hidden browser underneath. The tile's browser now closes a pop-up it fails to adopt, reclaims any page that belongs to no tab (on every tab close, with a periodic safety sweep), so a closed tab is *gone* — from the dashboard and from Alt+Tab.
- **The Browser ad-blocker now installs reliably.** Turning on "Block ads" could fail with "Impossibile installare il blocco pubblicità" through no fault of yours: right after the download unpacks, Windows' antivirus briefly holds the new files, and the final installation step hit that lock and gave up. It now waits the lock out and retries, so the one-click install completes.
- **Fixed the dashboard flashing white on reload with the Auto theme.** With the theme set to Auto, a reload could show the light (white) look for a moment — or until you reopened Settings — because the embedded display misreports its colour scheme and the reliable Windows reading only arrived a little later. Xenon now remembers the last known system theme, so a reload starts on the correct scheme immediately, and still refreshes the real Windows setting in the background.
- **Deck: cleaned up leftover profiles from deleted decks.** If you duplicated a Deck tile and later removed it, its profiles could linger invisibly — piling up as duplicate entries in the “Share profile” picker and under “From another Deck”, even though that deck was long gone. Those ghost profiles are no longer shown (only decks actually on your dashboard appear), and a new **“Remove decks no longer present”** button in the profile menu (edit mode) clears the leftovers for good in one tap. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Discord connect/disconnect is stable again.** Discord's local connection can serve only one app at a time — and the dashboard's own live link was holding it, so pressing **Connect** could fail instantly with a misleading "Discord isn't running". The dashboard now releases its connection before logging in, retries cleanly, and shows a specific "connection busy — try again" message when another app holds the line.
- **Honest guidance when Discord won't share notifications.** The Discord widget's own Notifications tab needs a Discord permission (`rpc.notifications.read`) that Discord does not grant to every app — and when it's withheld, reconnecting can't change that, so the old "just disconnect and reconnect" notice sent you in circles. The notice now tells the truth: it points you at removing the app under *Discord → User Settings → Authorizations* for a clean re-link, and reminds you that your Discord DMs and mentions show up in the new **Notifications tile** regardless, because that reads them straight from Windows.
- **Fixed a settings crash that broke saving and left the Notifications tile stuck on "Connecting…".** The Notifications widget had been registered without a matching layout default, so the server threw a 500 while normalizing the dashboard on every settings read *and* save — the dashboard couldn't load or persist any setting, and the tile could never turn its reader on. The default is restored, layout normalization now degrades gracefully instead of erroring if a widget ever lacks one, and the tile reconciles a stale on/off split on its own so it comes alive without a reload — and that self-heal now keeps retrying until the server confirms, instead of giving up after one attempt and leaving the tile stuck on "Connecting…" for good. Its header also got proper breathing room from the tile edges.
- **Share/import preset dialogs stay readable at any glass transparency.** If you turned the panel transparency down (Settings → Appearance), the "Share preset" and "Import preset" pop-ups became see-through, so the text and buttons were hard to read over whatever was behind them. Those dialogs now keep a solid background regardless of your glass setting — matching the colour picker — while normal panels stay as glassy as you like.
- **Spotify: fixed "Connected as" showing a blank name, and you can now fix or reset the Client ID.** After linking Spotify, the card could show a green "connected" dot but an empty username — and liking a song kept asking you to "reconnect Spotify" in a loop. It happened when the one-time profile read right after linking didn't go through; the dashboard now retries that read on its own, so the name fills in without you reconnecting. If it still stays blank, the card now tells you the usual cause — you approved with a different Spotify account than the one that created the app, or the app is in Development Mode and that account isn't added under "Users and Access" in the Spotify Developer Dashboard. And, like the other streaming integrations, the Spotify card now has **Edit credentials** and **Reset credentials** buttons, so a wrong Client ID is no longer a dead end. The Spotify tile also no longer wrongly says "Spotify isn't open" when the app is running but idle: Spotify's Web API doesn't expose a desktop app until it has played something once, so the tile now says **"No active Spotify device"** and tells you to press play once in Spotify to connect it. And if the tile can read your profile but not your playback (an older login made before we added the "read what's playing" permission, so Spotify is playing yet the tile stays empty), it now detects that specific case and tells you to **reconnect in Settings → Spotify to grant the missing permission**, instead of silently showing nothing. Most importantly, the tile now backs off when Spotify **rate-limits** it (HTTP 429): previously it kept polling straight through the limit, which pinned it in Spotify's penalty box so it could look permanently broken (blank name, no playback) — it now waits for Spotify's retry window, stops hammering so the limit clears on its own, and shows a brief "Spotify is busy" note while it recovers. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **App switcher: favorites now stick — across app restarts and PC reboots.** Starring an app in the "Open applications" panel used to key the favorite to the window's *title*, which changes constantly (the current browser tab, the open file, the playing Spotify track) and again after a reboot — so the star quietly "forgot" the app moments later. Favorites are now tied to the app itself, so a starred app stays a favorite: the star is filled whenever the app is open, it comes back the instant you reopen the app, and it survives a full PC restart. The favorites quick-bar shows a favorite only while its app is actually running (a closed one can't be focused), and it reappears the moment you open the app again. Existing stars are migrated automatically.
- **App switcher: app names and window titles are no longer cut off on shorter screens.** On the Xeneon Edge — or a small iCUE panel — the second row of app cards could be sliced right through its name and title. The cards are now more compact and the list snaps to whole cards, so every card shows its full name and title without clipping, and more apps fit at a glance.
- **Spotify: "Premium required" no longer shows up wrongly on Premium accounts.** Pressing shuffle, repeat or another control could pop "Spotify Premium required for playback" even on a Premium account. The cause: Spotify answers several different situations with the same HTTP 403, and the dashboard was treating *every* 403 as "not Premium." It now reads Spotify's actual reason and shows the right hint — only a genuine non-Premium account says **Premium required**; a login made before we added the playback-control permission now correctly says **reconnect Spotify in Settings → Spotify to grant permission** (which fixes it); and other cases point you to **start playback on a device first**. If you hit this, reconnecting Spotify once from Settings resolves it. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Discord widget: people joining or leaving your voice channel now show up instantly.** Before, the member list in the Discord tile only refreshed when *you* changed something (moved channel, toggled a setting) or when someone spoke — so a friend hopping into your channel could sit invisible until the next such event. The widget now listens for Discord's voice-membership events for your current channel, so joins, leaves, mutes and deafens appear live. It reuses the same single local Discord connection and only runs while the dashboard is open, so there's no extra cost. Thanks to the community on issue #61.
- **No more background flicker behind the Settings panel and the update dialog.** On some GPUs (typically discrete NVIDIA cards) the screen could flicker while a full-screen frosted panel was open — the Settings window, or the "update available" dialog — especially with a custom image or video background and the neon grid turned on. The cause: those panels blur everything behind them, and re-blurring the constantly-moving animated background every frame flickers on certain graphics setups. The animated background (and a background video) now holds still while such a panel is open — identical to look at behind the blur, just with nothing left to make it flicker — and resumes the moment you close the panel. Stacked panels are handled correctly too (opening "Check for updates" from inside Settings keeps things steady until you close both). Thanks to the reporters on issue #56.
- **The native app no longer trips "game mode" on itself.** The new full-screen Xenon app is borderless and edge-to-edge — the exact shape the game detector looks for — so on launch it could be mistaken for a full-screen game and switch the dashboard into Performance/game mode (pausing ambient effects) with no game actually running. Xenon's own app window is now excluded from game detection, matched precisely so real games with "Xenon" in their name (Xenonauts, Xenon Racer) are still detected normally.
- **OBS and creative apps no longer switch on Performance/game mode by mistake.** With Performance Mode set to auto for **Games only**, opening OBS (or Streamlabs, XSplit, vMix) could still trigger it — and so could Photoshop, Premiere, Blender or DaVinci Resolve. These apps keep drawing a live preview at game-like frame rates, so the frame-rate–based "windowed game" detector mistook them for a game. Streaming/broadcast tools are now never treated as a game, and creative editors aren't treated as one while in a window — so with only Games enabled, launching OBS leaves the dashboard exactly as it was. They're still recognised as *Streaming* and *Content creation* activities if you choose to enable those, and real full-screen games are detected as before.
- **The native app now works on any display, not just the Xeneon Edge.** If you don't have an Edge but still want the dedicated app, Xenon no longer opens as a borderless, taskbar-hidden kiosk you can't get out of — when no Edge is connected it opens as an ordinary, resizable window with a normal title bar and a taskbar entry, sized to fit your actual screen (so it never spills off a small display) while keeping the Edge's wide proportions so nothing looks stretched. From the tray icon you can switch it to **Fullscreen**, and — with more than one monitor — pick which display to **Show on**; both choices are remembered next time you launch. Plug an Edge in and it snaps back into the full edge-to-edge kiosk automatically. (You can also always just open the dashboard in a browser at `127.0.0.1:3030`.)
- **Minimal top bar: the floating clock/weather pill no longer covers the widget below it when you scroll.** With the compact "island" top bar, on a screen smaller than the Edge (or the native app on an ordinary monitor) scrolling a page slid its widgets up underneath the floating clock, so the pill ended up sitting on top of a tile's header. Xenon now reserves that strip at the very top of every page, so the space under the pill is always kept and nothing scrolls beneath it — on the Edge and on smaller displays alike.
- **Weather: the little rain/snow marks under the forecast icons are readable again.** On rainy or snowy days the "Next days" list (in both the Weather widget and the weather panel) showed odd pale-blue rectangles floating in the gaps between rows. They were the icon's precipitation dots, drawn in a way that came out square and dropped into the row below. They're now proper small round drops (and soft haze lines for fog) tucked neatly under each cloud, so a rainy day reads at a glance instead of looking broken.
- **Weather: the tile is tighter, and it now shrinks instead of clipping.** The Weather widget used to reserve a lot of empty space around the big temperature and gave its details, hourly timeline and 3-day forecast fixed sizes — so making the tile smaller just started scrolling or cutting things off, and it tended to hog half the dashboard. The padding and gaps are slimmed down, and every part of the widget now scales with the tile: as you make it smaller the text and icons shrink together, keeping the whole forecast (including the next 3 days) visible without scrolling or clipping — so you can give it a smaller footprint and fit another widget beside it. Thanks to the community feedback that asked for this.
- **Spotify: the Next/Previous buttons work even when Spotify is idle.** Skipping tracks could do nothing and show "No active Spotify device" whenever the desktop app was open but paused/idle — the exact same situation where the **Play** button already woke Spotify up and started music. Next and Previous now do the same: if there's no active device they wake an available one and then carry out the skip, so the buttons aren't dead in the one state you'd most want to press them. (Playback control still needs Spotify Premium — a Spotify limitation.)
- **Spotify: "Up Next" no longer shows a wrong next song for loose/random playback.** When you play a single track, a Liked Song, or a radio/autoplay mix — anything without a playlist or album behind it — Spotify's own "up next" data is only an autoplay guess and often doesn't match what actually plays next. The widget used to present that guess as fact; it now labels the Up Next list as **approximate** in exactly those cases (and shows the real order untouched when you're inside a playlist or album), so it never confidently tells you the wrong next song. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 📚 Website & documentation — refreshed for v4
- **Every key screenshot was recaptured on the real v4 dashboard, in English.** The site and the docs no longer show the old v3 design: system monitor, microphone, Deck, calendar, AI chat, weather, lock screen, layout editor, Settings (Appearance, Lighting, Xenon AI, Performance, Remote Control) and the full-dashboard overview are all fresh 2560×720 captures — plus brand-new shots of the widgets that didn't have any: **Stocks** (list + detail charts + ticker), **Football** (teams + team view with standings), **News**, and **Vitals**.
- **The website now tells the whole v4 story.** A new "Football, news and the rest of your day" feature block joins the Markets one, Vitals & Bit appear in the capability grid, the gallery grew four new frames (stock charts, football team view, news stream, vitals), and a broken Notifications image was fixed — all translated in the site's five languages (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Supporting the project is front and centre.** A new "Keep Xenon free" banner sits right before the Hall of supporters with a one-tap Buy-me-a-coffee button and a Discord link — matching the in-app Support section — so helping the project (or just saying hi on Discord) is never more than one scroll away.
- **The native app is now documented as the main way to run Xenon on the Edge.** The README's "Use it" step, the website's install section (in all five languages) and the surfaces list in FEATURES.md all lead with the native full-screen app — it opens by itself at login, no browser or iCUE needed — with the iCUE iFrame clearly repositioned as the alternative for people who prefer staying inside iCUE.

## [v3.7.1] - 2026-07-03
### 🗓 Calendar — week start + multi-day events
- **The calendar can now start the week on Sunday or Monday.** A new **Calendar** option in **Settings → Appearance** lets you pick the first day of the week; the month grid and the weekday header update instantly. It defaults to **Monday** (unchanged from before), and — like the clock format — the choice is saved and syncs across your dashboards. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **You can now create multi-day events yourself.** When adding an event, an optional **"Until"** date lets you span it across several days (a trip, a holiday, a deadline window) — it then shows as a dot under every day it covers and appears in each of those days' agendas, exactly like multi-day events from a subscribed calendar. Leave the field empty for a normal single-day event.

### 🐛 Fixes
- **You can now fix or reset streaming credentials after saving them (Discord, Twitch, YouTube).** Previously, once you saved a Client ID / secret for a streaming integration — even a wrong one — the card only offered **Connect** / **Disconnect** and hid the input fields, so a typo left you permanently stuck (Disconnect only clears the login token, not the app credentials). Each configured provider now has an **Edit credentials** button that reopens the setup form so you can paste the correct values, and a **Reset credentials** button that clears the stored keys and returns the card to first-time setup. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).
- **Multi-day calendar events now show on every day they span.** Events from a subscribed calendar (Google, Outlook, …) that last more than one day — a trip, a holiday, a multi-day conference — used to appear only on their start day, so a dot was missing from the following days and clicking one of those days showed nothing. They now correctly fill in as a dot under **every** day they cover and appear in that day's agenda when you tap it. (All-day event end dates are handled per the calendar standard, so a Mon–Fri event highlights Monday through Friday, not into the weekend.)

## [v3.7.0] - 2026-07-03
### 🤖 Streamer.bot — a dedicated dashboard widget (phase 3)
- **A new Streamer.bot tile with a live activity feed.** Add the **Streamer.bot** widget from the "+" palette (Streaming group) and watch your stream light up in real time on the Xeneon Edge: **follows, subs and re-subs, gift subs and gift bombs, cheers, raids, channel-point redemptions, hype trains, stream online/offline and announcements** — plus the YouTube equivalents (new subscribers, Super Chats, Super Stickers, members and gifted memberships). Each event shows who did it, a colour-coded icon per type, the amount where it applies (bits, viewers, months) and how long ago it happened. It's driven by the same single, efficient Streamer.bot connection as the stateful Deck keys — **pushed live, never polled** — so it reacts the instant something happens and costs nothing at rest.
- **A live Globals view, too.** A second tab in the widget lists your Streamer.bot **global variables** with their current values, updating live as they change — handy next to the stateful Deck keys that reflect them.
- **Reads only, stays out of the way.** The widget never sends anything to Streamer.bot (the Deck owns the actions); it shows a clear "connect in Settings → Streaming" prompt when Streamer.bot isn't set up, and an "Offline" state when it's configured but not running. Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH).

### 🤖 Streamer.bot — stateful "smart" Deck keys (phase 2)
- **A Deck key can now reflect a Streamer.bot global variable — it lights up on its own when the global is on.** In the key editor there's a new **"Reflect a Streamer.bot global"** picker: choose one of your Streamer.bot global variables and the key shows as active whenever that global is truthy. Optionally match a specific value (e.g. show the key as on only while a `mode` global equals `live`). The key's tap still does whatever you set it to — typically a Streamer.bot action that flips the global — so a single key both **controls and mirrors** the real state, just like the built-in mic/OBS toggle keys.
- **Truly live, and truly lightweight.** The dashboard keeps **one** connection to Streamer.bot open only while a dashboard is on screen and Streamer.bot is set up, and it **subscribes** to variable changes instead of polling — so a bound key flips the instant the global changes and costs essentially nothing when nothing's happening. The connection drops automatically when you close the dashboard, and reconnects on its own if Streamer.bot restarts. (Same efficient live-connection design as the Home Assistant tile.)
- Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH); the option only appears when Streamer.bot is connected.

### 🤖 Streamer.bot — deeper Deck control (phase 1)
- **A Deck key can now send a chat message through Streamer.bot.** New **"Streamer.bot: send chat"** action: pick the platform (Twitch, YouTube, Kick or Trovo), type the message, and choose whether it goes out from your **bot account** or your **own account** — one tap posts it to chat.
- **Fire Streamer.bot code triggers from a key.** New **"Streamer.bot: code trigger"** action with a live dropdown of your code triggers (typed by name when Streamer.bot is offline), so keys can kick off sub-actions and custom C# triggers directly, not just top-level actions.
- **Pass arguments to a Streamer.bot action.** The existing "do action" key gained an optional **Arguments (JSON)** field — e.g. `{"user":"bob","amount":5}` — so a single key can drive an action that expects inputs, instead of needing a separate action per value. Arguments also work on code triggers.
- All new controls are localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH) and appear only when Streamer.bot is connected, like the rest of the Streamer.bot category. (This is the first of a phased expansion; live stream events and a dedicated Streamer.bot widget are coming next.)

### 🎛 Deck — use an app's own icon, no image needed
- **Set up an app-launch key and grab its real icon in one tap.** When a Deck key opens an app — either a regular program (**Open app**) or a Microsoft Store app (**Open Store app**) — a new **"Use app icon"** button appears in the key's icon picker. Tap it and the key instantly takes on the application's **own built-in icon** (the same one you see in the Start menu and taskbar), so you no longer have to hunt down or make a picture just to make the key recognisable. It works for classic desktop programs and for Store/UWP apps alike; if an app has no usable icon, you can still pick an emoji, a built-in symbol or upload your own image as before.

### 🐛 Fixes
- **Streamer.bot now connects when its WebSocket authentication is "enabled but not enforced".** Streamer.bot can advertise a login challenge while still accepting connections without one — a very common setup. Xenon was always replying with a login attempt, and with no password that attempt is wrong, so Streamer.bot slammed the door ("Could not reach Streamer.bot"). Xenon now only logs in when you've actually entered a password; otherwise it connects normally. If you left the password blank because your Streamer.bot doesn't enforce authentication, it just works now. And a successful **Test connection** now turns the integration on across the dashboard (the widget and the stateful Deck keys), even if you left the Host field blank to use the default `127.0.0.1` — previously the test could say "Connected" while the widget still showed "not configured". When Streamer.bot is set up but not running (or its WebSocket Server isn't started), the Streamer.bot widget now says so and tells you how to fix it — and reconnects on its own the moment Streamer.bot is reachable.
- **Deck "Sheen" key animation now loops smoothly.** The sheen (light-sweep) key animation used to visibly snap back to the start at the end of each cycle. The highlight now sweeps fully off one edge and starts again from off the other edge, so it's invisible at the loop point — a continuous, seamless shine with no hard cut.

## [v3.6.0] - 03-07-2026
### 🏠 Smart Home — control your house from the dashboard (Home Assistant)
- **Your home's lights, sensors and appliances, right on the Xeneon Edge.** A new **Smart Home** tile connects to **Home Assistant** — the free, open-source, local home-automation hub — and shows the devices you choose, grouped by room, exactly like a proper smart-home panel: **one-tap toggles** for lights and switches, **run buttons** for scenes, scripts and buttons, and **live value cards** for temperature, humidity, power, air quality and any other sensor. Tap a light and it turns on instantly; the tile reflects what's really happening in your home.
- **A real control panel for every device — not just on/off.** Tap a device and a control panel slides up with exactly the controls *that* device supports, read live from Home Assistant. A **TV or soundbar** gets a full remote — power, volume slider and mute, input/source picker (HDMI, Netflix…), sound modes, transport (⏮ ⏯ ⏭) and a **channel box** to type a channel number (or name) and jump straight to it — which also snaps the TV back to live TV from any HDMI input. A **thermostat or AC** gets a big target-temperature stepper with the current reading, plus heat/cool/auto/dry mode, fan speed and presets. A **light** gets a brightness slider, warm-to-cool white and a colour palette. **Blinds** get open/stop/close and a position slider; **fans** get a speed slider, presets and oscillation; **robot vacuums** get start/pause/dock and suction. Numbers get a slider, dropdown helpers get their option list — every device finally does everything it can do, with a clean, modern, touch-friendly layout. (Previously a TV showed only a play button and helper entities showed a bare "—" — that's gone.)
- **One device, one card — no more duplicates.** Home Assistant often exposes a single appliance as several separate "entities" — a TV, for example, is a media player *plus* a remote *plus* restart/close-app buttons — which used to appear as four identical cards. They're now **merged into one card per physical device**, and its control panel gathers all its parts in one place (the TV's remote, its power, and its buttons together). The device picker in **Settings → Smart Home** matches this: entities are grouped under their device and each one is tagged with its type (Media player, Remote, Button, Sensor…), so you can tell at a glance what everything is — and the leftover clutter (a shopping list, a person, the sun) is clearly labelled for what it is.
- **It adapts to the space you give it.** With a roomy tile and just a device or two, the Smart Home widget now shows each device's **full controls inline** — no tap needed, the TV remote or the light's brightness slider is right there. Shrink the tile, add more widgets, or pick more devices and it automatically switches back to compact cards that open the control panel. It measures what actually fits and re-checks whenever you resize.
- **A complete hub — every capability a device exposes.** The panel now covers the full control surface of each device type, so you can do everything from the dashboard: media players add **stop, shuffle, repeat and a seek bar**; lights add **effects**; thermostats/ACs add **swing (louvre) modes**; blinds add **tilt** (open/close/position); fans add **direction** (forward/reverse); robot vacuums add **find-my-robot and spot cleaning**. And four new device types are fully supported: **alarm panels** (arm home/away/night, disarm, with a code field when required), **water heaters** (target temperature + operation mode), **valves** (open/stop/close + position) and **robot lawn mowers** (start/pause/dock).
- **Truly live, and truly lightweight.** The dashboard keeps a single connection to Home Assistant open **only while the Smart Home tile is on screen**, and updates **the moment something changes** (a light flips, a door opens, the washing machine finishes) instead of polling — so it reacts instantly yet costs essentially nothing when nothing's happening, and drops the connection entirely when the tile isn't shown or Home Assistant isn't set up. Bursts of changes (like a scene switching a dozen lights at once) are coalesced into one smooth update.
- **Two-minute setup, and it stays private.** In **Settings → Smart Home**, paste your Home Assistant address and a long-lived access token, tap **Connect**, then tick the devices you want on the tile from a searchable, room-grouped list. Everything runs **locally between your PC and your Home Assistant** — nothing goes to the cloud, and your access token never leaves the server (it's stored server-side, shown as "saved", and never sent back to the browser or included in a backup export).
- **Control it from a Deck key, too — now for real.** The Deck editor's **Home Assistant** category grew from three actions into a full set of one-tap device actions: **Light** (on/off/toggle/brighter/dimmer), **Media player** (play‑pause, next, previous, stop, volume ±, mute), **Cover/blind** (open/close/stop), **Climate** (heat/cool/auto/dry/off), **Fan**, **Vacuum** (start/pause/stop/dock/find), **Lock** (lock/unlock), **Alarm** (arm home/away/night, disarm, with a code field), plus **Run script**, **Press button**, **Activate scene**, and the original **Call service (advanced)**. The whole list is **capability-aware**: it only offers actions for the kinds of device you actually have connected — if all you have is a TV you'll see the Media, Button, Toggle and advanced actions, not Cover, Alarm or Vacuum — and each action's device picker likewise lists only the matching devices, so setting a key up is quick and mistake-proof. Like the other integrations, the category stays locked with a hint until you connect.
- Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH), and off by default — the tile starts hidden and appears in the **"+" → System** palette when you want it.

### 🪟 Deck — move windows around
- **New "Windows" Deck category.** A Deck key can now rearrange the window you were last using: **move it to the next / previous monitor**, **snap it to the left or right half**, **maximize**, **minimize**, or **center** it — handy on a multi-monitor desk without reaching for keyboard shortcuts. Moving a maximized window to another screen re-maximizes it there.

### 🌤 Weather — more air-quality detail
- **Pollen and NO₂ added to the weather details.** Alongside the existing air-quality readings (air quality index, PM2.5, PM10, UV), the weather widget and full-screen weather view can now also show **pollen** (where the data is available, e.g. across Europe) and **nitrogen dioxide (NO₂)** — each colour-coded green/amber/red by severity like the other metrics, and individually toggleable in **Settings → Weather → Details to show**. Especially useful where air quality and pollen matter day to day.

### 🎧 Discord voice control (#61)
- **Control Discord voice from a Deck key.** A new "Discord" category in the Deck editor adds one-tap voice actions that mirror what a Stream Deck plugin does — driven through Discord's own local app, no third-party plugin required:
  - **Mute / unmute** your microphone (toggle, or force one way).
  - **Deafen / undeafen** (mute everyone's audio for you).
  - **Push-to-talk** — switch your input mode between push-to-talk and voice activity.
  - **Join a voice channel** — pick any channel from your servers in the editor and jump straight into it with one tap; **leave voice** to hang up.
  - **Microphone and output volume** — nudge either up or down.
  - **Audio processing** — toggle noise suppression, echo cancellation, automatic gain or QoS priority.
- **New Discord dashboard widget.** Add a **Discord** tile from the "+" palette (Streaming group) for an at-a-glance voice panel with two internal tabs so each view gets the full tile height:
  - **Controls** — your mute / deafen / push-to-talk state and one-tap **mute, deafen, push-to-talk, leave, mic & output volume** and audio-processing toggles, plus — while you're in a call — **who's in it with a live green highlight on whoever's speaking** (works for server voice channels and DM/group calls).
  - **Channels** — the joinable voice channels **grouped by server**, using the whole widget so the list is fully readable; tap one to jump in. Each voice channel now shows **who's currently connected inside it, with a live headcount** (and mute/deafen markers on each person), refreshed while you're looking at the tab — so you can tell which channel has people, and who, before you join.

  Everything updates **in real time** — the widget reacts to voice changes as they happen (channel join/leave, mute, someone starts talking) instead of polling, so it's essentially free when nothing's happening.

  **If the Discord desktop app isn't running**, the widget now shows a clear **"Open Discord"** button over the whole tile (with the Discord mark) instead of sitting there with dead controls — one tap launches Discord, and the overlay clears itself the moment the app is up. It only appears when your account is linked but the app is closed; when Discord is running the widget looks exactly as before. Fully localised.

  The widget now follows the dashboard language properly (its labels were staying in the previous language after a switch), the server names above each group of channels are clearer and no longer render cut off, and the Controls tab spreads its contents to fill the tile instead of leaving empty space.
- **How to connect.** In Settings → Streaming there's now a Discord card. Because Discord has no cloud API for voice control, you create your own free Discord app (a two-minute step, linked from the card), paste its Client ID and Secret, then tap Connect and click Authorize in the pop-up Discord shows you. Your Discord desktop app just needs to be running. The Deck actions and the widget's controls stay inactive until you connect, with a hint pointing you here.
- **Note on soundboards.** Playing a Discord soundboard sound as *you* isn't something Discord exposes to apps, so it isn't included — but a Deck **keyboard-shortcut** key (for a soundboard app like Soundpad/Voicemod) or a **Streamer.bot** action still covers that.

### 🎵 Spotify — a full player on your dashboard
- **A proper Spotify remote, not just a read-out.** The new **Spotify** tile connects to your Spotify account and puts a real player on the dashboard. The centrepiece is a **now-playing hero**: large album art, the track and artist, and a **live seek bar** you can drag to scrub. Below it, full transport — **play/pause, previous, next, shuffle, repeat** (off / all / one), a **♥ like** that fills when the song is in your Liked Songs, and a **volume slider** for the active device. It shows **where playback is happening** (a device chip in the header), and the progress ticks smoothly second-by-second.
- **An immersive, album-driven design that looks great at any size.** The player wraps the whole card in an **ambient glow taken from the album art** — a soft, blurred wash of the cover's own colours, with a dark scrim so the text stays crisp — the same feel as a full-screen music app. The **cover is the star**, and the layout **reshapes itself to the tile**: a tall/portrait tile shows a **big centred cover** with the controls beneath it (and, when there's room, the queue below); a wide, short tile lays the cover beside the controls with the queue underneath; a small tile becomes a clean, cover-forward mini-player. Nothing clips or crowds, whatever shape you drag it to. (The tile also starts a little taller by default so the big cover has room to shine.)
- **When nothing's playing, it helps you start.** If Spotify is open but idle, the empty state shows a **Play** button that resumes playback. If the **Spotify app isn't running**, it shows an **Open Spotify** button that launches it — then switches back to the player once it's up. So the tile is never a dead end.
- **The three things Windows can't show, in tabs.** Under the player: **Up Next** (your live queue with cover art), **Playlists** (your playlists — tap one to start it), and **Devices** (your Spotify Connect targets — tap one to move playback there, with the active device marked).
- **Spotify actions on the Deck.** A **Spotify** category in the Deck editor with the whole set: **play/pause, next, previous, shuffle, repeat, like the current track, set/step volume, seek/restart, save to Liked Songs, play a playlist** (paste a link, URI or ID), or **switch to a named device**. Like the other integrations, the category stays locked with a hint until you connect.
- **The Media tile gets Spotify powers too.** When the Media tile's **Playback** tab is showing **Spotify** *and* your account is linked, it now grows a tidy Spotify strip right under the transport: a **seek bar**, **♥ save to Liked**, **shuffle** and **repeat**, plus **Playlists** and **Devices** buttons that open a bounded overlay panel (tap to play a playlist or move playback to another device, then it closes itself). For any other source — or if you haven't linked Spotify — the strip simply isn't there, so the tile stays clean.
- **Lightweight by design.** Both the widget and the Media-tile strip only talk to Spotify **while they're actually on screen** — a hidden or backgrounded dashboard does nothing. Playback state refreshes on a gentle interval while visible (with a local ticker keeping the seek bar smooth in between); playlists and devices load when you open them.
- **How to connect.** Spotify has its **own Settings → Spotify section** that explains what you get and walks you through it. You create your own free Spotify app (a two-minute step, linked from the section) and paste just its **Client ID** — Spotify uses the modern **PKCE** flow, so there's **no client secret**. The exact **redirect URI** to register is shown with a one-tap **Copy** button. Tap **Connect**, approve access in the Spotify tab that opens, and you're linked. Your token stays on your PC and is never sent to the browser. **Note:** reading the queue/playlists/devices works on any account; **playback control needs Spotify Premium** (a Spotify limitation).
- Fully localised (EN/IT/KO/JA/ZH), and off by default — the tile starts hidden and appears in the **"+" → Streaming** palette when you want it.

### 🧠 Xenon AI — now controls Spotify, your smart home and Discord by voice or chat
- **Xenon AI can now run the three new integrations end-to-end**, by voice or in chat — not just the dashboard. Ask in plain language and it does it: the new controls only appear to the assistant once you've connected the matching integration, so nothing changes for anyone who hasn't.
- **Spotify — full playback control, including "play *this* song".** Beyond play/pause, next/previous, shuffle, repeat, like, volume and seek, Xenon can now **search and play any song, artist, album or playlist by name** ("metti *Bohemian Rhapsody*", "play something by Daft Punk", "put on my Chill playlist"), **add a track to the queue** ("aggiungi *One More Time* in coda"), **switch the playback device** ("play on the living-room speaker"), and **tell you what's playing** and where. Playing and queuing need Spotify Premium, like the rest of playback control.
- **Home Assistant — control any device in detail.** Xenon can **list your devices** and then act on them: turn lights, switches and appliances **on/off/toggle**, **run a scene**, and adjust things in fine detail — **set a light's brightness and colour, a thermostat's temperature, a fan's speed, a blind's position**, and more ("accendi la luce del salotto", "porta il termostato a 21 gradi", "abbassa le luci al 30%", "chiudi le tapparelle"). It matches your request to the right device by its name and room.
- **Discord — voice control by name.** Xenon can **mute/unmute your mic, deafen/undeafen, switch push-to-talk, join a voice channel by name** ("entra nel canale Gaming"), **leave the call**, and **nudge your mic or output volume** — all through your running Discord desktop app.
- If you ask it to control something whose integration isn't connected yet, it says so and points you to the right Settings section instead of pretending it worked. Works with both the cloud (Gemini) and the local AI provider.

### 🌐 Browser widget — sound and favorites
- **Web pages now play sound.** Audio from a page open in the Browser tile (a YouTube or Twitch stream, a music site, an embedded video) is now audible — previously the embedded browser was always muted. Sound plays only from the tab you're actually viewing: background tabs, an off-screen Browser tile, and tiles paused by Performance/Game mode stay silent, so nothing keeps playing behind your back. Switching tabs or hiding the tile mutes it instantly, and the sound follows you back when you return.
- **Favorites bar for quick access.** Each Browser tile now has a favorites strip: save any page as a labelled shortcut and reopen it with one tap. Tap the ★ button in the toolbar to add the current page (name and address are pre-filled and editable), and remove a favorite with the × on its chip. The list is shared across every Browser tile and survives restarts, so your shortcuts are always where you left them.
- **Fixed: Browser tabs and addresses are now remembered across reloads.** The pages open in a Browser tile — including its extra tabs and which one was active — were being discarded whenever settings were saved, so the tile came back empty after a dashboard reload or restart. Your open pages now persist properly.
- **Sign-in pop-ups now work in the Browser tile (Google / Amazon / Twitch login).** "Continue with Google/Amazon" buttons open a real pop-up window, and until now the tile reused the current page for it, so after you authorized the sign-in the pop-up had nowhere to report back and the tile went black on the callback page. Pop-ups are now shown as their own view stacked over the page that opened them: you complete the sign-in in place, and when the pop-up closes you're returned to the original page — now logged in. If a pop-up doesn't close itself, the Back button dismisses it.
- **Sharper Browser tile.** Web pages now look noticeably crisper in a normal-sized Browser tile.
