Small tiles are rendered at a higher internal resolution (which also prompts sites like YouTube to serve sharper video), and the frame quality was raised — the stream is entirely local, so there's no bandwidth cost. Large and full-screen tiles keep their existing sharpness, and the extra detail is capped so it never weighs on performance.

### 🌤 Weather — choose exactly which details to show
- **Turn individual weather details on or off.** Settings → Weather now has a "Details to show" section where you can hide any single detail instead of only the whole block: the header chips (feels-like, wind, precipitation) and each metric (air quality, humidity, PM2.5, PM10, pressure, visibility, UV, clouds). Uncheck the ones you don't care about — for example hide visibility and the PM readings — and they disappear from both the Weather widget and the full-screen weather view, everywhere at once. Hiding every detail also drops the now-empty "Details" heading rather than leaving a bare title. Your choices are saved and everything stays visible by default, so nothing changes until you decide to trim it down.
- **Choose how often the weather refreshes.** Settings → Weather now has a "Refresh" option to set how frequently the weather updates — from every 10 minutes up to every 3 hours (default 30 minutes). Pick a shorter interval if you want the latest conditions more often, or a longer one to keep things calm. The change takes effect immediately, no reload needed.

### ✨ Interface polish
- **The System monitor now shows your CPU and GPU model on the label.** Next to the **CPU** and **GPU** headings you now see the actual chip — e.g. *Ryzen 7 7800X3D*, *NVIDIA RTX 5080* — cleaned up from the raw Windows string (no "(R)", "8-Core Processor", "GeForce" clutter) and kept on a single line: a long name simply trims with an ellipsis instead of wrapping. So you can tell at a glance which machine you're looking at.
- **Removed the coloured accent bar on the left edge of widgets.** The thin vertical line that ran down the left side of some tiles (System, Twitch, YouTube and others) has been removed everywhere for a cleaner, more uniform look.
- **Every tab now shows its icon in tabbed tiles.** When you merge widgets into a tabbed tile, tabs like Discord, OBS, Twitch, YouTube, Deck, Browser, Remote, Second screen and Weather were showing their name with no icon. Each tab now displays the same glyph the widget has in the "+" add menu, so tabbed tiles read at a glance.
- **Tidier "add widget" menu.** The "+" widget picker is now laid out as clean parallel columns — one per category — so a category (like Streaming) can no longer end up orphaned and misaligned at the bottom. Widgets are also re-grouped more intuitively: Browser now sits under Media, and Remote Control under System.
- **The "free up resources" dialog is readable again.** The Performance optimizer's confirmation dialog (the list of background apps to close, with their memory use) was too see-through — the dashboard behind it showed through and made the app names and numbers hard to read. It now sits on a solid, dimmed backdrop so every line is clearly legible.

## [v3.5.0] - 2026-07-02
### 🎛 Deck — total customization
The Deck editor grows from "pick an accent" into a full styling studio, per key and per device.
- **Gradient key faces.** A key background can now be a two-colour gradient — diagonal, vertical or radial — picked from one-tap preset pairs (sunset, ocean, royal, ember…) or composed from any two colours with the in-app picker. Gradients keep the lit-LCD look (bevel, sheen and a rim glow blending both colours) instead of turning into flat fills.
- **Photo + icon together.** A key can now hold a **background image with an icon and label on top**: the picture sits behind everything under an adjustable **darkening** scrim (0–85%) and an optional **blur** (0–20px), and when the key also has a colour or gradient the scrim tints to it — so the photo reads as a backlit key cap, not a washed-out thumbnail. This is separate from the existing "image as the whole face" mode, which still works.
- **Icon & label styling.** Colour the built-in vector icons with any colour, resize the icon (S/M/L), and style the label independently: position (below / above / hidden), size (S/M/L), bold, and its own colour.
- **Ambient key animations.** Two optional, battery-friendly cap animations: **Breathe** (the accent rim swells and relaxes) and **Sheen** (a soft light band slides across the face). They pause automatically with Performance Mode's "pause animations" and respect the system reduced-motion setting.
- **Animated GIF keys.** An uploaded GIF (up to ~900 KB) now stays animated, both as an icon and as a key backdrop — previously every upload was flattened to a static image.
- **Colors from image.** One tap extracts the dominant colours of the key's picture and builds a matching gradient face from them (same colour engine as the album-art accent).
- **Live preview.** The key editor now shows a real-size preview of the cap beside it, updating as you type and pick — background, icon, label, animation and the deck's own cap theme and shape, exactly as it will look once saved.
- **Copy / paste style, repaint a page.** The editor can copy a key's complete look (background, gradient, picture, icon/label styling, effects), paste it onto another key — also across Decks — or apply it to **every key on the current page** in one tap.
- **Whole-device themes.** The edit toolbar now restyles the entire deck: cap theme (**LCD** gloss — the classic, **Flat** minimal, **Neon** rim-glow with matching lit icons, **Glass** frost in the dashboard's Liquid Glass language), key shape (**rounded / square / circle**) and faceplate finish (**graphite / carbon fiber / brushed steel / midnight / invisible** — the last one removes the chassis so bare keys float on the dashboard).
- All of it is saved per Deck (duplicated Decks stay independent), survives restarts, travels with profile/key presets, and older Decks look exactly as before until you touch the new options.
- **Fixed: Deck keys for system shortcuts like "Show desktop" (Win+D) now behave exactly like your keyboard.** A shortcut key that uses the Windows key (Win+D, Win+E, Win+L, and similar) sometimes did nothing and "shook" to say it failed, and when Win+D did work it only minimised your windows — tapping it again never brought them back. These are shortcuts Windows itself handles no matter which window is focused, but the Deck was first switching focus to another app, which cancelled the "show desktop" toggle and, when the desktop was already showing, left nothing to switch to. Deck keys now send Windows-key shortcuts straight to the system, so Win+D reliably hides *and* restores your windows on alternating taps. App shortcuts (Ctrl+C, Alt+F4, window-snap Win+arrows…) are unaffected.

### 🔍 Sharp dashboard in iCUE widget mode — root cause found and auto-fixed (#53)
- **The blurry-dashboard-in-iCUE bug is finally understood and fixes itself.** The real cause (verified on-device): at Windows startup iCUE can associate its Xeneon Edge window with the *main* monitor's display scale instead of the Edge's own — a race with the USB display coming online, also triggered by DPI changes while iCUE runs. The dashboard then gets rendered ~1.5× too large and squeezed back onto the peanel, smearing text and thin lines. A page reload can't fix it; until now only removing and re-adding the widget in iCUE did.
- **Now the dashboard heals itself.** When it detects it is being rendered at the wrong scale inside iCUE, it asks the local server to nudge iCUE's Edge window by one pixel and back — an imperceptible move that makes iCUE re-read the correct display scale and re-render pixel-perfect at the panel's native resolution. No iCUE restart, no widget re-add, no settings to configure. If iCUE isn't running or the scale is already correct, the nudge does nothing.

### 🛡 Stability & security hardening (codebase audit)
- **Your data can no longer be corrupted by a crash mid-save.** Every saved file — settings, Deck configuration, tasks, timers, calendar events, notes, streaming sign-in tokens and lighting — is now written with a "write-to-temp-then-swap" technique, so a power loss, forced close or crash while saving can never leave a half-written file behind. Previously a badly-timed interruption could truncate one of these files, and on the next start the dashboard would silently reset that item to empty — the cause behind past reports of lost notes and Decks. A save now either fully completes or leaves the previous good copy untouched.
- **A tapped link in an Xenon AI reply can no longer run code.** Links in the assistant's answers are now restricted to normal web and email addresses (`http`, `https`, `mailto`); anything else is shown as plain text instead of a clickable link. This closes a path where content the AI read from elsewhere (a captured screen, a song title, a web result) could have slipped a booby-trapped link into a reply.
- **Websites you visit can no longer secretly control your media playback.** The play/pause, next, previous and media-source controls now carry the same cross-site protection as the mic and volume controls, so a random web page open in another tab can't skip your music or change your media source behind your back.
- **Cleaner shutdown — no leftover background processes.** Closing or restarting the server now also stops the in-game FPS reader (PresentMon) and the game-detection probe. Before, these could linger as orphaned background processes across restarts.
- **Deck "open file" keys reject a few more risky file types** (internet shortcuts, Java Web Start, ClickOnce and similar), which the registered-handler could otherwise have used to run code on a single tap. Launching apps and opening normal documents/folders is unchanged.
- **Small robustness fixes:** the per-app volume mixer no longer briefly blocks the server while reading its data, and a valid IPv6 (`[::1]`) local connection is no longer wrongly rejected.

## [v3.4.0] - 2026-07-02
### ✨ Weather — now a dashboard tile, plus choosable data sources
- **Weather can now live on the dashboard like any other widget.** Until now the forecast was only reachable from the little temperature chip in the top bar (or the lock screen); it's now also a proper tile you add from the **"+" → Productivity** palette. The tile is the **same live card as the full weather panel** — the animated sky, location, big temperature, condition and the feels‑like / wind / precipitation chips — and it **resizes cleanly** to whatever shape you give it. Alongside the card it can also show the **same detail cards, hourly timeline and 3‑day forecast as the full panel**, and you **choose which of those to show** per‑widget in Settings → Weather (turn them all off for a clean current‑conditions card, or on for a full weather board). The layout **adapts to the tile's shape** to avoid scrolling — on a wide tile the hero sits on the left with the extra sections laid out to its right (exactly like the full panel); on a tall/narrow tile they stack below. The hourly cards **stretch to fill the row**, the forecast uses elegant **iOS‑style temperature range bars** (a warm‑to‑cool gradient scaled across the days), the "now" hour is highlighted, and the whole widget carries a **subtle tint of the current sky** so it reads as one immersive scene. Tapping the card still opens the full panel. It reads the same live data as the top‑bar chip and follows your Settings → Weather city and °C/°F choice, and it now **saves like every other widget** (position, size and page persist across refreshes; removing it removes it everywhere). Existing dashboards are untouched: the tile starts hidden, ready to add when you want it.
- **You can now pick where the weather comes from — and it's more reliable.** Settings → Weather has a new **Data source** picker with three free, no-account providers: **Open-Meteo**, **MET Norway (yr.no)** and **wttr.in** (the original). The default, **Automatic**, tries them in order of reliability and instantly falls back to the next if one is down or slow — so the widget no longer goes blank or stale when a single service has a bad moment. If your readings looked slightly off, Open-Meteo and MET Norway are typically more accurate than wttr.in; just switch the source (or leave it on Automatic). Everything else — your city, °C/°F, the hourly timeline, the 3-day forecast and air quality — works the same across every source.

### 🛠 Browser widget — tabs, better site compatibility, links stop freezing the page
- **The Browser tile now has tabs.** A single Browser tile can hold several pages at once, like a normal browser: a **"+"** button in the toolbar opens a new tab, and a slim tab strip appears at the top to switch between them (each tab shows the site name and a close button). Only the tab you're looking at streams — background tabs stay loaded and ready but cost almost nothing — and your open tabs are remembered across reloads and restarts. Up to 6 tabs per tile.
- **Protected-media (DRM) sites work again.** The embedded browser wasn't loading its built-in Widevine module, so sites that need DRM — streaming services in general — could refuse to play or declare the browser unsupported. It now loads, so protected playback works.
- **The tile no longer presents itself as an automated/"headless" browser.** It now uses the normal desktop Edge identity, which some sites checked before allowing sign-in.
- **Clicking a link that opens in a new tab/window no longer freezes the page.** The Browser tile is a single view with no tab strip, so a link or button that tried to open a new tab used to spawn an invisible page and leave the visible one stuck. Such navigations — including "Continue with Google/Apple/…" style login popups — now open in place, in the same tile, so the flow completes instead of hanging.
- **New "clear site data" button in the Browser toolbar.** If a site misbehaves in the tile — refuses to load right, gets stuck, or leaves a broken cached state — this button wipes just that tile's stored data for the current site (cookies and cached storage) and reloads it from scratch. It only affects the site open in that tile (it will sign you out of it), so it asks for a confirming second tap before acting.
- **Known limitation — some sites' login pages block embedded browsers.** A few services (Twitch is the notable one) run their own anti-bot check on the username/password login form and reject any browser embedded/automated like this tile — with a "your browser is not supported" message. This is the site's decision, made live on their servers, not something the tile can spoof away, and clearing site data won't change it. Workaround: use the **"Continue with Google / Apple / Amazon"** buttons on those login screens instead of username + password — that path goes through the provider's own sign-in and usually isn't subject to the same check. Watching/browsing (without signing in) is unaffected.

### 🐛 Fixes
- **No more flickering behind the update dialog.** On some setups (weaker GPUs, or viewing the dashboard on the Xeneon Edge itself), the full-screen frosted backdrop of the "update available" dialog could flicker, because it was live-blurring the animated background (aurora/neon grid) every frame. The background is now momentarily paused while that dialog is open, so the blurred backdrop is steady — the effect looks the same, just without the flicker. (If you never saw this, it's because a strong desktop GPU renders that blur smoothly — it was hardware-dependent.)

## [v3.3.1] - 2026-07-01
### 🛠 Browser widget — no longer black until you touch the layout
- **The page now shows immediately, no longer a black rectangle until you open (and close) layout-editing mode** — and no longer black again after a full refresh. Two causes were fixed: (1) heavier pages (Google, YouTube, etc.) failed to start streaming at all — the stream was requested in the instant the page was still navigating and was silently rejected, leaving the tile black forever; it's now retried until the page is ready. (2) The live view only repainted on a change, so a page that had finished loading could sit on a stale blank frame (entering layout mode resized the tile, which was the only thing forcing a repaint); the tile now forces a fresh frame every time it (re)starts streaming or is resized. Together this also un-sticks reload/back/forward, which looked dead only because nothing was ever drawn.
- **A loading spinner now shows while a page opens**, so the tile clearly reads as "loading" during the connect/first-paint window instead of looking like a frozen black rectangle.
- **The tile detects visibility reliably inside tab groups and on other pages.** When the Browser was grouped in a tab or placed on a non-first page, it wasn't always recognised as on-screen, so it never opened. It now tracks real visibility however it's controlled (a tab, a page flip, scrolling) and streams only while actually visible, saving resources when it's off-screen.
- **Lighter, safer cleanup of leftover browser processes.** On a normal launch the startup cleanup now reaps only the exact browser Xenon itself recorded — no system-wide process scan — which is more precise (it can never touch your own Edge) and avoids a false-positive antivirus flag some users saw on 3.3.0. A broader sweep still runs, but only as a fallback if a launch is actually blocked by an older leftover process, and it no longer uses the pattern that tripped the antivirus.

## [v3.3.0] - 2026-07-01
### 🛠 Browser widget — black tile, dead addresses and silent failures fixed
- **No more working address bar over a solid black page** on some machines. The embedded browser now renders in software instead of on the GPU: `--headless=new` streamed all-black frames on many setups (older or hybrid Intel+NVIDIA/AMD graphics, or with no active graphics session), so you could type an address but the page stayed black and reload/back/forward seemed dead. Software rendering is plenty for a small tile and draws correctly everywhere.
- **Typing a plain word now searches instead of failing.** Entering `google` (no dot) used to open `https://google` and hit a DNS error; the address bar now behaves like a real browser — a bare word or phrase becomes a web search, while real addresses (`example.com`, `sub.site.co.uk/path`, `localhost:3030`, an IP) still open directly, no `https://` needed.
- **No more leftover Edge processes clogging the PC — and it self-heals.** The tile runs a headless Edge that wasn't fully shut down on close, so restarts could pile up orphaned processes that locked the browser profile and made the tile fail to start. It now tears down the whole Edge process tree when the tile is hidden/removed or the dashboard closes, and on every launch clears stale processes and profile locks (e.g. after closing the terminal window) and retries by itself — no manual cleanup ever. Edge also starts leaner (no extensions, background sync, component updates or crash reporter), so one tile is one small browser, not a cluster of helpers. If a page still can't open, the tile shows a short "try again in a moment" message instead of a technical error or a mute black rectangle.

### ✨ Xenon AI — richer dashboards it can actually build
- **It now uses tabs when asked (or when it makes sense)**: it can merge widgets into a single tabbed tile (e.g. OBS+Twitch on a streaming page, Tasks/Agenda/Notes on a work page) instead of only laying them side by side, so *"create a streaming page and use tabs where it makes sense"* is now honoured.
- **It can give a page a focal point**: the most important tile (OBS preview, music player) can be made wider than the rest instead of always splitting rows evenly, so AI-built pages look intentional.
- **It can put the same widget on more than one page**: ask to keep the media player, mic or tasks across pages and it mirrors the widget as a live copy — the manual "duplicate", now voice/chat-driven.
- **When it sets up a Deck, it can wire any kind of key**: the full range the Deck supports — open app/file/website, hotkey, webhook, soundboard clip, per-app volume, OBS scene/record/stream, Twitch/YouTube/Streamer.bot actions and more — not just a small handful, so *"set up a streaming deck"* yields a genuinely useful profile.

### ✨ Xenon AI — control your stream and per-app audio by voice/chat
- **Run your stream by voice**: with OBS, Twitch, YouTube or Streamer.bot connected, it acts on them directly — *"start recording"*, *"go live"*, *"switch to my Gioco scene"*, *"set the title to…"*, *"change the game to…"*, *"clip that"*, *"shout out @channel"*, start/stop a YouTube broadcast, trigger a Streamer.bot action. Tools appear only when the integration is set up; if one isn't connected it says so and points to Settings → Streaming instead of silently doing nothing.
- **Per-app volume by voice**: *"lower Spotify"*, *"mute Chrome"*, *"turn Discord up"* — adjust or mute one app's audio without touching master volume.

### 💅 Twitch widget — the chat is finally readable
- **The chat keeps a clean, readable block by default** instead of being squeezed under the action controls. The actions (title, category, chat message, shoutout, chat mode, ad break) keep their room on a tall tile but shrink into their own small scroll area when space is tight, so the chat always shows several messages.
- **Expanding the chat no longer hides your controls**: the expand arrow used to swap the whole actions panel out. Now the chat takes over most of the tile while the essential one-tap buttons — Go live, Mute, Clip, Marker — stay pinned above it; the wordy title/category/chat-mode fields step aside and return on collapse.

### 🧠 Xenon AI — it actually knows everything it can do
- **The assistant is now aware of its full control surface** and reaches for the right control instead of just describing it. Its briefing was a short, out-of-date list missing whole areas (RGB lighting, Performance Mode, page navigation, Deck profiles, live sensors, web search); it now has a complete picture — audio/mic, media, notes/tasks/calendar/timers, RGB lighting, system stats and sensors, opening/closing apps, locking the PC, themes, pages, panels, screen vision, plus opt-in Genesis/Streaming/Guardian tools when enabled — so requests are carried out fully, not partially. It's also told to say plainly when something genuinely isn't one of its abilities rather than pretending.
- **"What can you do?" / "can you control my PC?" now get honest answers**: it used to reply with a vague one-liner or answer "can you control my PC?" with only *monitoring*. It now leads with the truth that it actively controls the PC (not just watches it) and gives a concrete rundown of its real breadth — opening/closing apps, audio/mic and device switching, media, RGB lighting, locking the PC, live stats and sensors, appearance and exact colours, preferences, pages and panels, screen vision, plus your enabled opt-in tools (including confirmed Windows commands when PC Control is on) — kept short by voice and offered to expand.
- **It replies in the language you used**, spoken or typed: an out-loud question in Italian no longer gets an English answer just because the interface language is English.

### 🛠 Xenon AI voice — cleaner long answers, mic no longer opens early
- **Long spoken answers no longer overflow the voice screen**: lengthy replies used to render as one giant block of centered text running off the display, asterisks and all. They now shrink to a readable size, tidy stray bullet markers and scroll within the view — and in voice mode the assistant is told to keep it to a sentence or two and offer to go deeper rather than reciting a list.
- **The mic waits for Xenon to finish speaking before re-opening**: on longer replies it could re-open while the assistant was still talking and catch the tail of its own voice. The server (which knows when playback ends) now drives the hand-off, with a slightly longer pause after, so listening resumes only once the voice has stopped.
- **A confirmation card pauses listening until you close it**: when the PC-Control card appears during a voice session, Xenon stops listening behind it (so it can't catch your reply as a new command) and resumes only after you confirm or cancel.
- **The PC-Control card fits the screen**: a long command plus output could run off the bottom and hide the buttons; the card is now bounded to the screen and scrolls internally, with Consenti/Chiudi pinned and always reachable.

### ✨ Xenon AI — fine-grained control of look, preferences and devices
- **Set exact colours, not just named themes**: *"make the accent orange"*, *"usa lo sfondo #0b0b0b"*, *"modalità chiara"* apply precise accent/background/text colours and the light/dark/auto mode, not just one of the five presets.
- **Change dashboard preferences by voice/chat**: 12h/24h clock, temperature unit (°C/°F), interface language, weather location (auto or a city), and which widgets appear on the focus lock screen — all adjustable, applied live and saved.
- **Switch audio devices and media source hands-free**: *"switch to my headphones"*, *"usa il microfono USB"* — it lists your output/input devices and sets the one you name (and offers options if the name doesn't match), and can choose which app Now Playing follows (*"segui Spotify"*, *"torna automatico"*).

### 🔐 Xenon AI — optional "PC Control" for anything else (opt-in, always confirmed)
- **A new off-by-default option (Settings → Funzioni AI → "Controllo PC")** lets the assistant do things no built-in tool covers by proposing a Windows command — but nothing runs on its own. A confirmation card shows the **exact command** and a plain-language summary; it executes **only** after you tap *"Consenti ed esegui"*, with the result shown there. The command is decided and stored server-side and can't be altered by the page, the feature stays inert until switched on, and the assistant prefers its dedicated tools and flags anything risky first. Proposed commands are self-sufficient — e.g. creating a missing folder before writing a file into it — so a reasonable request succeeds first try.
- **It asks when genuinely unsure**: for ambiguous or potentially big/irreversible requests it asks one short clarifying question first, while still acting immediately when intent is clear.

## [v3.2.12] - 2026-06-30
### 🛠 Fixes — screen flickering (continued)
- **Less chance of the whole dashboard flickering while music is playing**, especially on hybrid-graphics laptops (those with both an Intel and an NVIDIA/AMD GPU). When a track is playing, the Media tile shows a soft blurred copy of the album cover behind it. That blurred layer was being kept permanently prepared on the GPU even when no music was playing — an always-on, full-size blurred surface that costs graphics memory for nothing and, on machines that switch between two GPUs, is exactly the kind of layer that can make the browser flicker the entire window. It is now prepared only while a cover is actually on screen and costs nothing when idle, which both lightens the load and removes a flicker trigger. The blurred ambient background glow was also isolated so that other things appearing on screen (like that cover) no longer force the browser to redraw the full-screen glow underneath them. This targets a Chromium-level flickering issue with blurred layers on dual-GPU setups; if it still flickers on such a machine, switching the dashboard's browser to a single GPU (Windows → Graphics settings) or turning off browser hardware acceleration is the remaining workaround.

## [v3.2.11] - 2026-06-30
### 🛠 Fixes — screen flickering
- **The dashboard no longer flickers when you have a custom image or video background**: the animated neon grid was being drawn *on top of* a custom wallpaper (only the softer "aurora" glow was correctly hidden behind one). On its own that's just visual clutter, but combined with the fix below it was also the most visible part of a flicker some people saw. The neon grid now hides itself whenever you set a custom background — exactly like the aurora already did — so your wallpaper (the forest video, a photo, anything you picked) shows cleanly with nothing animating over it. Turn off your custom background and the grid returns as before.
- **No more brief flicker while you close windows or Alt-Tab around the desktop**: the dashboard automatically pauses its animated background effects while a full-screen game is running ("game mode"). As you closed windows and tidied up, the focused window could momentarily *look* full-screen for a fraction of a second, which flipped game mode on and then straight back off — fading the ambient background out and in each time, seen as a flicker that stopped the instant you touched the dashboard (which brings it back into focus). Game mode now waits for the state to actually settle before reacting, so those split-second focus changes are ignored and the background stays steady. Pausing for a real game you start is unaffected. (Fixes the *"Screen flickering"* report.)

## [v3.2.10] - 2026-06-29
### 🛠 Fixes — Xenon AI voice input
- **The voice assistant no longer "goes quiet" while you're still mid-sentence**: a voice turn was force-stopped after a fixed **8 seconds**, so anything you said past that point was simply cut off — exactly the "sometimes it stops listening while I'm talking" report. The real end-of-turn is now driven by silence detection on the server, which stops the moment you actually finish speaking (about 2–3 seconds after you go quiet); the hard timer is now only a much longer **30-second** safety net for runaway recordings, so a normal multi-second sentence is never clipped. You can still stop it instantly at any time by tapping the screen, and tapping the orb restarts listening.
- **"Detected and active, but it doesn't hear me" no longer ends in a silent dead-end**: when a recording came back empty — a missed first word, a slow start, or a too-quiet mic — the whole voice session used to close without a word, which felt like a hang. Xenon now keeps listening and gives you another couple of tries with an on-screen *"Didn't catch that — try again"* hint, and only then ends the turn with a clear message pointing you to **Settings → Xenon AI** to check your microphone device and sensitivity. So instead of a mysterious silence you get a system that keeps listening when you mean to talk, stops when you're done, and tells you what to check if it genuinely can't hear you.
- **Switching your microphone now actually takes effect without restarting the server**: on setups that capture through DirectShow, Xenon bound to whichever microphone was the Windows default *when the server started* and never re-checked — so plugging in a headset and selecting it as your input did nothing, and recordings kept reading the old (often silent) device. Xenon now notices when your default microphone changes and re-binds its voice capture to the new device on the fly, so picking your headset just works.
- **New "Microphone test" button so you can confirm voice input works in 3 seconds** (Settings → Xenon AI): voice input records *server-side*, from a device that can differ from the one the Mic panel's level meter shows — which is why a mic could look "active" yet never be heard. The test runs that exact capture path for ~3 seconds and tells you plainly whether you were heard, **which device** was actually captured and at **what level (dB)**. If it didn't hear you it points you to fix it (pick another default mic, raise sensitivity). It's also the fastest way to report a problem: the result line is everything a maintainer needs in a single screenshot.

## [v3.2.9] - 2026-06-28
### 🛠 Fixes
- **The performance-optimization popup no longer keeps coming back after you dismiss it**: with automatic Performance Mode on, focusing a tracked app or game (OBS, a game, your editor…) opens the "optimize your PC" sheet so you can pick what to apply. Pressing **Cancel** hid it — but it didn't *remember* that you said no, so the moment that app regained focus the sheet popped up all over again, nagging you on every Alt-Tab back. Dismissing the sheet (Cancel or tapping outside it) now snoozes that activity for the rest of the session, exactly like the auto-suggest banner's "Ignore" already did, so it stays out of your way. Choosing **Apply** is unaffected, and the next fresh session still offers to optimize as before.

### ℹ️ Known issue — occasional soft rendering inside the iCUE widget at boot
On the Xeneon Edge the dashboard can occasionally look soft inside the iCUE widget — fuzzy text and thin lines — while the exact same dashboard stays razor sharp in a normal browser. We traced this all the way down and it is **not** a fault in the dashboard: it is an iCUE/QtWebEngine startup-timing issue. iCUE creates the widget's renderer at Windows logon, sometimes **before the Edge (a USB display) has finished being set up**, so the renderer is assigned the wrong display scale and the page is drawn at a size that doesn't match the panel, then resampled onto it — which is what smears the detail. That scale is then **frozen for the life of that renderer**, so a page refresh can't fix it (it reuses the same renderer and the same wrong scale).

The v3.2.9 attempt to correct this from inside the page (an auto-reload whenever the load came up mis-scaled) has been **removed**: we verified on-device that it cannot work — a refresh reuses the same renderer and therefore the same frozen scale, so it never recovers. (The earlier v3.2.8 page-zoom correction is left in place but only ever engages on a fractional-DPR wide-bar render and is a no-op at the panel's native scale; it cannot rebuild detail lost to resampling either.) In short: the render scale is set by iCUE and is not changeable or re-rolled from page-side code.

**Workaround that does work:** if the dashboard comes up soft after a PC restart, **remove and re-add the web widget in iCUE once** (re-creating it forces a brand-new renderer, which reads the now-stable display scale and renders crisp); it then stays sharp until the next restart. This is being reported to CORSAIR as the proper place to fix it (re-evaluate the web-widget's device scale *after* the USB display is enumerated).

## [v3.2.8] - 2026-06-25
### 🛠 Fixes
- **The dashboard no longer goes blurry when it runs inside iCUE on the Xeneon Edge**: in *iCUE Widgets* mode the dashboard could look soft and grainy — fuzzy text, pixelated thin lines and chart strokes — while the very same dashboard opened in a normal browser ("Desktop" mode) stayed razor sharp. The cause is that iCUE renders the page at a *fractional* display scale, so 1-pixel lines land between physical pixels and get smeared. Xenon already corrected for this by realigning the page to a whole-pixel scale, but it only did so **once, at startup** — and inside iCUE that scale isn't stable: it can read one way as the widget first loads and then shift after the widget settles, after the screen sleeps and wakes, or after a re-layout. So the correction got "stuck" on an outdated value, which is exactly why the blur came and went seemingly at random ("sometimes sharp, sometimes not"). The correction is now **re-evaluated live** whenever the display scale or the widget size changes, applying — or cleanly removing — itself to match the current state, so the dashboard stays crisp from the moment it loads and through sleep/wake and layout changes. It also now only nudges the scale when doing so genuinely sharpens the picture: on the common case where the display is already rendering near the panel's native resolution, it leaves the page completely alone instead of shrinking it (shrinking was softening the image rather than helping). Normal desktop and laptop browsers are untouched as before. (Fixes the *"Dashboard blurry in iCUE Widgets mode"* report.)
- **Thin curved outlines (the weather pill, the round chat buttons, the topbar buttons) look cleaner on the Xeneon Edge**: with the blur above resolved, a subtler artefact remained — those small *curved* 1-pixel borders could still look slightly jagged or broken up. This is because iCUE does a final, uneven rescale of the widget onto the panel that no page-side fix can fully undo, and a hairline thin line is the most fragile thing to put through it. Those few outlines now use a slightly more solid line (and the weather sun's soft glow is tightened) so they hold together through that rescale. This is a **device-only** refinement — it applies solely on the Xeneon Edge's wide fractional-scale display and changes nothing on a normal monitor.

## [v3.2.7] - 2026-06-24
### 🛠 Fixes
- **The one-click update finally works instead of always saying "Preparation failed"**: every in-app update since v3.2.4 stopped at *"Preparation failed — you can download manually"*, forcing a manual download. The cause was a typo in the release version itself — `package.json` shipped its version as `v3.2.6` (with a stray leading "v") while the safety check that validates a freshly-downloaded build expects plain `3.2.6`, so the two never matched and the update was rejected every time. The version is now clean semver again, and the validation tolerates a stray "v" on either side so this can't come back. **Why it matters:** because the auto-update kept failing, people downloaded releases by hand and, when replacing their folder, sometimes wiped their `server\data` — losing notes, Deck keys and settings. With the one-click update working again, the updater swaps files *in place* and never touches your data, so notes and Decks carry over automatically. Existing installs stuck on v3.2.4–v3.2.6 can update to this release one last time from the GitHub releases page; from here on, in-app updates work on their own.
- **The update popup no longer shows a doubled version like "from vv3.2.4"**: the same stray "v" leaked into the "Update available" dialog. Versions are now always rendered cleanly (`v3.2.6 · from v3.2.4`).
- **A failed update preparation now tells you *why***: instead of a blind "Preparation failed", the dialog now appends the reason (for example `version_mismatch` or `download_failed`), so a problem can be diagnosed from a screenshot instead of guessed at.
- **Deleting a page no longer leaves stale tile state behind**: removing a page already hides its widgets (restorable from the "+" palette), but a hidden widget kept the size and position it had on the now-deleted page — leftover saved state for a layout that no longer exists. Its geometry is now reset to the default on page removal, so nothing stale accumulates and a re-added widget gets a clean slot. (The layout already drops orphaned tab-groups, duplicated copies and invalid page references on every load, so dead state never piles up.)

## [v3.2.6] - 2026-06-23
### 🛠 Fixes
- Updated package.json version

## [v3.2.5] - 2026-06-23
- **Deleting a page now really removes everything on it** — including duplicated/tab-grouped tiles: previously, deleting a page hid its normal widgets and removed its duplicated *standalone* tiles, but any **tab-group** on that page (for example a duplicated Playback + Chat tile) was left behind and silently moved onto another page, so it kept reappearing no matter how many times you deleted. A duplicated tile's instances are now cleared along with the page, so "delete the page" actually deletes all of its widgets. Removing one duplicated tab from a tab tile (its **×**) now deletes that copy outright too, instead of leaving a stray standalone copy behind.
- **Overlapping tiles no longer show two widgets stacked on top of each other** (e.g. a Media+Chat tab tile where *Playback* and *Chat* both looked selected and the chat bled through behind the player, with a doubled message box): if two tiles ended up parked on the exact same spot on a page — for instance after duplicating a tab group — the dashboard drew them one on top of the other, so the hidden tab of the back tile showed through the front one. The dashboard now detects this and slides the stacked tile down into the first free space when the page loads, leaving the original tile and every other tile exactly where they were. Healthy layouts are untouched.


### ✨ New Features
- **Choose your clock format — 12-hour or 24-hour**: a new **Clock** option under **Settings → Appearance** lets you pick how the time is shown on the dashboard and the lock screen — **Auto** (follows your selected language, the previous behaviour), **12-hour** (with AM/PM) or **24-hour**. Until now the format was tied to the language with no way to override it, so an English user was stuck with AM/PM and couldn't switch to 24-hour. Your choice is saved and applies instantly to both clocks. (This also fixes a quiet inconsistency where the dashboard clock and the lock-screen clock could disagree on 12h vs 24h.)

### 🛠 Fixes
- **Your notes now reappear on their own after an update instead of looking blank**: occasionally after downloading a new version the Notes tile came up empty, even though the notes were perfectly safe — visible again as soon as you reopened the dashboard. The cause was timing: if the page reloaded a split second before the server had finished restarting, the one-time fetch of your notes failed and was never retried, so the box stayed empty until a manual refresh. Notes now retry loading on their own (with a short back-off) until they come through, so the tile repopulates by itself. Your notes were never lost — they live on the server — but now you won't have to reload to see them.
- **Reproducing a saved page no longer loses the System / Volume / Microphone tabs when you delete the other page**: if you saved a page that included the System tile and added it onto a new page, the live System panel (which physically hosts the Volume and Microphone tabs) only ever existed on one of the two pages. Deleting *that* page parked the live panel away and left the surviving page showing a dead, stats-less copy — your Volume and Microphone tabs vanished from the page you wanted to keep. Deleting a page now keeps the live System panel on the page you're keeping, so its Volume and Microphone tabs persist as expected. (Independent tiles like a Deck or Browser are unaffected — each copy keeps its own keys/address as before.)
- **Dropdown menus no longer get cut off at the edge of the screen**: on the short Xeneon Edge display, opening a dropdown whose list didn't fit (for example the Deck key editor's *LED reaction* "One-shot / Follows state" picker) could leave the options spilling past the bottom of the screen, where you couldn't reach them. Open dropdowns now always size and position themselves to stay fully on screen — scrolling inside the menu when the list is taller than the space available — so every option is reachable.
- **The one-click update no longer needs a Windows admin (UAC) prompt when Xenon is installed in your own folder**: the in-app updater always asked for administrator rights, which popped Windows' UAC dialog on the *primary* monitor — unreachable on multi-monitor or touchscreen setups like the Xeneon Edge, where users couldn't find or tap it and the update simply never proceeded. The updater now checks whether your install folder is writable (the normal case, when Xenon is unzipped to Desktop/Downloads): if so it applies the update directly with **no UAC prompt at all**. It only falls back to asking for administrator rights when the install really is in a protected location (e.g. Program Files). Note: this improvement takes effect for updates starting *from this version onward* — to get here, install this release once manually from the GitHub releases page.

## [v3.2.4] - 2026-06-17

### 🛠 Fixes
- **Deck hotkeys that use the Win key now actually fire** (Win+D, Win+E, …): after building a Win-based combo in the new composer, tapping the key did nothing. The Win key is a Windows "extended" key and was being sent without the flag that marks it as such, so Windows never saw a real Win press — only Ctrl/Alt/Shift combos worked. Win (and the navigation keys) are now sent correctly, so the whole composer works end to end.
- **The in-app update no longer gets stuck on "Updating…" with nothing happening**: when Xenon was running with administrator rights, the updater backed up your install and then silently stopped before swapping in the new files — leaving the dashboard frozen on "Updating…" and the server shut down. The cause: the already-elevated update helper kept running as a child of the app, so when the app stopped itself mid-update Windows killed the helper along with it. The helper now always relaunches itself as an independent process first, so the swap completes and the app restarts on its own. (Your data is backed up and automatically rolled back on any failure, so nothing is ever lost.)

## [v3.2.2] - 2026-06-17

### 🛠 Fixes
- **Recording a Deck hotkey no longer fires the shortcut while you set it up**: assigning a combo like **Win+D** used to trigger it the moment you pressed the keys (minimising your desktop) instead of just capturing it — because a web page can't stop Windows from acting on its own system shortcuts. The hotkey field is now a **composer**: tap the **Ctrl / Shift / Alt / Win** chips to choose modifiers, then press just the single main key (a lone key triggers nothing). Win+D becomes "tap *Win*, press *D*" — captured cleanly, never fired. Holding modifiers while you press the main key still works for safe combos like Ctrl+Shift+M.
- **Your installed local AI models now appear in the model picker**: under Settings → Xenon AI (local provider), the Model dropdown only offered the preset tiers (Light / Balanced / Powerful / Advanced) and a "Custom" field — models you'd actually pulled into Ollama were hidden unless you typed their exact tag by hand. The dropdown now lists every installed model under an **Installed** group, so you can select one directly; the list refreshes whenever the local AI panel opens.
- **A duplicated System panel now keeps its Sistema / Volume / Microfono tabs**: copying the System tile — or reproducing a saved page onto a new one — used to leave a stats-only panel with the Volume and Microphone tabs missing. Duplicates now carry the full tab bar with working tab switching, and every tab stays live (stats, network, volume and mic levels all mirror the original in real time). Each copy switches its own tabs independently of the original.
- **A duplicated Media player now keeps its proper layout instead of looking broken**: when you added a second Media tile, the artwork and the title/controls collapsed into a misaligned stack because the playback layout was tied to the original tile's internal name (which copies don't carry). The layout is now style-based, so every Media copy lays out exactly like the original — artwork on the left, track info and controls on the right.
- **Adding the Microphone (or Audio, Notes, Tasks, Calendar, Timer) to another page no longer makes it vanish from where it already was**: these widgets live inside a host tile by default — the Microphone and Audio sit in the **System** panel's tabs, and Notes/Tasks/Calendar/Timer in the **Agenda** panel — so adding one from another page's **+** menu used to *move* that single content over, leaving an empty gap where it had been. Adding it now creates an independent **copy** instead and leaves the original exactly where it was, so you really can have the mic (or any of these) in two places at once. Their live state (mute, level, lists, countdowns) stays mirrored across every copy as before.
- **No more duplicate "Genesis" toasts on top of the AI's own reply**: when you ask Xenon to build a dashboard, the assistant's reply already tells you what it created — but a *"Page created"* / *"Deck set up"* toast also popped up over the open AI overlay, overlapping the message. Those Genesis toasts are now shown only when the AI overlay is closed (for example when Genesis is triggered from a Deck key without the chat open), so they stay useful without doubling up on what the assistant just said.

### ✨ Improvements
- **Performance Mode settings are clearer, and Automatic mode can now ask before closing apps**: the two overlapping switches — *"Suggest automatically"* and *"Apply by itself"* — have been replaced by a single, easy-to-read **Mode** selector with three choices: **Manual** (only optimizes when you press *Optimize now*), **Suggest** (shows a prompt when an activity starts), and **Automatic** (applies the safe, reversible tweaks by itself and restores them when the activity ends). A short line under the selector explains what the chosen mode does, and the per-activity list is hidden in Manual mode where it doesn't apply. On top of that, **Automatic mode now opens the optimization panel when *"Offer to close background apps"* is on** — so even hands-off, you still get to choose which background apps to close (and review the Xenon AI plan, when AI is enabled) instead of that step being skipped silently; the resulting session is still treated as automatic and restores itself when you stop the activity. With app-closing off, Automatic mode stays fully silent as before.

## [v3.2.1] - 2026-06-15

### 🛠 Fixes
- **Fresh installs no longer end with "127.0.0.1 refused to connect"**: on a brand-new setup the installer could silently fail to install the widget's dependencies, so the server crashed the instant it started and the dashboard showed `ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED` even though every other setup step looked successful. The cause was a Windows quirk: the installer asked the system for "npm" and got handed npm's PowerShell wrapper (`npm.ps1`), which — when launched through the command prompt — Windows *opened in Notepad* instead of running, so `npm install` never actually ran, the `node_modules` folder stayed empty, and the server (which needs the `ws` package just to start) exited immediately. The installer now runs npm reliably by calling Node directly, **checks that all three required packages are really present** before and after installing (instead of assuming success from an exit code), and clearly tells you to run `npm install` manually if anything still didn't land. Anyone who already hit this can simply re-run `INSTALL.bat` with this version, or run `npm install` once in the Xenon folder.

## [v3.2.0] - 2026-06-15

### ✨ New Features
- **New "Browser" widget — a live, interactive web page inside the dashboard**: add it from a page's **+** menu (under *System*) and you get a real, controllable browser tile right on the Xeneon Edge — type an address and browse, tap links, scroll and type, with Back / Forward / Reload and an **expand-to-fullscreen** button. Unlike a plain embed it works with sites that normally refuse to be framed (YouTube, Google, most web apps), because it's driven by a dedicated headless Microsoft Edge under the hood rather than an `<iframe>`. It's built to be light: a tile only does any work **while it's actually on screen** — switch to another page and it stops streaming immediately, and the background Edge shuts itself down once no Browser tile is open, so an added-but-unused widget costs nothing. You can add several Browser tiles (each remembers its own address), and the whole thing is local-only — the page stream never leaves your PC. *Notes for this first version: it needs **Microsoft Edge** installed (it is, on every Windows 11 — the widget shows a clear message if not), and the tile shows **video only, no sound** (the page is rendered headless for efficiency) — a known limitation we may revisit.*
- **New "Second screen" widget — a real extra Windows desktop inside the dashboard**: add it from a page's **+** menu (under *System*) to get a genuine second monitor you can see and control from the Xeneon Edge — drag any app onto it, then tap, scroll and type to drive it, with an **expand-to-fullscreen** button. It's **one-click to set up**: the tile installs a signed virtual-display driver and creates the extra screen for you (just accept the Windows prompts); if a step can't be automated — winget missing, or a restart needed to finish — it tells you exactly what to do rather than failing silently. Like the Browser tile it's built to be light: it only streams **while it's actually on screen** and **pauses automatically while you game** (the same *"Pause heavy tiles"* Performance option), so an open-but-unused tile costs nothing, and a static desktop barely sends any frames. Everything stays local — the screen never leaves your PC. You can fine-tune it in **Settings → Second screen** (smoothness up to **60 FPS**, image quality and the virtual display's resolution) — picking a resolution now applies it to the virtual monitor instantly, without re-installing anything or rebooting (including ultra-wide modes like 2560×720 so the view fills the Xeneon Edge bar with no side bars). When the virtual screen's shape doesn't match the tile, a **fit toggle** on the tile lets you choose between *filling the tile edge-to-edge* (cropping the overflow) and *showing the whole screen* (letterboxed) — your choice is remembered. The **mouse pointer is now drawn into the view**, so you can always see where you're pointing (the capture previously never included the cursor, which made the virtual screen feel uncontrollable). Touch behaves naturally on a large tile: by default a **swipe scrolls the dashboard** (so the tile no longer swallows your page swipes) while a **tap clicks** in the virtual screen — both at once, no mode switch. A toolbar **toggle** flips to *full control* when you need to drag inside the screen (window moves, sliders, text selection). The toolbar buttons were also enlarged for touch. The screen now also **persists properly**: it stays set up across restarts and automatically returns to your chosen resolution (Windows otherwise resets a virtual monitor to a tiny default after a reboot), so you never have to set it up again. When you're done with it, **Rimuovi schermo** removes the virtual monitor cleanly, now with a confirmation first. *Notes for this first version: it needs the **Xenon Helper** companion (installed by INSTALL.bat; the tile shows a clear message if it's missing), the live view is **video only, no sound**, and some hardware-accelerated/DRM-protected windows (certain video players) may show black — ordinary apps capture fine.*
- **Performance Mode now frees the Browser tile while you game**: a new option in **Settings → Performance** — *"Pause heavy tiles while gaming"* (on by default) — automatically suspends the Browser widget's live stream while a game is running or an optimization session is active, then resumes it on its own when you're done. Because the stream is what costs resources, pausing it (and letting the background Edge shut down) means an open Browser tile takes essentially nothing away from your game. Prefer to keep it live mid-game? Just turn the option off. This also covers the future second-screen tile.
- **Deck → Streamer.bot actions**: a new Deck action lets a key fire any of your **Streamer.bot** actions directly, so you can drive Twitch/YouTube/Kick automations, OBS scenes, sound effects, chat commands and everything else you've built in Streamer.bot from a Xenon Deck button — including a **second PC**, since Xenon connects out to wherever Streamer.bot is running (point the host at that PC's LAN address). Set it up in **Settings → Streaming → Streamer.bot**: enter the WebSocket Server host, port (default `8080`) and password (only if you enabled authentication), then **Verifica connessione** confirms it's reachable and shows how many actions were found. In the Deck key editor, **Streamer.bot: esegui azione** then offers a dropdown of your live actions to pick from. The connection is opened only when needed and closes itself when idle, so an unconfigured or unused Streamer.bot costs nothing.
- **More native Twitch Deck actions**: alongside the existing clip / marker / ad-break keys, a connected Twitch channel now gets five more one-tap actions in the Deck editor — **set the stream title**, **change the category/game** (just type the game name; Xenon resolves it for you), **send a chat message**, **shout out another channel**, and **switch chat mode** (emote-only, followers-only, subscribers-only, slow, or back to normal). Note: these need a few extra Twitch permissions, so if you connected Twitch before this update, reconnect once in **Settings → Streaming → Twitch** to grant them.
- **The Twitch dashboard widget gained the full action set, reorganised for clarity**: the widget's Actions card now holds everything in tidy groups — a quick row (Go live, Mute, Clip, Marker), inline fields to **set the title**, **set the category**, **send a chat message** and **shout out a channel** (type and press Enter or the send button), and a clearly labelled **Chat mode** and **Ad break** selector. The stray, unlabelled "30s" box is gone — it's now plainly the **Ad break** duration next to its Run button. Actions that only work while you're live (clip, marker, ad, shoutout) dim when the channel is offline; title, category and chat work anytime.
- **Expand the Twitch chat to fill the widget**: a new toggle in the chat card's header blows the chat up to the full widget (hiding the action controls) for read-along streaming, then collapses it back to the normal split layout — your other cards keep their own hide/order settings.
- **Deck action picker now shows what you're missing**: the OBS, Twitch / YouTube, Streamer.bot and Remote-control categories used to vanish completely from the Deck key editor until each service was set up — so it wasn't obvious those actions even existed. They now always appear, shown as a greyed, locked hint that points you to the right place (e.g. *"Connect Twitch/YouTube in Settings → Streaming"*) and turn into the full action list the moment the service is connected.
- **Update notifications with an in-app "What's new"**: Xenon now tells you when a newer version is out instead of leaving you to check GitHub. At startup, if an update is available, a tidy dialog shows the new version and its **release notes rendered nicely** right inside the dashboard — with a **Download** button, **Later**, and **Don't show again** (so it never nags you twice for the same version). When one is available you get a **red notification dot** on the **Settings** button (and on the in-Settings update pill) that clears itself once you've updated; the manual **Check for updates** button only shows when you're already up to date, so there's never a confusing pair of buttons. The check is local-friendly and private: the server asks GitHub for the latest release at most once a day (and only on demand for the manual button), and if you're offline it simply stays quiet.
- **Redesigned notifications**: every in-app notice — calendar reminders, finished timers, update messages, Genesis/Guardian/backup confirmations — now uses **one unified, polished toast**. Before, reminders and updates shared a single card with a fixed clock icon (so an update notice oddly showed a clock), while finished timers used a totally different little pill — inconsistent and easy to misread. The new toasts are **colour- and icon-coded by type** (reminder, timer, success, update, warning, error), **stack neatly** when several arrive instead of overwriting each other, show a progress bar that **pauses when you hover**, and can be dismissed individually. Cleaner, clearer, and much nicer to look at.
- **One-click update (optional)**: from the same dialog you can now also let Xenon update itself. It works in two safe steps — first **Update now** downloads and verifies the new version in the background *without touching your running install*, then **Apply & restart** swaps it in and relaunches. Your settings, notes, calendar and everything under your data folder are preserved, and if anything goes wrong the previous version is automatically restored from a backup. The manual **Download** button is still there as a fallback, and self-update is automatically disabled for developer (git) checkouts.
- **Remote control: "On-demand startup" — stop Sunshine and Tailscale from running 24/7**: setting up remote PC control installs Sunshine and Tailscale, and their own installers register them to **start with Windows and stay running**, even when you never connect from your phone. A new **On-demand startup** toggle in the Remote Control panel (and dashboard widget) flips both services to manual start, so they no longer launch at boot — Xenon then starts them only when you **enable** remote control and stops them when you **disable** it. One administrator (UAC) prompt applies the change; turning it back off restores the always-on default. Less idle background, smaller attack surface, and no Tailscale VPN connection sitting open when you're not using it.

### 🛠 Fixes
- **Streamer.bot connection now actually works** (it always failed before): **Verifica connessione** reported *"Streamer.bot non raggiungibile"* and the Deck couldn't list or fire your Streamer.bot actions, even though Streamer.bot showed the Xenon client connected and *Authenticated: True*. The cause was deep: Streamer.bot's WebSocket Server compresses its replies, and the WebSocket client Xenon used (the one built into Node.js) silently corrupts those compressed messages into empty data — so every reply (the login acknowledgement, the action list, …) was lost and the request eventually timed out. Xenon now uses a WebSocket client that decodes the compression correctly, so authenticating, listing actions and firing them all work. The connect/request timeouts were also raised and the test button now shows the underlying reason when something genuinely fails. *(OBS was unaffected because OBS-websocket doesn't use that compression.)*
- **The Twitch widget no longer shows "Connect in Settings" when your account is already connected**: the "not linked" banner was stuck on permanently — a styling rule kept it visible even after the attribute that should hide it was set — so a fully connected channel still nagged you to connect. It now correctly disappears once Twitch is linked.
- **The Twitch widget now makes it clear when your account isn't linked** (instead of a confusing empty "OFFLINE" panel): the widget's live status, channel name, chat and the Clip/Marker/Ad buttons all need Xenon to be connected to your Twitch account — but the **Go live** button works without it, because it drives OBS. So you could go live (and really be live on Twitch via OBS) while the panel still showed "— / OFFLINE" with an empty chat, with no hint why. The widget now says **"Not linked"** rather than a misleading "Offline" when the account isn't connected, and shows a **tap-to-fix banner** that jumps straight to *Settings → Streaming* to connect it. (Connecting still needs your own Twitch app **Client ID** — Twitch/YouTube can't ship one in an open-source project.)
- **A connected Twitch/YouTube account no longer asks you to re-enter your Client ID**: the app credentials are stored server-side and never sent back to the browser, so when they couldn't be read (for example a `TWITCH_CLIENT_ID` set via environment variable rather than saved in Settings), the **Settings → Streaming** card showed the setup form even though the account was connected. A live connection now keeps its connected state and, if the credentials can't be found, shows a **warning plus a re-entry form** so you can save them here and keep it working across restarts.
- **The media panel now tells Twitch, YouTube and SoundCloud apart instead of labelling every browser "YouTube"**: Windows only tells Xenon *which app* is playing (your browser), never *which site*, so anything playing in Chrome/Edge/Firefox was stamped "YouTube" — watching a Twitch stream still showed the YouTube badge. Xenon now reads the browser tab actually making sound and shows the **real service, with its official logo** — Twitch, YouTube or SoundCloud. It **remembers the stream while it plays**, so the right service (and logo) stays put even after you switch to another tab or window. The **source dropdown** (shown when more than one thing is playing) now matches the badge too. When a site genuinely can't be identified it honestly names the **browser itself**, shown with that browser's own icon, rather than guessing "YouTube".
- **Game mode no longer mistakes the Steam client for a game**: after you closed a game, Steam's own window (Big Picture / the library, which is a full-screen-capable browser-style surface) could be read as a running game — so the **Game Companion pill stayed up labelled "Steamwebhelper"** and ambient effects kept pausing as if you were still playing. The Steam client is now excluded from game detection (a real game always runs as its own program), while titles that merely start with "Steam" — like *SteamWorld* — are still detected normally.

## [v3.1.1] - 2026-06-13

### ✨ Improvements
- **The "+" add-widget menu now fits on screen without scrolling**: the popover that opens from a page's **+** button used to stack every category in one tall column, so on the wide-but-short Xeneon Edge display the bottom widgets (and their categories) were cut off and you had to scroll to reach them. It's now a tidy **multi-column layout** — each category sits in its own column side by side — so the whole list is visible at a glance and adapts to the available width (fewer columns on a narrow window, more on a wide one).
- **Reuse a Deck profile on a newly added Deck**: now that each Deck is independent (below), a freshly added Deck rightly starts with a single empty profile — but its **profile menu now lists the profiles you already built on your other Decks**, and tapping one **copies it in** (every key included — the new Deck's grid grows if needed so none are dropped) and makes it active. It's a copy, so the two Decks stay independent and editing it here never touches the original. This means you no longer have to save a profile as a preset first just to reuse it — though saved **profile presets** still appear in the same menu as before.
- **Each Deck is now its own Deck**: previously every Deck on the dashboard shared one pool of keys, so adding a second Deck showed it already full, and editing a key on one changed it on all of them — confusing, and the source of layouts getting reshuffled across restarts. Now **every Deck is independent**: it has its own keys, profiles and grid, a newly added Deck starts **empty**, and editing one never touches another. Your existing Deck and its keys are kept exactly as they are on update (each Deck you currently see keeps what it shows); from there on they're simply no longer linked. To copy a configuration from one Deck to another, save it as a **profile preset** and insert it on the other — the clean, explicit way. *(The Deck no longer mirrors itself across pages when duplicated; other duplicated widgets, which mirror live data like CPU or the current track, are unchanged.)*
- **Deck tile no longer offers a misleading "save as preset"**: a layout preset stores placement only, so on a standalone Deck — which now owns its keys per-instance — it would have restored an **empty** grid. That bookmark is gone from standalone Deck tiles; to save and reuse a Deck's keys, use the Deck's own **profile preset** (the bookmark inside the Deck's profile menu). Tab-group and page presets are unchanged.

### 🛠 Fixes
- **A Deck key edit no longer gets lost after a restart — Deck saving rebuilt on a single source of truth**: the Deck used to be saved by every open dashboard (the Xeneon Edge display, a browser tab on the PC, …) pushing its *entire* copy of all Decks to the server, with "whose copy wins" decided by counters each one kept on its own. Those counters aren't comparable across devices, so a dashboard you hadn't used in a while could come back after a reboot, look "newest" by its own count, and overwrite everything — reverting a key you'd just changed and even wiping a Deck it had never seen. That whole mechanism is gone. Now the **server owns the saved Decks** and every dashboard sends **only the precise change you actually made** ("this key on this Deck changed", "this Deck was removed"), kept in a small local outbox and **retried until the server confirms it** — so an edit made while the server is restarting still lands, and a stale dashboard simply has nothing to send and can never overwrite or delete anything. Crucially, this now holds even for a dashboard still running the *previous* version's Deck code (e.g. a browser tab you left open before updating): its old "push everything" save is now accepted **additively** — it can only restore a Deck the server is missing entirely, never overwrite one that's already there — so it can no longer race in after a reboot and revert the button you just changed. As a bonus, when you edit a Deck on one screen, **every other open dashboard updates live** within a moment instead of after a reload. Nothing changes in how you use the Deck. *(This release also fixes the deeper reason the loss kept happening: a Deck key with an **image icon** makes the saved data large, and the save was being sent in a "survives page close" mode that browsers cap at 64KB — so once a Deck held a couple of image icons, the save silently failed every time and the change only ever lived on the screen you edited it on. The save no longer uses that capped mode, so Decks with image icons now reach the server reliably.)* *(Tip: a key can run different actions on **tap** vs **hold**, and a configured key can be saved as a **key preset** to reuse on another Deck.)*
- **RGB on the cooler and fans now lights up after a reboot, not just the RAM**: with an **iCUE LINK** setup, the cooler and fans connect through the iCUE LINK System Hub — and right after a Windows restart iCUE reports its SDK session "ready" a moment before it has finished registering the devices on that hub. Xenon enumerated in that gap, found the RAM (a directly-connected module) but saw the hub as having **zero LEDs**, and never looked again — so music, album colours and effects lit only the RAM while the cooler and fans stayed dark until the next server restart. Xenon now notices an incomplete device list (a device reported with no LEDs, not just an empty list) and **re-checks for a few seconds** until iCUE finishes bringing the LINK devices online, then paints them — bounded so a hub that genuinely has no RGB attached doesn't keep retrying. Opening **Settings → Illuminazione** also triggers the same refresh.
- **The Deck no longer reshuffles its keys (or loses an edit) across restarts**: when a Deck is shown in a smaller tile (e.g. inside a tab), auto-fit re-flows the keys to fit the available space — but it was *saving* that re-flowed column count as your real layout, so your carefully arranged keys came back rearranged after a reboot and a button you'd just replaced could be reverted. Auto-fit is now strictly a *display* adjustment: your saved grid stays exactly as you set it, and an edit made on the fitted view is folded back onto your real layout without ever moving the other keys. For a perfectly fixed layout you can still turn **Auto** off in the Deck editor and set the columns/rows by hand. (Together with each Deck now being independent — see above — this closes the whole family of "the Deck rearranges itself" issues.)

## [v3.1.0] - 2026-06-12

### ✨ New Features
- **Backup & restore your whole configuration**: a new **Settings → Backup** section exports everything that makes your Xenon yours — dashboard layout and pages, Deck profiles and keys, calendar events, tasks, timers, notes and settings — as **one portable file**. Import it on a fresh install (or after a Windows reinstall) and everything comes back with a single tap. API keys, passwords and credentials are **deliberately never included**, so the file is safe to keep on a cloud drive. On a normal browser the export downloads the file; on the Xeneon Edge display (where the built-in browser has no download manager) Xenon saves it straight to your **Downloads** folder and shows you the path — so export works the same everywhere.
- **Xenon tells you when an update is out**: the dashboard now checks the project's GitHub releases (at most once a day, completely silent when offline) and shows a small **"Update available"** pill at the bottom of the Settings sidebar linking straight to the release page. No auto-downloads, no telemetry — it only compares version numbers.
- **Album-art gradient on external lights too**: the per-LED cover gradient introduced for Corsair devices now reaches the external providers. **WLED strips** paint the real gradient across their LEDs, **Philips Hue** spreads the cover's colours across the bridge's colour bulbs (first bulb takes the dominant colour, the others walk the gradient), and multi-device **Govee / LIFX / Nanoleaf** setups give each lamp its own cover colour instead of all-identical. Single lamps keep the classic uniform tint, and everything still updates only when the track changes — zero idle cost.

### ✨ Improvements
- **Album-art gradient across the LEDs**: when music plays, Xenon now extracts up to **three distinct colours** from the cover (not just one) and spreads them as a smooth gradient across each Corsair device's LEDs — a strip or fan ring shows the cover's whole personality instead of a single tint. Colours qualify only if they are genuinely different hues with real weight in the artwork, so noisy covers don't produce random stripes; covers with one dominant colour keep the classic uniform look, and transient flashes (events, Deck reactions) still take the whole device. Zero idle cost: the gradient is computed once per track, never on a timer.
- **A real colour picker, everywhere**: the native colour dialog never worked inside the iCUE browser, so every colour choice in Xenon was limited to a handful of preset swatches or typing a hex code by hand. Xenon now has its own built-in picker — a saturation/brightness area, a hue strip, a live hex field and the quick presets — that opens from: the **Deck key editor** (key accent, press-effect colour, LED reaction colour, via the new rainbow swatch), the **Lighting page** (fixed colour, animations, event flashes — tap the colour square), and **Settings** (accent, background, text and grid colours — tap the preview square). Touch-friendly and fully in-app, so it works on the Xeneon Edge screen and inside iCUE alike. The popover keeps a solid background regardless of the theme's glass transparency, so it stays readable over any content.
- **Album-art lighting is far more vivid and varied**: the colour extracted from the now-playing cover was being softened for on-screen readability and then sent *as-is* to the RGB LEDs — where a softened mid-tone renders as a washed-out pastel, making most albums look nearly the same. The LEDs now receive the same hue at **full vividness** (the dashboard keeps the softer variant, which is correct for text and buttons). Reds are red, yellows pop, blues glow.
- **The cover colour is found much more often**: two fixes — dark or muted covers are no longer rejected as "too grey" so easily (the threshold was conservative), and when Windows announces a new track *before* publishing its cover art (very common), Xenon now retries shortly after instead of giving up — so the album tint and LEDs no longer fall back to defaults on tracks that clearly have artwork.
- **The colour picker remembers your recent colours**: the last six custom colours you picked appear as a new row under the presets — pick a brand colour once, reuse it everywhere with one tap.
- **Bigger touch targets across the dashboard**: the page dots in the top bar now have a much larger (invisible) touch area, dropdown options are taller, the Deck editor's colour swatches and reorder buttons are finger-sized, and the colour picker's hue strip is easier to grab — all sized for the Xeneon Edge touchscreen, with no visual redesign.

### ⚡ Performance
- **New native helper (Xenon Helper)**: Xenon now ships an optional native companion, `xenon-helper.exe` (~11MB, no runtime to install), that replaces background PowerShell helpers with small native processes (~20MB instead of ~100MB each). Three moved in this release: the **media reader** — now-playing info served in ~2ms, and the helper *listens to Windows' media events*, so track changes and play/pause appear on the dashboard **instantly** instead of up to 2 seconds later — the **game-mode probe**, which now also reacts the instant you switch into or out of a game — and the **app-switcher probe** (see below). The helper is completely optional: if the exe is missing or anything goes wrong, Xenon silently uses the existing PowerShell paths, exactly as before. (Hardware sensor readings deliberately stay on the PowerShell path: the LibreHardwareMonitor library installed on users' machines can only run there.) `INSTALL.bat` downloads the helper automatically from the GitHub release — the exe is built by a public CI workflow from the tagged source, so its provenance is verifiable — and refreshes it on update if it's outdated; if the download fails, everything keeps working without it. `UNINSTALL.bat` removes it.
- **The Apps panel now opens near-instantly**: listing your open windows (with live previews and icons) used to launch a PowerShell process that *compiled C# code on every single open* — roughly a second of waiting before anything appeared, and the same again on every focus tap. The native Xenon Helper now does it directly (about 2× faster end-to-end, with no compilation step at all), and as always falls back transparently to the PowerShell path when the helper isn't installed. Re-run `INSTALL.bat` (or wait for the next release's auto-refresh) to get the updated helper.
- **No more PowerShell processes popping up every two seconds**: the now-playing info (track, artist, album art, progress) used to be read by launching a brand-new PowerShell process for every refresh — roughly one every 2 seconds while the dashboard is open. Each launch costs a full PowerShell startup, which showed up as `powershell.exe` flickering at the top of Task Manager and could measurably raise CPU usage and temperatures (reported by a user as ~5°C). Media is now read by a **single long-lived background helper** that stays connected to Windows' media system and answers each refresh in a few milliseconds, with the album art re-read only when the track actually changes. If the helper ever has a problem, Xenon falls back transparently to the old per-refresh method, so nothing breaks — it just uses a little more CPU until the helper recovers.
- **Sensor readings are ~10× cheaper**: the background helper that reads CPU temperature and GPU load/temperature used to rebuild its entire LibreHardwareMonitor session on every reading — re-scanning the disk for the library, re-enumerating all hardware and re-opening the kernel driver every few seconds, then querying three WMI fallbacks even when it already had a good value. The session is now opened once and kept alive (a reading went from ~500ms to ~30ms of CPU), fallbacks only run when the library really has nothing, and the nvidia-smi path and GPU name lookups are cached. If the session ever breaks (sleep/resume, driver reset), it rebuilds itself on the next reading.
